Sawm — Fasting
beginner
6 min
Kaffarah is Exclusive to Ramadan Fast
Ruling that kaffarah is specific to Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for non-Ramadan fasts and explain the reasoning based on qiyas jali.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is exclusive to intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast – other fasts only require qada.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh of fasting: the severe penalty of kaffarah is attached only to breaking the Ramadan fast. Other fasts, whether make-up or voluntary, if broken intentionally, do not require kaffarah. This ruling is based on a straightforward analogy (qiyas jali) that recognizes the unique sanctity of Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: intentionally breaking a fast other than Ramadan. The ruling is that only qada is required, no kaffarah.
2
Locate the dalil
The text provides a reason: because breaking the fast in Ramadan is greater in sin. This reasoning forms the basis of a qiyas jali argument.
The dalil is not a text but a rational analogy.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
Identify the original case (asl): intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast, which requires kaffarah. The new case (far'): breaking a non-Ramadan fast. The effective cause (illa) for kaffarah is the extreme gravity of the act. Since this illa is not present in the far', kaffarah is not applied.
The illa is 'greater sin' (ablagh fil jinaya).
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person who breaks a non-Ramadan fast (e.g., make-up, nazr, nafl) only needs to make up that fast; no expiation. This prevents unnecessary burden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رمضان کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے روزہ کو فاسد کرنے میں صرف قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں
وَلَيْسَ فِى افْسَادِ صَوْمٍ غَيْرِ رَمَضَانَ كَفَّارَةً لِأَنَّ الْإِفْطَارَ فِى رَمْضَانَ أَبْلَعُ فِي الْجِنَايَةِ فَلَا يُلْحَقُ بِهِ غَيْرُهُ ترجمہ اور رمضان کے علاوہ روزہ فاسد کرنے میں کفارہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ رمضان میں روزہ توڑنا جرم میں بہت بڑھا ہوا سے لہذا اس کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ کو لاحق نہ کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر غیر رمضاں میں روز ہ ر کھ کر اس کو عمد ا تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان
In spoiling a fast other than Ramadan, there is only qada, no kaffarah.
And there is no kaffarah in spoiling a fast other than Ramadan, because breaking the fast in Ramadan is greater in sin, so other (fasts) are not annexed to it. Translation: And in spoiling a fast other than Ramadan, there is no kaffarah, because breaking the fast in Ramadan is far greater in transgression, therefore other fasts are not attached to it. Explanation: If one fasts in other than Ramadan and intentionally breaks it, then no kaffarah is obligatory upon him. The proof is that Ramadan...
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof by analogy (qiyas jali) and a textual reasoning. The passage states that intentionally breaking a fast that is not the obligatory Ramadan fast (e.g., a missed make-up fast, a voluntary fast, or a fast of a different month) does not entail kaffarah. Only qada (make-up) is required if the fast is invalidated deliberately. The reason given is that the sin of breaking a Ramadan fast is extremely severe because of its sacredness, so the severe penalty of kaffarah is exclusive to it. Other fasts are not like Ramadan in sanctity, so they are not annexed to this ruling. The proof provided is that the sin (al-jinayah) in Ramadan is much greater, thus the punishment is specific. This is a clear statement that kaffarah is not applied by analogy to other fasts.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): The expiation required for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast (fasting two consecutive months or feeding 60 poor people).
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or broken fast on another day.
الجنایة (al-jinayah): The transgression or sin associated with an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required if someone intentionally breaks a make-up fast (qada) for a missed Ramadan day?
A) He must make up the fast and also perform kaffarah.
B) He must only make up the fast; no kaffarah.
C) He must only perform kaffarah; no make-up.
D) He does not need to do anything.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that kaffarah is limited to intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast; for all other fasts, only qada is obligatory.

Tarteeb and Taba' in Kaffarah for Breaking Ramadan Fast
Discusses sequence and continuity required in expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tarteeb and taba' in kaffarah for breaking a Ramadan fast, explain the supporting evidence, and refute opposing views.

Core Idea
Sequence and continuity are conditions for kaffarah of fasting, based on hadith and analogy to zihar.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the expiation (kaffarah) for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast must follow a specific order (tarteeb) and be performed consecutively (taba'). The Hanafi school requires both, but some scholars argue for choice (takhyeer) or deny the need for continuity. We will explore the evidence and reasoning that establish the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that tarteeb and taba' are obligatory conditions for the validity of kaffarah. Explain what this means: first free a slave, if unable then fast two consecutive months, if unable then feed sixty poor.
Tarteeb and taba' are shurut (conditions), not arkan.
2
Identify the opponents and their proofs
Name the two opposing views: those who allow takhyeer (choice) citing the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and those who deny taba' using qiyas. Understand their apparent evidence.
Opponents may be from within or outside the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
Analyze the primary hadith of the bedouin which explicitly mentions the order and uses the word 'mutabi'ayn'. Also examine the qiyas to zihar kaffarah where both conditions are agreed upon.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala in its indication.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to opponents
Understand the refutation: the hadith of Sa'd does not establish choice; it only lists permissible items. Qiyas is invalid when it contradicts clear text (nass).
The principle: al-qiyas fi muqabil al-nass fasid.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if tarteeb is violated, the kaffarah is invalid; if taba' is broken, the fasts must be restarted from the beginning.
This shows why the condition matters in application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رسول پاک صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہنس پڑے حتی کہ آپ کے اگلے دانت کھل گئے اور ایک روایت میں انیاب ( دانت ) اور ایک روایت میں نواجذ کا لفظ ہے پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ لو اور اپنے بیوی بچوں کو کھلا دو اور ابو داؤد کی روایت میں امام زہری نے یہ زیادتی کی ہے کہ یہ رخصت خاص طور پر اسی کے لئے ہے اسی روایت کو تھوڑے سے لفظی تغیر کے ساتھ صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے جس کا ترجمہ عبارت کے ترجمہ کے ساتھ گذر چکا اس روایت سے ایک بات تو یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ اعتاق رقبہ، دو ماہ کے روزے اور ساٹھ مساکین کو کھانا دینے کے درمیان اختیار نہیں دیا گیا ہے بلکہ یہ ترتیب ضروری ہے کہ اگر غلام آزاد کرنے پر قادر ہوتو غلام آزاد کرنا ضروری ہے اور اگر اس پر قدرت نہ ہو تو دو ماہ کے مسلسل روزے رکھنا ضروری ہے اور اگر اس پر بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا دے دوسری بات یہ معلوم ہوئی کہ دو ماہ کے روزوں میں تابع اور تسلسل شرط ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں شہرین کے بعد متابعین کا لفظ بھی موجود ہے۔ اور قائلین تغییر کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث سعد بن ابی وقاص کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں ان چیزوں کو بیان کرنا مقصود ہے جن سے کفارہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے ترتیب یا تخیر کو بیان کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اور قائلین عدم تابع کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قیاس نص کے مقابلہ میں فاسد ہے۔

ہمارا مستدل وہ حدیث بھی ہے جو گذشتہ مسئلہ میں مذکور ہے یعنی مَنْ أَفْطَرَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَعَلَيْهِ مَا عَلَى الْمُظَاهِرِ ، اس حدیث میں کفارہ صوم کو ظہار کے کفارہ پر قیاس کیا ہے اور ظہار کے کفارہ میں ترتیب اور تابع دونوں شرط ہیں لہذا کفار صوم میں بھی دونوں چیز میں شرط ہوں گی ۔
The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) laughed until his front teeth became visible, and in one narration the word 'aniyab' (canine teeth) and in another 'nawajidh' is mentioned. Then he said: 'Take it and feed your wife and children.' In Abu Dawud's narration, Imam Zuhri added that this concession is specifically for him. The author of Hidayah mentioned this narration with slight variation. From this hadith it became clear that there is no choice between freeing a slave, fasting two months, and feeding sixty poor; rather sequence is obligatory: if one is able to free a slave, freeing is obligatory; if unable, then fasting two consecutive months; if unable, then feeding sixty poor. The second point is that continuity (taba') is also a condition for the two months of fasting, because in the hadith the word 'mutabi'ayn' appears after 'shahrayn'. As for those who say there is a choice (takhyeer) and cite the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, the response is that that hadith aims to mention items by which expiation is fulfilled, not sequence or choice. As for those who deny continuity via qiyas, the response is that qiyas is invalid when conflicting with text.

Our evidence is also the hadith mentioned in the previous issue: 'Whoever breaks the fast in Ramadan, upon him is what is upon the one who performs zihar.' In this hadith, expiation of fasting is analogized to expiation of zihar, and in zihar expiation both sequence and continuity are conditions. Therefore, in expiation of fasting both conditions are required.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the conditions of kaffarah for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast. The author expands on the ruling from Al-Hidayah, establishing that both tarteeb (sequence) and taba' (continuity) are required. The primary evidence is the hadith of the bedouin, which explicitly mentions freeing a slave, then fasting, then feeding, indicating a necessary order. Additionally, the word 'mutabi'ayn' in the hadith confirms continuity. The author then refutes two opposing views: those who claim choice (takhyeer) citing Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas's hadith, and those who reject continuity through qiyas. The refutation is that the primary hadith is clear text (nass), and qiyas cannot override it. Finally, the author reinforces the Hanafi position by citing the hadith making kaffarah of fasting analogous to that of zihar, where both conditions are unanimously required. Thus, the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that tarteeb and taba' are mandatory for kaffarah of fasting.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tarteeb): Sequence: the obligation to perform the expiatory acts in a specific order (free slave, then fast, then feed).
تابع (taba'): Continuity: fasting two months consecutively without break.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions for the kaffarah (expiation) for breaking a Ramadan fast according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sequence (tarteeb) and choice (takhyeer)
B) Sequence (tarteeb) and continuity (taba')
C) Continuity (taba') and feeding only
D) Choice (takhyeer) and fasting only

Key Takeaway
Tarteeb and taba' are wajib conditions for kaffarah of fasting in the Hanafi school, supported by hadith and qiyas to zihar.

Non-Penetrative Intercourse and the Fast: Qada vs Kaffarah
Ruling on non-penetrative intercourse with discharge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on non-penetrative intercourse with discharge during a fast and explain why qada is required but kaffarah is not, using the distinction between ma'na and surah.

Core Idea
Discharge from non-penetrative intercourse breaks the fast but does not trigger kaffarah.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case: a fasting person engages in sexual activity without actual penetration (e.g., rubbing on thighs) and experiences discharge. How does the law treat this? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the 'form' (surah) and the 'meaning' (ma'na) of intercourse. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its consequences for the obligation of qada and kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its components
First, identify the scenario: a fasting person uses their organ on an area other than the private parts (front or back), and discharge occurs. Note that penetration into a private part is absent.
The act is incomplete intercourse (ma duna al-farj), not full penetration (idkhal).
2
Apply the form–meaning distinction
Analyse the act using two concepts: surah (form) and ma'na (meaning). Surah of intercourse is the physical insertion of one private part into another. Ma'na is the purpose or essence, which is the act leading to discharge. Here surah is absent, but ma'na is present because discharge occurred from a deliberate sexual act.
Kaffarah requires both form and meaning; qada requires only essence.
3
Derive the ruling
Since the ma'na is found, the fast is invalidated, making qada obligatory. Since the surah is absent, kaffarah is not required. The ruling is: wajib (obligatory) to make up the fast, no expiation.
This is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.
4
Confirm the legal principle
The underlying principle: for kaffarah to be wajib, the full act of intercourse (penetration) must occur. Any lesser act that causes discharge only demands qada.
This matches the general Hanafi rule that kaffarah is tied to actual penetration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مادون الفرج میں جماع کیا اور انزال بھی ہو گیا قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں

وَمَنْ جَامَعَ فِيْمَا دُونَ الْفَرُ فَانْزَلَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ لِوُجُودِ الْجِمَاعِ مَعْنَى وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لِإِنْعِدَامِهِ صُورَةً

ترجمہ اور جس نے فرج کے علاوہ جماع کیا پھر اس کو انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہے کیونکہ معنی جماع پایا گیا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ صور جماع معدوم ہو گیا۔ تشریح فرج سے مراد قبل اور ڈیر ہے اب مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اگر قبل اور دبر کے علاوہ میں مثلاً رانوں میں یا پیٹ میں بحالت روز وذکر کا استعمال کیا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ قضا تو اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ معنی جماع پایا گیا اور کفارہ اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ صورۃ جماع نہیں پایا گیا کیونکہ صورۃ جامع کے لئے ادخال فرج فی الفرج ضروری ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔
He who had intercourse other than the private parts and had discharge: qada is required, not kaffarah.

And whoever has intercourse in something other than the private part and then has discharge, upon him is qada because the meaning of intercourse is found, and no kaffarah upon him because the form is absent.

Translation: And whoever has intercourse other than the private part and then has discharge, on him is qada because the meaning of intercourse is found, and no kaffarah on him because the form of intercourse is absent. Explanation: The private part (farj) refers to the front and back. So the meaning is that if one uses his organ on the thighs or belly while fasting and has discharge, then qada is obligatory and kaffarah is not. Qada is obligatory because the meaning of intercourse is present, and kaffarah is not obligatory because the form of intercourse is not present, since for the form of intercourse insertion of the private part into the private part is necessary, and that is not found.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that addresses a specific case: a fasting person engages in sexual activity other than actual penetration of the private parts (front or back) and experiences discharge. The ruling is that the fast becomes invalid, requiring qada (make-up), but no kaffarah (expiation). The reasoning is based on two concepts: 'form' (surah) and 'meaning' (ma'na). Actual intercourse is defined as penetration of one private part into another, which is the 'surah' of intercourse. This is absent here. However, the 'ma'na' (the essence or purpose of intercourse, which is the act leading to discharge) is present. For kaffarah to be obligatory, both form and meaning are required, similar to the complete act. Since only the meaning is present, qada is due but not kaffarah.

Key Terms
مادون الفرج (ma duna al-farj): Anything other than the front and back private parts (i.e., thighs, belly, etc.).
قضا (qada): Make-up fast required to compensate for a broken obligation.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation, a heavier penalty for certain violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a fasting person engages in intercourse between the thighs with discharge?
A) No qada, no kaffarah
B) Qada only
C) Kaffarah only
D) Both qada and kaffarah

Key Takeaway
When fasting, non-penetrative sexual activity with discharge requires qada but not kaffarah because the form of intercourse (penetration) is missing.

No Kaffarah for Breaking Fast Outside Ramadan
Explains why kaffarah is limited to Ramadan fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school limits kaffarah to Ramadan fasts and apply the principle that kaffarah is not extended by analogy.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is wajib only for Ramadan fasts because breaking it involves two offenses: against the fast and the month.

The source passage addresses a common question: does breaking any fast require kaffarah? The Hanafi ruling is clear that kaffarah is exclusive to Ramadan. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: the dual offense and the principle that exceptions to qiyas are not extended.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact fiqh ruling: no kaffarah for invalidating a fast other than Ramadan.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is the reasoning (talil) that breaking a Ramadan fast is a greater offense because it combines two jinayat: against the fast itself and against the holy month.
3
Analyze the nature of the proof
The text states that kaffarah for Ramadan is proven by a nass (text) that is contrary to qiyas, i.e., it is an exception. Therefore, it cannot be extended by analogy.
4
Examine why analogy is blocked
The illa (effective cause) for kaffarah is the severe offense. Non-Ramadan fasts lack the second offense, so the illa is absent; thus qiyas is invalid.
5
Understand the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: other schools may extend kaffarah to other obligatory fasts, but Hanafi restricts it to Ramadan.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِى افْسَادِ صَوْمٍ غَيْرِ رَمَضَانَ كَفَّارَةً لِأَنَّ الْإِفْطَارَ فِى رَمْضَانَ أَبْلَعُ فِي الْجِنَايَةِ فَلَا يُلْحَقُ بِهِ غَيْرُهُ ترجمہ اور رمضان کے علاوہ روزہ فاسد کرنے میں کفارہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ رمضان میں روزہ توڑنا جرم میں بہت بڑھا ہوا ہے لہذا اس کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ کو لاحق نہ کیا جائے گا۔

تشریح مسئلہ اگر غیر رمضاں میں روز ہ ر کھ کر اس کو عمد ا تو ڑ دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے اندر روزہ توڑنا بڑا جام ہے بہ نسبت غیر رمضان میں توڑنے کے کیونکہ رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے کی صورت میں دو جنایتیں ہیں ایک جنایت علی الصوم ، دوم جنایت علی شہر رمضان اور غیر رمضان میں فقط ایک جنایت ہے یعنی جنایت علی الصوم بہر حال رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے کی جنایت اقوئی ہے اور غیر رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے کی جنایت ادنی ہے اور اقومی کے اندر حکم ثابت کرنے سے ادنی کے اندر اس حکم کا ثابت ہونا لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے ثبوت کفارہ کا حکم رمضان کے اندر تو روزہ توڑنے کے ساتھ متعلق ہو گا لیکن غیر رمضان میں یہ حکم ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ نیز رمضان کا روزہ توڑنے سے کفارہ خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہے لہذا اس پر دوسرے روزوں کے توڑنے کو قیاس نہ کیا جائے گا۔
And there is no kaffarah in invalidating a fast other than Ramadan, because breaking the fast in Ramadan is greater in offense, so others are not likened to it.

Translation: And in invalidating a fast other than Ramadan, there is no kaffarah, because breaking the fast in Ramadan is a much greater crime, so other than it is not annexed to it.

Explanation: If one fasts outside Ramadan and deliberately breaks it, no kaffarah is obligatory. The proof is that breaking a fast in Ramadan is a major crime compared to outside Ramadan, because breaking a fast in Ramadan involves two offences: one against the fast itself, and a second against the month of Ramadan. Outside Ramadan, there is only one offence — against the fast. Thus, the offence in Ramadan is stronger, and the offence outside Ramadan is lesser. The ruling established for the stronger does not necessarily apply to the lesser. So the ruling of kaffarah is attached to breaking the fast in Ramadan, but not outside. Also, kaffarah for breaking Ramadan fast is proven by text that is contrary to analogy (qiyas), so other fasts cannot be analogized to it.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing that kaffarah (expiation) is only applicable when a Ramadan fast is deliberately broken, not for any other fast. The reason given is that breaking a Ramadan fast is a more severe offense because it combines disrespect to the fast itself and to the sacred month. Outside Ramadan, only the fast is violated. The author explains that since kaffarah is established by a textual evidence (nass) that is contrary to qiyas (i.e., it is an exception), it cannot be extended by analogy to other fasts. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and highlights the special status of Ramadan.

Key Terms
جنایت (jinayah): Offense or violation against the sanctity of fasting.
ابلع (abla'): Greater, more severe (in terms of offense).
لافی (la yulhaq): Cannot be annexed or analogized to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kaffarah not required for deliberately breaking a fast outside Ramadan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the fast is less important
B) Because there is only one offense, while Ramadan has two
C) Because qada is sufficient
D) Because the text does not mention it

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah (expiation) for deliberately breaking a fast is wajib only in Ramadan due to the dual offense and the exception to analogy.

Acts That Invalidate the Fast: Enema, Nose Drops, and Ear Drops
Ruling with proof on enema, nose drops, ear drops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three acts that invalidate the fast via non-oral routes and explain the evidence from hadith and the principle of 'ma'na al-fitr'.

Core Idea
Entering a beneficial substance to the body cavity invalidates the fast, even via enema, nose, or ear.

This lesson examines three specific acts that break the fast: administering an enema, snuffing medicine into the nose, and pouring medicine into the ear. These are ruled as invalidators because they involve delivering a beneficial substance to the internal cavity, which constitutes the meaning of iftar. We will also see why kaffarah is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts
List the three acts mentioned: ihtiqan (enema), isti'at (nose drops), and qatr fi al-udhun (ear drops). Recognize that each involves intentional insertion of a substance.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'al-fitr mima dakhala' (breaking the fast is by what enters). This is a general principle. Note that the Hanafi school applies it to any entry into the body cavity.
The hadith is reported with zanni thubut.
3
Understand the meaning of iftar
The text defines the meaning of iftar as 'wusul ma fihi salah al-badan ila al-jawf' (reaching something beneficial to the body into the cavity). This is the 'illa for invalidation.
Benefit is key: pure water in the ear is not beneficial, so it does not break the fast.
4
Apply the no-kaffarah rule
Note that although the fast is broken, no kaffarah is due because the form (surah) of normal eating/drinking is absent. Kaffarah only applies to intentional eating/drinking in the usual manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حقنہ کرانا ناک میں دوا ڈالنا کان میں کوئی دوائی کا نا مفسد صوم ہے

وَمَنِ احْتَقَنَ أوِ اسْتَعَطَ أو أَقْطَرَفِى أُذُنِهِ أَفْطَرَ لِقَوْلِهِ الْفِطْرَ مِمَّا دَخَلَ وَلِوُجُودِ مَعْنَى الْفِطْرِ وَهُوَ وُصُولُ مَا فيهِ صَلاحُ الْبَدَنِ إِلَى الْجَوْفِ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لإِنْعِدَامِهِ صُوَرَةً

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے حقنہ لیا یا ناک میں کوئی چیز چڑھائی یا اپنے کان میں کوئی دوا پکائی تو روزہ افطار ہوگیا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ فطر اس چیز سے ہوتا ہے جو داخل ہو اور اس لئے کہ فطر کے معنی پائے گئے ہیں اور فطر کے معنی ہیں اس چیز کا جوف تک پہنچنا جس میں صلاح بدن ہو اور اس پر کفارہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ داخل ہونے کی صورت معدوم ہو گئی ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ: اگر روزہ دار نے حقہ کرایا یعنی پائخانہ کے راستہ سے اندر دوا پہنچائی یا ناک کے ذریعہ دوا پہنچائی گئی یا کان میں دوا نی کائی گئی تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں سے ہر صورت میں روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الفِطْرُ مِمَّا دَخَلَ وَلَيسَ مِمَّا حَرَج یعنی کسی چیز کے اندر پیٹ میں جانے سے روزہ ٹوتا ہے اور نکلنے سے نہیں ٹو تھا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں افطار کے معنی پائے گئے ہیں کیونکہ افطار کے معنی کسی چیز کو نفع بدن کے لئے معدہ اور جوف میں پہنچانا ہیں۔ کانوں میں پانی پکانا یا خود بخود داخل ہو جانا مفسد صوم نہیں

وَلَوْ أَقْطَرَ فِي أُذُنَيْهِ الْمَاءَ أَوْ دَخَلَهُمَا لَا يَفْسُدُ صَوْمَ لِعَدَمِ الْمَعْنَى وَالصُورَةِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أَدْخَلَهُ اللَّهُنَ

ترجمہ اور اگر روزہ دار نے اپنے کانوں میں پانی پڑکا یا یا پائی کا نون میں خود داخل ہو گیا تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا نہ معنی مافطار ہوا اور نہ صورۃ بر خلاف اس کے کہ جب اس نے تیل داخل کیا۔

تشریح مسئلہ اگر روزہ دار نے اپنے کانوں میں پانی پکایا یا پانی خود بخود کانوں میں داخل ہو گیا بایں طور کہ دریا سے عبور کرتے ہوئے پانی کانوں میں گھس گیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا کیونکہ فطر نہ معنا موجود ہے اور نہ صورۃ اس لئے نہیں کہ کسی چیز کومنہ میں ڈال کر نگلنا نہیں پایا گیا پس افطار جب نہ معنا ہوا اور نہ صورۃ ہوا تو روزہ بھی فاسد نہ ہو گا ہاں اگر کان میں تیل داخل کیا تو افطار ہو جائے گا کیونکہ تیل ڈالنے سے چونکہ اصلاح بدن مقصود ہوتا ہے اس لئے معنی افطار پایا گیا۔
Administering an enema, putting medicine in the nose, or putting medicine in the ear invalidates the fast.

And whoever administers an enema, or snuffs medicine, or puts drops in his ear, his fast is broken because of his statement: 'Breaking the fast is from what enters,' and because the meaning of breaking the fast is found, which is reaching something beneficial to the body into the cavity; and no kaffarah on him because the form of entering is absent.

Translation: And whoever takes an enema, or puts something in his nose, or pours medicine in his ear, his fast is broken because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not by what exits.' And because the meaning of breaking the fast is found: reaching something beneficial to the body into the stomach or cavity. And no kaffarah on him because the form of entry is absent.

Explanation: If a fasting person takes an enema (medicine enters through the anus), or medicine is inserted through the nose, or medicine is poured into the ear, in all three cases the fast is broken. Proof: The Prophet said: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not by what exits.' Second proof: In these cases, the meaning of iftar is found, which is reaching something beneficial to the body into the stomach or cavity. Putting water in the ears or water entering by itself does not invalidate the fast.

And if one pours water into his ears or it enters them, his fast is not invalidated, because neither the meaning nor the form of iftar is present, contrary to when one puts oil in them.

Translation: And if a fasting person pours water into his ears or water enters by itself, his fast is not invalidated, neither in meaning nor in form. Unlike the case when he puts oil.

Explanation: If a fasting person pours water into his ears or water enters accidentally while crossing a river, in both cases the fast is not invalidated because neither the meaning nor the form of iftar is present. The form is absent because nothing is swallowed through the mouth; the meaning is absent because water is not considered beneficial for the body like oil. However, if oil is put in the ear, the fast is broken because with oil, bodily benefit is intended, so the meaning of iftar is found.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, covering three distinct cases: administering an enema, putting medicine in the nose, and putting medicine in the ear. All three invalidate the fast because a beneficial substance reaches the inner body (cavity or stomach) through an external route, which constitutes the meaning of iftar. The hadith 'al-fitr mima dakhala' is cited as evidence. However, kaffarah is not imposed because the act lacks the complete form of eating or drinking. A second sub-ruling distinguishes water from oil: water entering the ears, whether poured or accidental, does not break the fast because it does not serve as bodily nourishment (no ma'na of iftar) and there is no surah of ingesting. Oil, on the other hand, is a beneficial substance, so it breaks the fast. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle that iftar occurs by the entry of anything that is typically beneficial to the body, even through non-oral routes, except when the substance is not beneficial (like water in the ear) or accidental.

Key Terms
احتقان (ihtiqan): Administering an enema; introducing medicine through the rectum.
استعاط (isti'at): Snuffing or insufflating medicine into the nose.
قطر (qatr): Pouring drops into the ear or nose.
جوف (jawf): Internal cavity of the body, including stomach and digestive tract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they are not foods or drinks.
B) Because the act was accidental.
C) Because the form of normal eating/drinking is absent.
D) Because the fast is not actually broken.

Key Takeaway
Enema, nose drops, and ear drops invalidate the fast because they deliver a beneficial substance to the body cavity, but no kaffarah is due because the normal form of ingestion is absent.

Water vs. Oil in the Ear: The Distinction Based on Benefit
Distinction between water and oil in ear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between water and oil entering the ear during fasting, applying the Hanafi principles of 'ma'na' and 'surah'.

Core Idea
Water in the ear does not break the fast; oil does. The difference is benefit.

This lesson tackles a nuanced ruling: pouring water into the ear or having it enter accidentally does not invalidate the fast, but pouring oil does. The key lies in the concepts of 'ma'na' (meaning/benefit) and 'surah' (form). While the form is absent in both, the benefit (ma'na) is present only in oil, making it an invalidator.

Guided Path
1
State the rule for water in ear
The text says: if water is poured into the ears or enters them, the fast is not invalidated. Reason: neither the meaning nor the form of iftar is present.
Water is not considered beneficial for the body in this context.
2
State the rule for oil in ear
Contrast: if oil is put in the ear, the fast is broken. Reason: oil is beneficial (ma'na present), even though the form is absent.
The passage explicitly says 'bikhilaf ma idha adkhalahu al-duhn'.
3
Analyze the 'ma'na' and 'surah' framework
The fiqh principle: for iftar to occur, either surah (form of eating/drinking) or ma'na (delivery of benefit to the body) must be present. Water in ear has neither; oil has ma'na but not surah, so it still invalidates.
This framework explains why enema, nose drops, ear drops (medicine) also break the fast: they have ma'na.
4
Apply to accidental entry
Even if water enters accidentally (e.g., while swimming), the fast remains valid. The absence of ma'na and surah is not affected by intention.

Source Text

Ruling on Enema, Nasal Drops, and Ear Drops
Ruling on enema, nasal drops, and ear drops breaking the fast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on enema, nasal drops, and ear drops during fasting and explain the evidence and the distinction between water and oil in the ear.

Core Idea
Medicine entering through any natural passage breaks the fast, but kaffarah is not required.

The Hanafi school considers that anything entering the body cavity (jawf) through a natural opening, if beneficial, nullifies the fast. This is based on a hadith and the meaning of iftar. However, expiation is waived because the action does not resemble eating in form. A nuanced sub-ruling differentiates water from oil in the ear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
List the actions: enema (ihtiqan), snuffing medicine into the nose (isti'tat), and pouring medicine into the ear (iqtaar). State that each breaks the fast according to the Hanafi school.
The ear ruling only applies if the substance is beneficial (like oil), not if it is plain water.
2
Examine the primary evidence (dalil)
Recall the hadith: 'al-fitr mimma dakhala' (breaking the fast is by what enters). This is a hadith reported by al-Daraqutni. The principle is that anything that enters and is beneficial breaks the fast.
The hadith is zanni in transmission but qat'i in indication.
3
Understand the rationale (wajh al-dalalah)
The phrase mimma dakhala implies that the cause of breaking is entry. The Hanafi school interprets 'entry' as reaching the jawf via a natural passage, regardless of whether it is consumed through the mouth.
The meaning (ma'na) of iftar is delivering something beneficial to the body.
4
Note the absence of kaffarah
Though the fast is void (fasad), no expiation (kaffarah) is required because the form (surah) of eating and drinking is not present; the substance does not pass through the mouth.
Kaffarah is only for intentional eating/drinking or sexual intercourse.
5
Distinguish water vs. oil in the ear
Pouring water into the ear does not break the fast because water is not typically intended for bodily benefit; hence both the meaning and form of iftar are absent. Oil, being beneficial, breaks the fast.
This distinction is based on istihsan (juristic preference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حقنہ کرانا ناک میں دوا ڈالنا کان میں کوئی دوائی کا نا مفسد صوم ہے
وَمَنِ احْتَقَنَ أوِ اسْتَعَطَ أو أَقْطَرَفِى أُذُنِهِ أَفْطَرَ لِقَوْلِهِ الْفِطْرَ مِمَّا دَخَلَ وَلِوُجُودِ مَعْنَى الْفِطْرِ وَهُوَ وُصُولُ مَا فيهِ صَلاحُ الْبَدَنِ إِلَى الْجَوْفِ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِ لإِنْعَدَامِهِ صُوَرَةً

وَلَوْ أَقْطَرَ فِي أُذُنَيْهِ الْمَاءَ أَوْ دَخَلَهُمَا لَا يَفْسُدُ صَوْمَ لانْعِدَامِ الْمَعْنَى وَالصُورَةِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أَدْخَلَهُ اللَّهُنَ

And whoever uses an enema or snuffs a medicine or pours into his ear has broken his fast, due to his (saw) statement: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not by what exits', and due to the presence of the meaning of breaking the fast, which is the arrival of something beneficial to the body into the cavity (jawf), and there is no kaffarah (expiation) upon him because the form (surah) of entering is absent. Commentary: If a fasting person administers an enema (medicine through the anus), or snuffs medicine through the nose, or puts medicine in the ear, in all three cases the fast is broken. The proof is the hadith: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not by what exits.' The second proof is that the meaning of iftar (breaking fast) is present: delivering something beneficial to the stomach or cavity. And if one puts water in his ears or water enters by itself, the fast is not spoiled because neither the meaning nor the form of iftar is present. But if one puts oil in the ear, the fast is broken because the meaning of iftar (benefiting the body) is present.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on actions that break the fast by inserting medicine into three body openings: the rectum (enema), the nose, and the ear. The ruling is based on the hadith 'al-fitr mimma dakhala' (breaking the fast is by what enters), as transmitted by the Prophet (saw). The Hanafi school derives from this that any substance that enters the body cavity (jawf) through a natural passage and has a beneficial effect breaks the fast. However, kaffarah (expiation) is not required for these actions because the act is not similar to eating and drinking in form — the substance does not enter through the mouth and reach the stomach in the usual manner. A sub-ruling distinguishes between water and oil in the ear: water does not break the fast because it neither has the form (swallowing) nor the meaning (benefit), whereas oil breaks it because it is intended for medical benefit. This distinction is made on the basis of istihsan (juristic preference).

Key Terms
احتقان (ihtiqan): Administering an enema (medicine through the rectum)
استعاط (isti'tat): Snuffing medicine into the nose
اقطار (iqtaar): Pouring medicine into the ear
الفطر (al-fitr): Breaking the fast; the legal nullification of the fast
الجوف (al-jawf): The internal cavity of the body (stomach, intestines, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does pouring water into the ear break the fast?
A) Yes, because any liquid entering the body breaks the fast.
B) No, because water does not benefit the body in the same way as oil.
C) Yes, because water can reach the cavity.
D) No, because the hadith only mentions eating and drinking.

Key Takeaway
Inserting beneficial substances into the rectum, nose, or ear voids the fast but does not require kaffarah, while plain water in the ear is an exception.

Wet Medicine on Deep Wounds: Does it Break the Fast?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wet medicine for deep wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding wet medicine applied to deep wounds (ja'ifah/ammah) and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Wet medicine flows, dry medicine blocks: certainty determines if fast is broken.

Fasting requires keeping the body free from anything reaching the internal cavity. But when a wound penetrates the cavity, applying medicine raises a dispute: does it nullify the fast? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes because wet medicine flows, while his two students say no due to lack of certainty. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its circumstances
We have a fasting person who applies medicine to a deep wound that has already reached the body cavity (ja'ifah) or brain (ammah). The medicine is wet (ratb). The question: does this action break the fast?
The wound is pre-existing and penetrates the cavity; the medicine is applied externally.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the fast is broken. His reason: the wetness of the medicine mixes with the wound's moisture, increasing its downward inclination, so it necessarily reaches the cavity with certainty. This is a talil based on the nature of liquids.
He distinguishes wet from dry medicine; dry medicine absorbs moisture and blocks the passage, so it does not break the fast.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the fast is not broken. Their reason: lack of certainty that the medicine actually reaches the cavity. The wound passage may be closed at times; therefore the arrival is doubtful, and doubt does not nullify the fast. They analogize to dry medicine, which does not break the fast.
They emphasize the principle that certainty (yaqin) is required to nullify the fast.
4
Understand the point of disagreement
Both sides agree that if the medicine definitely reaches the cavity, the fast is broken. The disagreement is over the assessment of certainty: Abu Hanifa considers the flow of wet medicine as giving certain knowledge; the Sahibayn consider it probable but not certain.
The dispute hinges on epistemological certainty in a hidden internal process.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: the fast is broken when wet medicine is applied to a deep wound. Dry medicine remains non-breaking.
This is the opinion taken for fatwa, as stated in Al-Hidayah and later works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جائفہ زخم کی دوا کی وہ دوا جوف اور دماغ تک پہنچ گئی تو مفسد صوم ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
وَلَوْ دَاوَى جَائِفَةً أَوْ أَمَةٌ بِدَوَاءٍ فَوَصَلَ إلى جَوْفِهِ أَوْ دِمَاعِهِ أَفَطَرَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَالَّذِي يَصِلُ هُوَ الرَّطْبُ وَقَالَا لا يُفْطِرُ لِعَدَمِ التَّيْقَنِ بِالوُصُولِ لِانْضِمَامِ الْمَنْقَذِ مَرَّةً وَإِنسَاعِهِ أُخْرَى كَمَا فِى الْيَابِس مِنَ الدَّوَاء وَلَهُ أنَّ رُطُوبَةَ الدَّوَاءِ تَلاقى رُطُوبَةِ الْجَرَاحَةِ فَيَزْدَادُ مَيْلًا إِلَى الْأَسْفَلِ فَيَصِلُ إِلَى الْجَوْفِ بِخِلَافِ الْبَابِسِ لأَنَّهُ يَنْشِفُ رُطُوبَةَ الْجَرَاحَةِ فَيَنْسَدُّ فَمُهَا

تشریح جائفہ اس زخم کو کہتے ہیں جو جوف تک پہنچا ہوا ہو اور آمنہ اس زخم کو کہتے ہیں جو دماغ تک پہنچ چکا ہو۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ روزہ دار نے جائفہ یعنی پیٹ کے زخم میں یا سر کے زخم میں تر دواڈالی اور وہ سرایت کر کے پیٹ یا دماغ تک پہنچ گئی تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا روزہ فاسد ہو گیا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک فاسد نہیں ہوا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زخم کے اندر سے جوف یا دماغ تک دوا پہنچنے کی راہ کبھی تو بند رہتی ہے اور کبھی کھلی رہتی ہے پس اندر تک دوا پہنچے کا بقین نہیں ہے اور جب یقین نہیں بلکہ شک ہے اور شک کی وجہ سے روزہ فاسد نہیں ہو گا اس لئے اس صورت میں روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ خشک دوا ڈالنے کی صورت میں روز و فاسد نہیں ہوتا امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پیٹ کے زخم یا سر کے زخم میں ڈالی ہوئی دوا کا جوف یا دماغ کے اندر پہنچے کا یقینی علم تو متعد ر ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک باطنی چیز ہے لیکن ظاہر یہی ہے کہ جب دوا کی رطوبت زخم کی رطوبت کے ساتھ ملے گی تو اندر کی طرف اس کے میلان میں اضافہ ہی ہوگا اور جب اندر کی طرف میلان زیادہ ہوا تو وہ بالیقین جوف اور دماغ کے اندر پہنچ جائے گی اور جب جوف اور دماغ کے اندر پہنچ گئی تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائی گا اس کے برخلاف خشک دوا کہ جب اس کو زخم پر ڈالا جاتا ہے تو وہ زخم کی رطوبت کو اپنے اندر جذب کر کے زخم کے منہ کو بند کر دیتی ہے اور جب زخم کا منہ بند ہو گیا تو جوف کے اندر دوا کے پہنچنے کا امکان باقی نہ رہا اس لئے خشک دوا ڈالنے کی صورت میں روزہ فاسد نہ ہوا اور تر دوا کو خشک دوا پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔
And if he treated a penetrating wound (ja'ifah) or a head wound (ammah) with medicine, and it reached his cavity (jawf) or his brain (dimagh), he breaks his fast according to Abu Hanifa, and the medicine that reaches is wet. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not break his fast due to lack of certainty of arrival, because the passage sometimes closes and sometimes opens, as with dry medicine. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is the proof that the wetness of the medicine meets the wetness of the wound, so its downward inclination increases, and it reaches the cavity, unlike dry medicine because it absorbs the wound's moisture and its mouth closes.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a fasting person who applies medicine to a deep wound. A ja'ifah is a wound that penetrates to the body cavity (stomach area), and an ammah is a wound that reaches the brain (head). The question is: if wet medicine is applied to such a wound and it reaches the cavity or brain, does the fast break? Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the fast is broken (fasad) because the wetness of the medicine mixes with the wound's moisture, increasing its downward flow and making its arrival to the cavity certain. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the fast is not broken because there is no certainty that the medicine actually reached the cavity; the path through the wound may be blocked. They analogize it to dry medicine, which does not break the fast because it absorbs moisture and blocks the passage. Abu Hanifa distinguishes wet from dry, arguing that wet medicine necessarily flows inward. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa in this case, as the clear flow of wet medicine is considered certain. This dispute illustrates the Hanafi principle that certainty is required to nullify the fast, and differing assessments of certainty lead to different rulings.

Key Terms
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound that penetrates into the body cavity (chest or abdomen)
آمنة (ammah): A wound that penetrates to the brain (head wound)
رطب (ratb): Wet or liquid medicine
يابس (yabis): Dry or solid medicine

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason for the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding wet medicine applied to a deep wound?
A) Disagreement over whether the medicine is halal to use during fasting.
B) Disagreement over whether the medicine actually reaches the cavity (jawf) with certainty.
C) Disagreement over whether the hadith about entering applies to wounds.
D) Disagreement over the definition of 'wound'.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, applying wet medicine to a deep wound (ja'ifah/ammah) breaks the fast, because the wetness ensures certain entry into the cavity, unlike dry medicine which blocks the passage.

Ruling on Inserting Medicine into the Urethra (Ihlil)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether medicine entering the urethra breaks the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on whether medicine in the urethra breaks the fast and explain the anatomical basis for the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
The bladder is a barrier: Abu Hanifa rules the fast remains valid.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about what counts as reaching the body cavity (jawf) during fasting. The case of medicine inserted into the urethra (ihlil) raises the question: does it break the fast? The disagreement hinges on whether the bladder is a barrier or a passage. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi school's approach to novel medical procedures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the three positions
The act is inserting medicine into the urethra (ihlil). Note that Abu Hanifa says the fast is not broken, Abu Yusuf says it is broken, and Muhammad's view is mudtarib (inconsistent).
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself, not between madhahib.
2
Understand the anatomical basis for Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa considers the bladder (mathanah) a barrier (ha'il) between the urethra and the cavity. The medicine does not reach the jawf; it remains in the urethra/bladder.
Urine seeps (yatarashshahu) rather than flowing directly from the cavity.
3
Understand the anatomical basis for Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds there is a direct passage (manfadh) from the urethra to the cavity, as evidenced by urine exiting. Therefore, medicine reaches the cavity and breaks the fast.
This is a factual disagreement about anatomy, not fiqh principles.
4
Note Muhammad's inconsistency
Imam Muhammad's position is described as mudtarib (unsettled) – he may have held both views or wavered. This reduces the weight of his opinion.
The madhhab does not rely on his view in this case.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the fast is not broken. The dispute is considered over anatomy, not fiqh, and the madhhab follows Abu Hanifa.
No qada' or kaffarah is required if a fasting person uses such medicine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذکر کے سوراخ میں دوائی کا نا مفسد صوم نہیں .. اقوال فقہاء
وَلَوْ أَقْطَرَ فِي إِحْلِيلِهِ لَمْ يُفْطِرُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يُفْطِرُ وَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ مُضْطَرَبٌ فِيهِ فَكَأَنَّهُ وَقَعَ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْجَوْفِ مَنفَذ او لِهَذَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْهُ البَولُ وَوَقَعَ فَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ الْمَثَانَةَ بَيْنَهُمَا حَائِلُ وَالْبَولُ يَتَرَشَحُ مِنْهُ وَ هذَا لَيْسَ مِنْ بَابِ الْفِقَهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر روزہ دار نے اپنے ذکر کے سوراخ میں دوائی کائی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک افطار نہیں ہوا اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ افطار ہو جائے گا اور امام محمد کا قول اس میں مضطرب ہے گویا ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ ثابت ہوا کہ اس کے اصلیل اور جوف کے درمیان پہنچنے کی راہ ہے اور اسی وجہ سے اس سے پیشاب نکلتا ہے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ ثابت ہوا کہ اصلیل الوجوف کے درمیان مثانہ جاہلی ہے اور
And if he pours medicine into his urethra (ihlil), he does not break his fast according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he breaks his fast. And the statement of Muhammad is inconsistent (mudtarib) about it. So it occurred to Abu Yusuf that between it and the cavity there is a passage (manfadh), and that is why urine comes out of it. And it occurred to Abu Hanifa that between the urethra and the cavity there is a barrier (ha'il), the bladder, and urine seeps from it. And this is not from the category of fiqh (but rather anatomy).
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on inserting medicine into the urethra (ihlil — the external opening of the male genital) during fasting. There is a three-way intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the fast is not broken because the bladder acts as a barrier (ha'il) between the urethra and the body cavity (jawf); therefore, the medicine does not reach the cavity. Imam Abu Yusuf rules that the fast is broken because he considers there to be a direct passage (manfadh) from the urethra to the cavity, evidenced by the exit of urine. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's position is described as mudtarib (inconsistent or unsettled) — he may have held both views or had doubts. The commentary notes that this dispute is based on anatomical understanding rather than pure fiqh principles, indicating that the disagreement is over physical fact (whether the bladder is a complete barrier) rather than legal theory. The authoritative (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: inserting medicine into the urethra does not break the fast. However, the text is incomplete, as the explanation of Abu Hanifa's proof continues (the urine seeps out rather than comes directly).

Key Terms
إحليل (ihlil): The external opening of the urethra (the male urinary meatus)
مثانة (mathanah): The bladder
حائل (ha'il): Barrier, obstruction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa rule that inserting medicine into the urethra does not break the fast?
A) Because medicine is not food.
B) Because the bladder acts as a barrier between the urethra and the body cavity.
C) Because the hadith only mentions entering from the mouth.
D) Because Muhammad al-Shaybani's view is inconsistent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab relies on Abu Hanifa's view that the bladder is a barrier, so medicine inserted into the urethra does not break the fast.

Medicine in Urethra and the Validity of Fasting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on urethral medicine and fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on urethral medicine and identify the anatomical factor that determines the ruling.

Core Idea
The fast is broken only if the medicine reaches the internal cavity via a proven pathway.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: does inserting medicine into the urethra invalidate the fast? The answer hinges not on a legal maxim but on an anatomical fact—whether a passage exists from the urethra to the stomach. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf differ, and the commentator of al-Hidayah resolves the issue by deferring to medical knowledge.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and the conflicting reports from Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Abu Hanifa: fast not broken. Abu Yusuf: fast broken. Muhammad: unsettled.
2
Identify the root of disagreement
The dispute is based on whether there is a direct anatomical pathway from the urethra to the internal cavity (jwf).
Both imams agree on the general principle: reaching the jwf with medicine breaks the fast.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf’s proof
Abu Yusuf argues that urine exits through the urethra, proving the existence of a pathway. He analogizes to an enema, which clearly breaks the fast.
His evidence is empirical: the passage of urine.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa’s response
Abu Hanifa contends that the bladder (mathānah) is a barrier; urine merely oozes out and does not indicate a direct, open passage to the stomach.
The bladder intervenes, preventing the medicine from reaching the jwf.
5
Determine the author’s resolution
The author of al-Hidayah declares this a medical, not a legal, issue. The ruling follows the findings of anatomists.
If modern medicine confirms a pathway, the fast is broken; if not, it remains valid.

پیشاب اس سے مترشح ہوتا ہے اور یہ باب فقہ سے نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر روزہ دار نے اپنی پیشاب گاہ کے سوراخ میں دوانی کائی تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فاسد ہو جائے گا اور رہا امام محمد کا قول تو وہ مضطرب ہے چنانچہ مبسوط میں مذکور ہے کہ امام محمد امام ابو حنیفہ کی ساتھ ہیں اور امام طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کیساتھ ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس اختلاف کی بنیاد اس پر ہے کہ پیشاب گاہ کے سوراخ اور جوف کے درمیان کوئی ایسی راہ ہے یا نہیں جس سے کسی سیال چیز کو داخل کیا جا سکے حضرت امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ سوراخ اور جوف کے درمیان ایسا راستہ موجود ہے اور دلیل اسکی یہ ہے کہ پیشاب اندر سے اس راستہ سے نکل کر آتا ہے اور اگر کوئی راستہ نہ ہوتا تو پیشاب کس طرح نکلتا پس جب جوف اور ذکر کے سوراخ کے درمیان راستہ موجود ہے تو دوا جو ذ کر کے سوراخ میں ڈالی گئی ہے وہ جوف تک پہنچ جائے گی اور جوف تک کسی چیز کا اصلاح بدن کے لئے پہنچا نا مفسد صوم ہے لہذا اس سے بھی روز و فاسد ہو جائے گا جیسا کہ حقنہ سے فاسد ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور حضرت امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ پیشاب گاہ کے سوراخ اور جوف کے درمیان مثانہ حائل ہے اور ر با پیشاب کا نکلنا تو وہ اس سے مترشح ہوتا ہے پس جب امام صاحب کی تحقیق کے مطابق جوف اور سوراج کے درمیان مثانہ حائل ہے تو ذکر کے سوراخ میں ڈالی ہوئی دوا جوف تک نہ پہنچ سکے گی اور جب جوف تک نہیں پہنچی تو روزہ بھی فاسد نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جوف اور ذکر کے سوراخ کے درمیان راہ کا ہونا یا نہ ہو نا فقہ کا مسئلہ نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کا تعلق اطباء کے علم تشریح الا بدان سے ہے اس لئے اس مسئلہ میں انہیں کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اگر اطباء کہیں کہ جوف اور ذکر کے سوراخ کے درمیان راستہ ہے تو فساد صوم کا حکم لگا دیا جائے جیسا کہ قاضی ابو یوسف کا مذہب ہے اور اگر کہیں کہ راستہ نہیں تو عدم فساد کا حکم لگا دیا جائے جیسا کہ امام الہمام قدوۃ الا نام سیدنا حضرت امام اعظم کا مذہب ہے۔
Urine oozes from it, and this is not a chapter of fiqh. Explanation: The issue is that if a fasting person inserts medicine into the opening of his urethra, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the fast is not broken, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is broken. As for Imam Muhammad's statement, it is inconsistent: in al-Mabsut it is mentioned that Imam Muhammad agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa, and Imam Tahawi has mentioned that he agrees with Imam Abu Yusuf. The author of al-Hidayah says: The basis of this disagreement is whether there is a pathway between the urethral opening and the internal cavity (jwf) through which a fluid can be introduced. Imam Abu Yusuf says such a pathway exists, and his evidence is that urine emerges from inside through this pathway; if there were no pathway, how would urine come out? So when there is a pathway between the cavity and the urethral opening, the medicine inserted into the urethra will reach the cavity, and reaching the cavity for the purpose of bodily correction breaks the fast, so the fast is broken by this, just as it is broken by an enema. Imam Abu Hanifa said that the bladder intervenes between the urethral opening and the cavity, and urine oozes from it. So according to his investigation, since the bladder is a barrier, the medicine inserted into the urethra cannot reach the cavity, and since it does not reach the cavity, the fast is not broken. The author of al-Hidayah says: Whether there is a pathway between the cavity and the urethral opening is not a matter of fiqh but rather belongs to the medical science of anatomy; therefore in this matter one should refer to physicians. If physicians say there is a pathway, then the ruling of breaking the fast is applied, as is the madhhab of Qadi Abu Yusuf; and if they say there is no pathway, then the ruling of non-breakage is applied, as is the madhhab of the Great Imam, the leader of mankind, our master.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a fasting person inserting medicine into the urethra. The author, the commentator of al-Hidayah, first summarizes the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the fast is not broken; Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it is broken; and Imam Muhammad's position is unsettled, with conflicting transmissions. The key point of contention is anatomical: whether there is a direct passage from the urethra to the internal cavity (stomach/intestines). Abu Yusuf argues yes, because urine exits through that passage, and analogizes to an enema which breaks the fast. Abu Hanifa argues that the bladder is a barrier, so medicine cannot reach the cavity. The commentator then makes an important methodological observation: this is not a purely legal question but depends on empirical medical facts. Therefore, the ruling should follow the established anatomical knowledge of physicians. If they confirm a pathway, the fast is broken (following Abu Yusuf); if not, it remains intact (following Abu Hanifa). This illustrates that Hanafi fiqh can defer to external expertise when the issue involves non-legal facts.

Key Terms
دوانی (dawā): Medicine or suppository inserted into the urethra.
مثانہ (mathānah): Bladder, considered a barrier between urethra and internal cavity.
جوف (jawf): Internal cavity of the body (stomach/intestines); reaching it with substance intended for nutrition or medication breaks the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whether the medicine is food or medicine
B) Whether there is a pathway from the urethra to the internal cavity
C) Whether the medicine reaches the stomach through swallowing
D) Whether the person intended to break the fast

Key Takeaway
The ruling on urethral medicine depends on an anatomical fact, not purely legal reasoning; if a pathway exists, the fast is broken; if not, it remains valid.

Tasting Food Does Not Break Fast
Ruling with talil on tasting without swallowing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasting food while fasting and explain the distinction between form (surah) and meaning (ma'na) in evaluating whether an act invalidates the fast.

Core Idea
Tasting without swallowing does not break the fast; the key is avoiding both form and meaning of iftar.

In this lesson, we examine a common scenario for a fasting person: tasting food while cooking or checking seasoning. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a fundamental analytical tool—the distinction between the form (surah) and the meaning (ma'na) of iftar. Understanding this distinction allows you to correctly assess many edge cases in fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tasting food without swallowing. The ruling: the fast remains valid (sahih), but the act itself is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
The fast is not broken because there is no swallowing.
2
Understand the surah/ma'na framework
The author explains that for the fast to break, either the form (surah) of swallowing must occur, or the meaning (ma'na) of nourishment reaching the internal cavity must occur. Here, neither happens.
Surah refers to the physical act of swallowing; ma'na refers to the substantive benefit.
3
Recognize the reason for dislike
The act is disliked because it exposes the fast to potential invalidation, e.g., accidental swallowing.
This is a precautionary ruling, not a prohibition.
4
Apply the principle to other scenarios
Use the same framework: if a person accidentally swallows while rinsing, the fast breaks because surah (swallowing) occurred, even though the intent was absent.
Intent matters for sin, not for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی چیز کے چکھنے سے روزہ ٹوٹتا ہے یا نہیں؟
وَ مَنْ ذَاقَ شَيْأُ بِفَمِه لَمْ يُفْطِرُ لِعَدَمِ الْفِطْرِ صُورَةَ وَ مَعْنَى وَ يُكْرَهُ لَهُ ذَالِكَ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَعْرِيضِ الصَّوْمِ عَلَى الْفَسَادِ
ترجمہ اور جس نے اپنے منہ سے کوئی چیز چکھی تو اس کا روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوا کیونکہ فطر نہ صورت ہے اور نہ معنی ہے البتہ اس کے لئے یہ فعل مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس فعل میں روزہ کو فساد پر پیش کرنا ہے۔ تشریح - مسئلہ اگر کسی نے اپنے منہ سے کچھ چکھا تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں نہ تو صورۂ افطار ہوا کہ کسی چیز کو نگلا ہو اور نہ معنی افطار ہوا ہو کہ اصلاح بدن کے لئے کوئی چیز جوف میں پہنچائی گئی ہو پس جب نہ صورۃ افطار ہوا اور نہ معنی افطار ہوا تو روزہ کیونکر فاسد ہوگا البتہ یہ عمل مکروہ ضرور ہے اور وجہ کر بہت یہ ہے کہ اس عمل میں روزہ کا فساد پر پیش کرنا ہوا۔
Does tasting something break the fast? And whoever tastes something with his mouth, his fast is not broken, because there is no breaking of the fast in form nor in meaning. Yet it is disliked for him due to exposing the fast to invalidation. Translation: And whoever tastes something with his mouth, his fast is not invalidated, because there is neither form nor meaning of breaking. Nevertheless, this act is disliked for him because in it there is exposing the fast to invalidation. Explanation: If someone tastes something with his mouth, his fast will not break, because in this case there is neither the form of breaking (swallowing something) nor the meaning of breaking (conveying something to the cavity for bodily correction). So when neither the form nor the meaning of breaking occurred, how could the fast be invalidated? However, this act is disliked, and the reason for dislike is that in this act there is exposing the fast to invalidation.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: tasting food (or any substance) without swallowing does not invalidate the fast. The reasoning is twofold: first, there is no 'form' of iftar (i.e., no actual swallowing), and second, there is no 'meaning' of iftar (i.e., no nutrition or medication reaching the internal cavity). Thus, the fast remains valid. However, the act is makruh (disliked) because it potentially leads to accidentally swallowing something, thereby exposing the fast to the risk of invalidation. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ذاق (dhāqa): To taste with the tongue without swallowing.
صورة (ṣūrah): The apparent act of swallowing; the physical form of eating/drinking.
معنى (maʿnā): The substantive benefit of nutrition or medication reaching the internal cavity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tasting food without swallowing makruh for a fasting person?
A) Because it directly breaks the fast
B) Because it involves using the mouth for food
C) Because it exposes the fast to the risk of invalidation
D) Because it nullifies the reward of fasting

Key Takeaway
The fast breaks only if there is swallowing (surah) or nourishment/medication reaching the cavity (ma'na); mere tasting without swallowing leaves the fast intact, though it is disliked.

Woman Chewing Food for Child During Fast
Ruling on a fasting woman chewing food for her infant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a fasting woman chewing food for her infant and distinguish between when it is makruh and when it is permissible based on the availability of an alternative.

Core Idea
Chewing food for an infant while fasting is normally makruh, but necessity (lack of alternative) makes it permissible.

Fasting mothers often face the dilemma of needing to feed their infants solid food by chewing it first. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this act, which balances the sanctity of the fast with the obligation to care for the child. The core principle is that the ruling changes based on whether an alternative to the mother's chewing exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is a fasting woman chewing solid food for her infant. The default ruling (assuming no special circumstances) is makruh (disliked).
Makruh here refers to tanzihi (slightly disliked), not tahrimi (prohibited).
2
Find the condition that changes the ruling
The ruling changes if she has no alternative (budd) — i.e., no other non-fasting person can chew the food for the child. If she has an alternative, it remains makruh; if not, it becomes permissible (la ba'sa).
The Arabic phrase 'لا بأس' indicates no sin or harm.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
The permissibility is based on the necessity of preserving the child's life. The text draws an analogy (qiyas) to the case where a mother may break her fast if she fears for the child's life, showing a hierarchy of obligations: care for the child overrides the fast in cases of necessity.
This is an application of the legal maxim 'al-darura tubihu al-mahzurat' (necessity permits the prohibited).
4
Apply to concrete scenarios
Test the ruling: Scenario A: Mother alone, baby hungry, no one to help → permissible. Scenario B: Grandmother present who can chew the food → mother should not chew (makruh).
The presence of any adult not obligated to fast (e.g., a child past puberty who is not fasting? Actually a non-fasting adult is the alternative.

عورت کا بچے کے لئے حالت روزہ میں کھانا چبانے کا حکم
وَيُكْرَهُ لِلْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَمْضَعَ لِصَيِّيهَا الطَّعَامَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهَا مِنْهُ بُثْلَمَا بَيَّنَا وَلَا بَأْسَ إِذَا لَمْ تَجِدْ مِنْهُ بُدا صِيالَةً لِلوَلَدِ أَلَا ترى أن لَهَا أنْ تُفْطَرَ إِذَا خَافَتْ عَلَى وَلَدِهَا
ترجمہ اور عورت کے لئے اپنے بچہ کے لئے کھانا چبانا مکروہ ہے بشرطیکہ اس کے واسطے اس سے کوئی چارہ ہو۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور جب اس سے کوئی چارہ نہ ہو تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے بچہ کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر، کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر اس کو بچہ پر خوف ہو تو اس کے لئے افطار کرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح روزے کی حالت میں عورت کے لئے اپنے بچہ کو کھانا چبا چبا کر کھلانا مکروہ ہے بشرطیکہ اس عورت کے لئے دوسرا چارہ کار موجود ہو مثلاً اس کے پاس کوئی ایسا آدمی بیٹھا ہے جس پر روزہ فرض نہ ہو اور وہ اس بچہ کو چبا کر کھلا سکتا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں عورت کا چبانا مکروہ ہے اور وجہ کراہت وہی ہے کہ اس صورت میں روزہ کا فساد پر پیش کرنا لازم آئے گا اور اگر خود چبا کر کھلانے کے سواء کوئی چارہ نہ ہو تو پھر کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ بچہ کی حفاظت بھی ضروری ہے چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ اگر شیر خوار بچہ کے شدت بھول کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو اور عورت کو روزہ کی حالت میں دودھ نہیں اتر تا تو اس صورت میں عورت کے لئے افطار کی اجازت ہے۔
Ruling on a woman chewing food for her child while fasting: And it is disliked for a woman to chew food for her infant if she has an alternative to it, as we have explained. And there is no harm if she finds no alternative, for the preservation of the child. Do you not see that she is permitted to break her fast if she fears for her child? Translation: And it is disliked for a woman to chew food for her child if she has an alternative. For the reason we have mentioned. And if she has no alternative, then there is no harm, for the preservation of the child. Do you not see that if she fears for her child, she is permitted to break her fast? Explanation: For a woman fasting, it is disliked to chew food and feed it to her child, provided there is another alternative available, for example, if there is a person who is not fasting and can chew for the child. In such a case, her chewing is disliked, because it exposes the fast to invalidation. But if there is no alternative except her chewing, then there is no harm, because the protection of the child is also necessary. Indeed, if a nursing mother fears that the child may die due to extreme hunger and her milk does not come down, she is permitted to break her fast.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage provides a nuanced ruling for a fasting woman who needs to chew food for her infant. The default ruling is makruh (disliked) because chewing produces saliva that could be swallowed unintentionally, risking the fast. However, this karahah applies only if an alternative exists, such as a non-fasting person who can chew the food. If there is no alternative, it becomes permissible (no harm) because preserving the child's life takes precedence. The text further supports this by noting that if the child is in danger (e.g., from hunger and lack of milk), the mother is even allowed to break her fast entirely. This shows the Hanafi concern for necessity (darurah) and hierarchy of obligations: preserving life can override the fast.

Key Terms
مضغ (maḍgh): Chewing food for an infant before feeding.
صبی (ṣabiyy): Infant or young child who cannot chew solid food independently.
چارہ (chārah): Alternative or means to avoid the disliked act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a fasting woman has no alternative but to chew food for her child?
A) It remains makruh
B) It is haram
C) There is no harm (ja'iz)
D) Her fast becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
A fasting woman may chew food for her infant only when no alternative exists; otherwise, it is disliked.

Chewing Gum Does Not Break the Fast: Hanafi Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with expansion on chewing gum during fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on chewing gum while fasting, identify the two exceptions where it may invalidate the fast, and explain why it is considered makruh.

Core Idea
Chewing gum does not break the fast unless it is non-cohesive or black and particles reach the stomach; but it is still disliked.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, we examine a nuanced ruling regarding chewing gum (ʿilk) during a fast. The basic principle is that the fast remains valid because gum clings to the teeth and does not reach the cavity. However, the text presents two reported exceptions and explains the disliked nature of the act, with a distinction between men and women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Find the statement that chewing gum does not break the fast and the reason given (it does not reach the cavity).
The Arabic word ʿilk refers to resin or gum.
2
Recognize the two exceptions
The text mentions two scenarios that may break the fast: gum that is not cohesive (powdery) and black gum. Understand why each may allow particles to reach the stomach.
3
Understand the makruh ruling
Even when the fast is valid, chewing gum is disliked for two reasons: it risks the fast and creates suspicion. Grasp the concept of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking excuses).
4
Distinguish between men and women
For women not fasting, gum is not disliked because it substitutes for miswak. For men, it is disliked unless for medical reasons, and some scholars say it is not recommended due to resemblance to women.

Source Text

Chewing gum does not break the fast: And chewing gum does not break the fast because it does not reach his cavity. And it is said: if it is not cohesive, it breaks because some of its parts reach it. And it is said: if it is black, it breaks even if it is cohesive, because it disintegrates. However, it is disliked for the fasting person because of exposing the fast to invalidation, and because he will be suspected of breaking the fast. And it is not disliked for a woman if she is not fasting, because for women it takes the place of the miswak. And it is disliked for men, according to what is said, if it is not due to an illness. And it is said: it is not recommended because of resemblance to women. Translation: And chewing gum does not break the fast for the fasting person because it will not reach his cavity. And some said: when the gum is not cohesive, it breaks the fast because some of its parts reach the cavity. And some said: when the gum is black, it breaks even if it is cohesive, because black gum disintegrates. But chewing gum is disliked for the fasting person because it exposes the fast to invalidation and because he will be suspected of breaking the fast. And it is not disliked for a woman if she is not fasting, because for women chewing gum serves as a substitute for miswak. And for men, it is disliked, according to what is said, provided it is not due to an illness. And some said: it is not recommended because it resembles women. Explanation: The issue is that if a fasting person chews gum, his fast is not broken because gum, due to its stickiness, clings to the teeth and does not reach the cavity. And whatever does not reach the cavity does not break the fast. And some jurists said: if the gum is not cohesive but rather fine particles, then chewing it breaks the fast because some parts reach the cavity. And some jurists said: if the gum is black in color, then chewing it breaks the fast even if it is cohesive, because black gum disintegrates into particles and some parts reach the cavity. However, even if the fast is not broken, chewing gum is disliked for the fasting person because it exposes the fast to invalidation, since it is possible that some particles descend through the throat. A second reason is that people will suspect him of breaking the fast, i.e., when he is...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on chewing gum (resin) while fasting. The basic ruling is that it does not break the fast because gum, being sticky, clings to the teeth and does not reach the internal cavity. However, there are two reported exceptions: (1) if the gum is not cohesive but powdery, it may break because particles can reach the stomach; (2) if the gum is black, it tends to disintegrate, so even if cohesive at first, it may break. Despite the fast not being invalidated, chewing gum is makruh for the fasting person for two reasons: it risks the fast (particles might be swallowed) and it creates suspicion that one is eating. For women who are not fasting, it is not disliked because gum serves as a substitute for the miswak (teeth-cleaning stick). For men, it is disliked unless for a medical reason, and some say it is not recommended because it resembles women's behavior. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the complete ruling is clear: the default is that gum does not break the fast, with exceptions for non-cohesive or black types.

Key Terms
علك (ʿilk): Chewing gum or resin, a substance that is chewed but not swallowed.
ملتئم (multaʾim): Cohesive, sticking together as a single mass.
مسواک (miswāk): A teeth-cleaning stick; used here as an analogous permissible oral activity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The default Hanafi ruling is that chewing gum does not break the fast unless the gum is non-cohesive or black and particles reach the stomach; nevertheless, it is disliked for the fasting person due to risk and suspicion.
