Chewing Gum While Fasting: Ruling and Rationale
Explaining the ruling on chewing gum during fasting with reasons and variant opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on chewing gum while fasting and explain the reasons for its dislikedness (karaha) and the distinctions based on gum type and gender.

Core Idea
Chewing gum does not break the fast, but is makruh for the fasting person.

You might wonder whether chewing gum invalidates your fast. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: chewing gum itself does not break the fast as long as no particles reach the stomach. However, it is discouraged (makruh) because it exposes the fast to potential corruption and causes suspicion. The ruling also differentiates based on the gum’s cohesion and the person’s gender.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and its basis
The text opens with the general ruling: chewing gum does not break the fast. The reason given is that the gum does not reach the stomach. Observe that the ruling is based on the physical path of the gum (wusul ila al-jawf).
This is a direct causal reasoning (taʿlīl) without textual proof.
2
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
The text reports two alternative opinions (qīla): if the gum is not cohesive (multanima) or is black (aswad), it may invalidate the fast because particles can reach the stomach. Understand that these opinions are considered weaker (marjūḥ) in the school.
The first opinion (la yufṭir) is the mufta bihi.
3
Understand the reasons for karaha
Even though the fast remains valid, chewing gum is makruh for two reasons: (1) it exposes the fast to corruption (taʿrīḍ al-ṣawm lil-fasād) – accidental swallowing of particles; (2) it leads to suspicion (yuttahamu bil-ifṭār).
This highlights the Hanafi concern for both the act's integrity and social perception.
4
Apply the gender distinction
The text states that for a non-fasting woman, gum is not makruh because it substitutes for miswak. For men, it is disliked (unless due to illness) and some even say it is not mustaḥabb because of resemblance to women (tashabbuh bi al-nisāʾ).
Note the gender-specific reasoning: women's use of gum as an oral cleaning tool is analogous to miswak, which is recommended for women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَضْعُ الْعِلْكِ لَا يُفْطِرُ الصَّائِمُ لأَنَّهُ لَا يَضِلُّ إِلى جَوْفِهِ وَقِيلَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مُلْتَنِمًا يُفْسِدُ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِلُ إِلَيْهِ بَعْضُ أَجْزَائِهِ وَ قِيْلَ إِذَا كَانَ أَسْوَدُ يُفْسِدُ وَ إِنْ كَانَ مُلْتَئِمًا لأنَّهُ يَتَفَكَّتُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَكْرَة لِلصَّائِمِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَعْرِيضِ الصَّوْمِ لِلْفَسَادِ ولأنَّه يُتّهمُ بالا فُطَار وَلَا يَكْرَهُ لِلْمَرْأَةِ إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنُ صَائِمَةً لِقِيَامِهِ مَقَامَ السَوَاكِ فِى حَقَّهِنَّ وَيَكْرَهُ لِلرِّجَالِ عَلى مَاقِيلَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ عِلَّةٍ وَقِيلَ لَا يَسْتَحِبُّ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ التَّشْبِيْهِ بِالنِّسَاءِ
Chewing gum does not break the fast of a fasting person because it does not reach his stomach. And it was said: if it is not cohesive it invalidates because some of its parts reach him. And it was said: if it is black it invalidates even if cohesive because it crumbles. However, it is disliked for the fasting person because of exposing the fast to corruption and because he is suspected of breaking his fast. And it is not disliked for a woman if she is not fasting because it takes the place of miswak for them. And it is disliked for men according to what was said unless it is due to an illness. And it was said: it is not recommended because of resemblance to women.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on chewing gum (ʿilk) while fasting. It begins by stating the general ruling: chewing gum does not invalidate the fast because the gum, due to its cohesiveness, does not reach the stomach. Then it presents two alternative opinions: first, if the gum is not cohesive (i.e., powdery), it invalidates the fast because some particles reach the stomach; second, if the gum is black, it invalidates even if cohesive because black gum tends to crumble. Despite the fast not being invalidated, chewing gum is makruh (disliked) for the fasting person for two reasons: (1) it exposes the fast to potential corruption (since some particles might accidentally go down), and (2) it causes suspicion that one is eating. For women who are not fasting, it is not makruh because gum serves as a substitute for miswak in their case (as miswak may be harsh). For men, it is disliked unless they have an illness that necessitates it; some say it is merely not recommended (mustahabb) due to resembling women. This reflects Hanafi concern for both the integrity of the fast and social perception.

Key Terms
مَضْعُ الْعِلْكِ (maḍʿ al-ʿilk): Chewing gum (resinous substance) with the teeth to extract its flavor or benefit.
مُلْتَنِمًا (multaniman): Cohesive, stuck together (referring to gum that holds its form).
يَتَفَكَّتُ (yatafakkatu): It crumbles, breaks into pieces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is made from impure substances
D) Because it is forbidden by consensus

Key Takeaway
Chewing gum does not break the fast but is makruh for the fasting person due to risk of corruption and suspicion.

Applying Kohl and Mustache Oil While Fasting
Permissibility of kohl and mustache oil with intention conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying kohl and mustache oil during fasting and explain how intention affects permissibility.

Core Idea
Kohl and mustache oil do not invalidate the fast; intention for treatment vs. adornment changes the ruling for men.

In this lesson, we examine the permissibility of applying kohl (antimony) to the eyes and oil to the mustache while fasting. The Hanafi school holds that these actions are generally allowed because they are forms of comfort that do not enter the body. However, intention plays a crucial role, especially for men, where adornment is discouraged. We will explore the textual proof from the Prophet's practice on Ashura and the conditions that affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their default ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses two actions: applying kohl to the eyes and oiling the mustache. The default ruling is 'no harm' (la ba's), indicating permissibility (mubah).
The phrase 'la ba'sa' is a common Hanafi expression for permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Prophet's recommendation (nadb) of kohl on Ashura alongside fasting. Identify this as a Sunnah proof (Sunnah ahad) that kohl does not conflict with fasting.
The hadith is not quoted in full but referenced; the combination implies compatibility.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand that the Prophet would not recommend both kohl and fasting together if kohl harmed the fast. This indicates that external applications do not break it.
The proof is inferential: the conjunction of two recommendations shows they are compatible.
4
Apply the condition of intention for men
The text explicitly states that for men, kohl is permissible only if intended for treatment (tadawi), not adornment (zinah). Oiling the mustache is recommended if not for adornment.
Intention (niyyah) distinguishes between permissible and disliked acts for men.
5
Note the beard length limitation
The passage adds that one should not oil the mustache to lengthen the beard beyond the sunnah length (a fistful, qabda). This shows a limit related to grooming.
This is an additional guidance, not a ruling on fasting validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأسَ بِالكُحْلِ وَدُهْنِ الشَّارِبِ لأَنَّهُ نَرْعُ ارْتِفَاقِ لَيْسَ مِنْ مَّحْطُورِ القَوْمِ وَقَدْ نَدْبَ النَّبِيُّ إِلَى الْإِكْتِحَالِ يَوْمَ عَاشُورَاء وَإِلَى الصَّوْمِ فِيهِ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالاكْتِحَالِ لِلرِّجَالِ إِذَا قَصَدْ بِهِ التَّدَاوِي دُونَ الزَّيْنَةِ وَيَسْتَحْسِنُ دُهُنُ الشَّارِبِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُن مِن قَصْدِهِ الرِّيْنَةَ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْمَلْ عَمَلَ الْخِصَابِ وَلَا يَفْعَلُ لَتَطْوِيلِ اللَّحْيَةِ إِذَا كَانَتْ بِقَدَرٍ المسنون وَهُوَ الْقُبْضَةُ
And there is no harm in applying kohl (antimony) and oiling the mustache, because it is a type of comfort that is not among the prohibited things for fasting. And indeed the Prophet recommended applying kohl on the day of Ashura and fasting on it. And there is no harm in kohl for men if he intends treatment, not adornment. And oiling the mustache is recommended if his intention is not adornment, because it acts like dye (khidab). And he should not do it for lengthening the beard if it is already of the recommended length, which is a fistful.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah rules on using kohl (surma) and oil on the mustache during fasting. The general principle: these are permissible because they fall under everyday comforts (irtifāq), not among the prohibitions of fasting (maḥẓūrāt al-ṣawm). The author provides a proof from the Sunnah: the Prophet ﷺ recommended both fasting and applying kohl on the day of Ashura, implying kohl does not harm the fast. For men, kohl is permissible only if intended for medical treatment, not for beautification (zīnah). Oil on the mustache is considered commendable (yastaḥsin) if not for adornment, because it serves the same purpose as dye (khidāb). The passage concludes by mentioning that one should not apply oil to lengthen the beard if it is already at the Sunnah length (a fistful, qabḍah). This reflects the Hanafi approach: actions that are not inherently contradictory to fasting are permitted, while intentions matter for avoiding dislike.

Key Terms
الكُحْل (al-kuhl): Antimony powder applied to the eyes (kohl/surma).
دُهْنِ الشَّارِبِ (duhn al-shārib): Applying oil to the mustache.
الْقُبْضَةُ (al-qabḍah): A fistful – the recommended length of the beard (grabbing it, anything beyond is excess).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Applying kohl and mustache oil does not break the fast; intention determines the recommendation for men.

Chewing Gum While Fasting: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling on chewing gum for fasting and non-fasting persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for chewing gum (gond) for a fasting person, a non-fasting woman, and a non-fasting man, and explain the underlying principles of sadd al-dhara'i' and tashabbuh bi al-nisa.

Core Idea
Chewing gum while fasting is makruh tanzih due to suspicion; for women it substitutes miswak; for men it is mubah but not mustahab.

This lesson examines a specific ruling on chewing gum (gond) during fasting. The text distinguishes between the fasting and non-fasting states, and between men and women, based on principles of avoiding suspicion and gender imitation. Understanding this nuanced ruling helps you apply similar reasoning to other acts that may appear like eating.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person's state
Determine whether the person is fasting or not, and whether male or female. The ruling changes based on these factors.
Fasting includes both obligatory and voluntary fasts.
2
Apply the ruling for a fasting person
For any fasting person (male or female), chewing gum is makruh tanzih because it gives the appearance of eating and causes suspicion.
This is based on the maxim 'sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).
3
Apply the ruling for a non-fasting woman
For a non-fasting woman, chewing gum is not makruh but rather stands in place of miswak, which is sunnah. It is considered mustahab for her due to delicate teeth.
This is a concession specific to women.
4
Apply the ruling for a non-fasting man
For a non-fasting man without illness, chewing gum is mubah (permissible) but not mustahab. Some scholars even consider it makruh to avoid resemblance to women.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is mubah but not mustahab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دیکھے گا کہ کچھ کھا رہا ہے تو اس کو روزہ نہ رکھنے کے ساتھ متہم کرے گا اور لوگ اسکو برا خیال کریں گے اور جو فعل ظاہر میں لوگوں کو برا نظر آئے تو وہ مکروہ ہے اس لئے یہ بھی مکروہ ہوگا۔ اور ڈورت اگر روزہ دار نہ ہو تو اس کو گوند چہانا مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ عورتوں کے حق میں گوند چبانا مسواک کرنے کے قائم مقام ہے اور گوند کو مسواک کے قائم مقام اس لئے قرار دیا ہے کہ عورتیں انتہائی کمزور اور نازک ہوتی ہیں اور ان کے دانت بھی کمزور اور مسوڑھے بھی نازک ہوں گے تو وہ مسواک جیسی بدن خراش چیز کو کس طرح برداشت کر سکتی ہیں ہاں مردوں کو اگر کوئی بیماری نہ ہو اور ان کے لئے گوند چبانا تعمر وہ ہے ان بعض نے کہا ہے کہ مردوں کے لئے گوند چہانا مباح تو ہے مگر مستحب نہیں ہے اور مستحب اس لئے نہیں کہ مردوں کے لئے گوند چہانے کی صورت میں مردوں کا عورتوں کے مشابہ ہونا لازم آئے گا اور تشہیہ بالنساء قطعاً مناسب نہیں ہے اس لئے مردوں کے گوند چبانے کو مکروہ یا غیر مستحب قرار دیا ہے۔
He will see that he is eating something, so he will suspect that he is not keeping the fast, and people will think badly of him. An act that appears bad to people in appearance is makruh, so this too will be makruh. And if the other (woman) is not fasting, then chewing gum for her is not makruh because for women, chewing gum stands in place of using a miswak. Gum has been made equivalent to miswak because women are extremely weak and delicate, and their teeth are also weak and gums are delicate, so how can they bear a rough thing like a miswak? But for men, if they have no illness, chewing gum for them is... some have said that for men, chewing gum is permissible but not mustahab. It is not mustahab because if men chew gum, it would necessitate men resembling women, and resemblance to women is absolutely not appropriate. Therefore, men's chewing gum is declared makruh or non-mustahab.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about chewing gum (gond) during fasting. It distinguishes between a fasting person and a non-fasting person, and between men and women. The author states that if a fasting person chews gum, it is makruh because it gives the appearance of eating and people will suspect him. For a non-fasting woman, it is not makruh because gum-chewing serves as a substitute for miswak due to women's delicate teeth. For a non-fasting man, it is merely permissible (mubah) but not recommended (mustahab) to avoid resemblance to women. Some scholars consider it makruh for men altogether. The underlying principle is avoiding acts that cause suspicion (sadd al-dhara'i') and avoiding imitation of the opposite gender.

Key Terms
گوند (gond): Gum, a type of resin chewed as a mouth freshener.
مسواک (miswak): A tooth-cleaning twig used as a sunnah act.

D) It is mubah with no issue.

Key Takeaway
Chewing gum while fasting is makruh tanzih; for non-fasting women it is a miswak substitute; for men it is mubah but not mustahab.

Applying Kohl and Oiling Mustache While Fasting
Ruling that kohl and oiling mustache do not break the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying kohl and oiling the mustache during fasting and explain the evidence and conditions.

Core Idea
Comforts of life do not break the fast; kohl and oil are permissible unless done for adornment.

Fasting requires abstaining from food, drink, and sexual relations, but what about actions that are merely comforting or beautifying? The Hanafi school addresses this through the principle of 'comfort (irtifāq)' not being prohibited. In this lesson, we examine the ruling on applying kohl (surma) to the eyes and oiling the mustache during a fast, drawing on the Prophet's practice on the day of Ashura and the conditions that refine the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, note the acts in question: applying kohl to the eyes and oiling the mustache. The text states there is no harm (lā ba's) – meaning permissibility.
The default ruling for these acts is permissibility (ibāha).
2
Understand the Principle
The author explains the rationale: these are comforts (irtifāq) of life, not from the prohibited actions (maḥẓūrāt) of fasting. This principle applies broadly to non-nutritive substances.
Comforts are not automatically prohibited unless they fall under food/drink or sexual acts.
3
Analyze the Evidence from Ashura
The Prophet ﷺ encouraged applying kohl and fasting on Ashura. If kohl broke the fast, he would not have recommended it on a fasting day. This hadith provides a proof (dalīl) that kohl does not invalidate the fast.
The hadith is ahad but its indication is clear (dalāla qaṭ‘iyya) – the encouragement implies no nullification.
4
Note the Conditions for Men
The text specifies that for men, kohl must be for treatment (tadāwī) and not for adornment (zīna). Similarly, oiling the mustache is mustaḥsan (commendable) only if adornment is not intended.
Adornment is considered makrūh for men because it resembles women's practices.
5
Apply the Same Reasoning to Beard Oiling
The passage extends to beard oiling: if the beard has reached the sunnah length (one fistful), one should not oil it to lengthen it further. The sunnah is to trim the excess, as practiced by Ibn ‘Umar.
This shows that the ruling is not just about breaking the fast but also about recommended grooming.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سرمہ اور مونچھوں کو تیل لگانا مفسد صوم نہیں
وَلَا بَأسَ بِالكُحْلِ وَدُهْنِ الشَّارِبِ لأَنَّهُ نَرْعُ ارْتِفَاقِ لَيْسَ مِنْ مَّحْطُورِ القَوْمِ وَقَدْ نَدْبَ النَّبِيُّ إِلَى الْإِكْتِحَالِ يَوْمَ عَاشُورَاء وَإِلَى الصَّوْمِ فِيهِ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالاكْتِحَالِ لِلرِّجَالِ إِذَا قَصَدْ بِهِ التَّدَاوِي دُونَ الزَّيْنَةِ وَيَسْتَحْسِنُ دُهُنُ الشَّارِبِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُن مِن قَصْدِهِ الرِّيْنَةَ لِأَنَّهُ يَعْمَلْ عَمَلَ الْخِصَابِ وَلَا يَفْعَلُ لَتَطْوِيلِ اللَّحْيَةِ إِذَا كَانَتْ بِقَدَرٍ المسنون وَهُوَ الْقُبْضَةُ
ترجمہ اور سرمہ لگانے اور مونچھوں کو تیل لگانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایک قسم کی آسائش ہے اور آسائش روزے کی ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہے حالانکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عاشورا کے دن رور و ر کھنے اور سرمہ لگانے کو مندوب قرار دیا ہے اور مردوں کے واسطے سرمہ لگانے میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ سرمہ لگانے سے دوا کرنا مقصود ہے نہ کہ زینت اور مونچھوں کو تیل لگانا مستحسن سے جبکہ اس کا ارادو زیانت کا نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ خضاب کا کام دیتا ہے اور داڑھی بڑھانے کے لئے ایسا نہ کرنا چاہئے جبکہ داڑھی مقدار مسنون ہو اور وہ ایک
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ روزے کی حالت میں سرمہ لگانا اور مونچھوں کو تیل لگانا بلا کراہت جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیز ہیں زندگی کی آسائش میں سے ہیں اور آسائش زندگی روزے کی ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہیں اس لئے ان دونوں چیزوں کے استعمال کرنے میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے بلکہ جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے یوم عاشوراء میں دو چیزوں کو مندوب قرار دیا ہے ایک روزہ ، دوم سرمہ لگانا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ روزہ کی حالت میں سرمہ لگانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ورنہ آنحضور نے روزے کے دن سرمہ لگانے کو مندوب کیوں
قرار دیتے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مردوں کے لئے بغرض تداوی سرمہ لگانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے البتہ زینت حاصل کرنے کے لئے مردوں کا سرمہ لگانا غیر مناسب ہے کیونکہ سرمہ لگانا عورتوں کی زینت ہے اسی طرح اگر مونچھوں کو تیل لگانے سے زینت مقصود نہ ہو تو سن ہے کیونکہ مونچھوں کو تیل لگانا خضاب کا کام کرتا ہے اور خضاب کرنا سنت سے ثابت ہے اور اس لئے مونچھوں کو تیل لگانا مستحسن
و پسندیدہ ہو گا صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ داڑھی بڑھانے کے ارادے سے بھی تیل نہ لگائے بشرطیکہ اداڑھی مقدار مسنون یعنی ایک مٹھی ہو ایک مٹھی کے بقدر داڑھی کے مسنون ہونے پر وہ حدیث دلیل ہے جس کو امام ترندی نے جامع ترندی میں روایت کیا ہے عَن رَّسُولِ اللهِ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَأْخُذُ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ مِنْ طُولِهَا وَعَرضها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنی داڑھی کے طول اور عرض سے لیا کرتے تھے یعنی کاٹ کر کم کرتے تھے لیکن عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیث اس کے معارض ہے حدیث یہ ہے کہ احصوا الشوارب وَاعْفُوا اللحى عن مونچھیں موند و اور داڑھی بڑھاؤ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبداللہ بن عمر جو اس حدیث کے راوی ہیں ان کا خود عمل یہ تھا کہ ایک مٹھی سے زائد داڑھی کاٹ دیا کرتے تھے چنانچہ مروی ہے عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أنَّه كَانَ يَقْصُ عَلَى اللَّحْيَةِ ثُمَّ يَقْصُّ مَاتَحْتَ الْقُبْضَةِ عن ابن عمر اپنی ذاری پکڑتے تھے پھر ایک مٹھی سے نیچے کی داڑھی کاٹ دیا کرتے تھے ۔
Kohl and oiling the mustache do not break the fast. And there is no harm in kohl and oiling the mustache because it is a type of comfort and not from the prohibited actions of the people. And the Prophet (SAW) encouraged applying kohl on Ashura and fasting on that day. And there is no harm in men applying kohl when they intend treatment, not adornment. And oiling the mustache is mustahsan if one does not intend adornment, because it acts like henna. And one should not do it to lengthen the beard if it is at the sunnah length, which is a fistful. Translation: And there is no harm in applying kohl and oiling the mustache because it is a type of comfort and comfort is not among the prohibitions of fasting, while the Prophet (SAW) declared applying kohl and fasting on Ashura as recommended. And for men, there is no harm in applying kohl when treatment is intended, not adornment. And oiling the mustache is mustahsan when adornment is not intended, because it acts like henna. And one should not do it to lengthen the beard if the beard is at the sunnah length, which is one fistful. Explanation: The issue is that applying kohl and oiling the mustache during fasting is permissible without dislike because both are comforts of life and comforts of life are not among the prohibitions of fasting. Rather, the Messenger of Allah (SAW) declared two things as recommended on the day of Ashura: fasting and applying kohl. This proves that there is no harm in applying kohl during fasting, otherwise the Prophet would not have recommended it on a fasting day. The author of al-Hidayah said: For men, applying kohl for treatment is not problematic, but for adornment it is inappropriate because kohl is women's adornment. Similarly, if oiling the mustache is not for adornment, then it is sunnah because oiling the mustache acts like henna, and using henna is proven as sunnah. Therefore, oiling the mustache is mustahsan and commendable. The author of al-Hidayah said: One should not oil the beard to lengthen it, provided the beard is of the sunnah length, i.e., one fistful. The evidence for the beard being sunnah at one fistful is the hadith narrated by Imam al-Tirmidhi in Jami' al-Tirmidhi from the Messenger of Allah that he used to trim from the length and width of his beard. But the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar contradicts this: 'Trim the mustaches and let the beards grow.' The response is that Abdullah ibn Umar himself, who narrated this hadith, used to trim his beard beyond a fistful. It is narrated from Ibn Umar that he would grasp his beard and then trim what was below the grip.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage combines a ruling statement and proof. The author states that applying kohl and oiling the mustache do not break the fast. The proof is the Prophet's practice on Ashura. The ruling is further qualified: for men, kohl is allowed only for medicinal purposes, not for adornment, since adornment is for women. Similarly, oiling the mustache is recommended (mustahsan) if not for adornment, as it serves like henna. The passage also addresses beard length: if the beard has reached the sunnah length of one fistful, one should not oil it to make it longer, as the sunnah is to trim the excess beyond a fistful. This is supported by a hadith from Ibn Umar who practiced trimming beyond the fist.

Key Terms
سرمہ (surma): Kohl, antimony powder applied to the eyes.
خضاب (khidhab): Dyeing, especially of hair or beard with henna.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is applying kohl during fasting permissible according to this passage?
A) Because it is a type of food.
B) Because it is a comfort and not prohibited.
C) Because it is only for women.
D) Because it nullifies the fast but is excused.

Key Takeaway
Kohl and oiling the mustache are permissible during fasting as comforts, provided they are not done for adornment.

intermediate

The Miswak Dispute: General vs Specific Hadith
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on afternoon miswak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on using miswak during fasting, identify the Shafi'i objection and its basis, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the principles of hadith criticism and qiyas.

Core Idea
The general hadith 'miswak is best for the fasting person' permits it anytime; a weak specific hadith cannot restrict it.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: may a fasting person use a wet miswak in the afternoon? The Hanafi school permits it without dislike, citing a general hadith from Ibn Majah. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering it makruh after midday based on a hadith from al-Tabarani and al-Dar Qutni, and an analogy with the blood of a martyr. We will unpack the proofs, the Hanafi critique, and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: it is permissible (mubah) without dislike for a fasting person to use wet or dry miswak at any time, morning or evening.
The source says 'no harm' and 'permissible without dislike'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its primary proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is makruh in the afternoon (evening). His proof: a hadith specifically prohibiting miswak in the evening, reported by al-Tabarani and al-Dar Qutni.
Also a secondary proof: qiyas on the blood of a martyr – just as martyr's blood is preserved, the fasting person's mouth odor (khuluf) should be preserved.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis argue that the Shafi'i hadith is weak (da'if) and contradicted by the general hadith. The qiyas on martyr's blood is invalid because the khuluf is an effect of worship (worthy of concealment), while martyr's blood is an effect of oppression (a sign of honor).
They also note the general hadith from Ibn Majah has no time restriction.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In practice: Hanafis can use miswak at any time during the fast; Shafi'is avoid it after noon. This affects daily practice, especially in social settings.
The difference leads to different fatwas in the same situation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is considered stronger and is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, as stated in Al-Hidayah.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani.

صبح و شام روزہ دار کے لئے تر اور خشک مسواک کرنا روزہ کو نہیں تو ڑتا
وَلَا بَأسَ بِالسّوَابِ الرَّطْبِ بِالْغَدَاةِ وَالْعَشِي لِلصَّائِمِ لِقَوْلِهِ * خَيرُ خِلَالِ الصَّائِمِ السّوَاكُ مِنْ غَيْر فصل وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى يَكْرَهُ بِالعَشِى لما فِيهِ مِنَ ازَالَةِ الأثَرِ الْمَحْمُودِ وَهُوَ الْخَوفٌ فَشَابَهَ دَمُ الشَّهِيدِ قُلْنَا هُوَ اثر العِبَادَةِ وَالْألْيَقُ بِهِ الْإِخْفَاء بِخَلافِ دَمِ الشَّهِيدِ لِأَنَّةَ أَثَرُ الظَّلْمِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الرَّحِبِ الْأَحْصَر وَبَيْنَ الْمُبْلُولِ بِالْمَاءِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ اور روزہ دار کے لئے صبح و شام تر مسواک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ روزہ دار کی بہترین خصلت مسواک ہے بغیر کسی تفصیل کے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ شام کے وقت مکروہہ کیونکہ اس وقت مسواک کرنے میں اثر محمود یعنی خلوف کا زائل کرنا ہے پس یہ شہد کے خون کے مشابہ ہے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ خلوف عبادت کا اثر ہے اور عبادت کے زیادہ مناسب چھپانا ہے برخلاف شہید کے خون کے یہ اس لئے کہ وہ ظلم کا اثر ہے اور اصلی تری اور پانی سے بھگونے کی ترمی کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک روزہ دار کے لئے گیلی اور پانی میں بھیگی ہوئی مسواک کرنا صبح کے وقت بھی اور شام کے وقت بھی بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک شام کے وقت روزہ دار کے لئے مسواک کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ امام شافعی کا مستدل وہ حدیث ہے جسکو طبرانی اور دار قطنی نے روایت کیا ہے نہ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسّلامُ قَالَ إِذَا صُنتُمْ فَاسْتَاكُوا بِالْغَدَاةِ وَلَا تَسْهَا كُوا بِالْعَشِيِّ فَإِنَّ الصَّائِمَ إِذَا يَبِسَتْ شَفَتَاهُ كَانَتْ لَهُ نُورًا يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ یعنی جب تم روز درکھو تو صبح کو مسواک کرو اور شام کے وقت مسواک نہ کرو کیونکہ جب روزہ دار کے ہونٹ خشک ہو جائیں گے تو قیامت کے دن اس کے لئے ایک نور ہوگا ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ روزہ دار کے منہ کی بو جسکو حدیث میں اللہ کے نزدیک مشک کی خوشبو سے بہتر کہا گیا ہے مسواک کرنے سے اس کا زائل کرنا لازم آتا ہے پس اس کو باقی رکھنے کے لئے شام کے وقت مسواک کرنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے اور یہ بوشہید کے خوان کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے پس جس طرح شہید کے خون کو زائل نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ بغیر نسل کے دفن کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح روزہ دار کے منہ کی بو کو بھی زائل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل ابن ماجہ کی حدیث خَيْرُ خِلَالِ الصَّائِمِ السّواک ہے یعنی روزہ دار کی بہترین خصلت مسواک کرنا ہے اس
Wet and dry miswak in the morning and evening does not break the fast for a fasting person. And there is no harm in the wet miswak in the morning and evening for the fasting person because of his statement: 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is miswak' without any qualification. And al-Shafi'i said: It is makruh in the evening because it removes the praiseworthy effect, which is the khuluf (mouth odor), so it resembles the blood of the martyr. We (Hanafis) say: This khuluf is an effect of worship, and it is more appropriate to conceal it, unlike the martyr's blood because that is an effect of oppression. And there is no difference between a fresh green stick and one moistened with water because of the hadith we narrated. Translation: And there is no harm in using wet miswak in the morning and evening for the fasting person because the Prophet (SAW) said: The best characteristic of a fasting person is miswak without any distinction. And Imam al-Shafi'i said it is makruh in the evening because it removes the praiseworthy effect, i.e., the khuluf, so it resembles the blood of the martyr. We (Hanafis) say: This khuluf is an effect of worship, and it is more appropriate to conceal it, unlike the martyr's blood because that is an effect of oppression. And there is no difference between a fresh green stick and one moistened with water because of the hadith we narrated. Explanation: The issue is that according to us (Hanafis), using wet or water-moistened miswak is permissible without dislike for a fasting person both in the morning and evening. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is makruh in the evening. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith reported by al-Tabarani and al-Dar Qutni: 'When you fast, use miswak in the morning and do not use miswak in the evening, for when the fasting person's lips dry, that will be a light for him on the Day of Judgment.' A second evidence is that the smell of the fasting person's mouth, which is said in hadith to be better to Allah than the scent of musk, is removed by miswak, so to preserve it, he is prohibited from using miswak in the evening. This smell resembles the blood of the martyr; just as the martyr's blood is not removed but is buried uncleaned, similarly the fasting person's mouth smell should not be removed. Our (Hanafi) evidence is the hadith of Ibn Majah: 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is miswak.' This text is cut off.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the use of miswak (toothstick) by a fasting person in the afternoon (evening). The Hanafi position, based on the general hadith 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is miswak,' is that it is permissible without dislike at any time, whether the miswak is fresh, dry, or moistened. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that miswak in the afternoon is makruh because it removes the praised odor (khuluf) that arises from the stomach of a fasting person, which is akin to the blood of a martyr that should not be washed off. The Hanafi response is that the khuluf is an effect of worship, and worship is best concealed, but that does not make miswak prohibited; rather, concealment is a separate recommendation. The text also clarifies that there is no difference between a fresh green miswak and one moistened with water. The Hanafi proof is the general hadith from Ibn Majah, while the Shafi'i proof is a specific hadith from Tabarani and Dar Qutni. The Hanafi critique is that the Shafi'i hadith is weak and contradictory to the general principle.

Key Terms
مسواک (miswak): A tooth-cleaning stick, usually from the arak tree.
خلوف (khuluf): The change in mouth odor of a fasting person due to emptiness of stomach.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on using a wet miswak in the afternoon for a fasting person?
A) It is makruh tanzih.
B) It is haram.
C) It is permissible without dislike.
D) It is mustahab only in the morning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits miswak at any time during fast based on a general, authentic hadith; the Shafi'i restriction is based on a weak hadith and a flawed analogy.

Ruling on Oiling the Beard for Growth While Fasting
Ruling on oiling beard for growth while fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fasting person oiling the beard with the intention of growing it, and explain the evidence and reconciliation of conflicting hadith.

Core Idea
A fasting person must not oil the beard for growth if it has reached the sunnah length of one fist.

The author of Hidayah presents a specific ruling regarding a fasting person applying oil to the beard with the intention of making it grow. This lesson unpacks the condition of beard length and the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the action of Ibn Umar, showing how the Hanafi school reconciles apparently conflicting hadith to derive this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Condition
Read the sentence: 'صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ داڑھی بڑھانے کے ارادے سے بھی تیل نہ لگائے بشرطیکہ داڑھی مقدار مسنون یعنی ایک مٹھی ہو'. The ruling is that one should not apply oil with the intention of beard growth, but only if the beard has already reached the sunnah measure of one fist.
The condition is crucial: the ruling applies only when the beard is at or beyond the sunnah length.
2
Understand the Sunnah Beard Length
The text cites a hadith from Tirmidhi that the Prophet (ﷺ) would trim the length and width of his beard, indicating that the sunnah is to keep it trimmed to about a fistful. The one-fist measure is derived from this practice.
The hadith is 'عَن رَّسُولِ اللهِ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَأْخُذُ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ مِنْ طُولِهَا وَعَرضها'.
3
Reconcile the Conflicting Hadith
The hadith 'أحفوا الشوارب وأعفوا اللحى' (Trim the moustaches and let the beards grow) seems to oppose trimming. The text resolves this by noting that Abdullah ibn Umar, the narrator, himself used to cut what exceeded a fist, proving that 'letting grow' means only up to a fist.
The action of Ibn Umar is decisive in clarification: he would hold his beard and cut anything below the grip.
4
Apply the Ruling to Intention
The prohibition is specifically linked to the intention of making the beard grow longer. If the intention is softening or maintenance, the ruling may differ. The text focuses on the growth intention as the trigger for prohibition.
This is an example of al-umur bi-maqasidiha – rulings depend on intention.
5
Conclude the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) for a fasting person to apply oil for beard growth when the beard has already reached the sunnah length. The evidence is drawn from prophetic practice and the interpretation of the 'let grow' hadith.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ داڑھی بڑھانے کے ارادے سے بھی تیل نہ لگائے بشرطیکہ اداڑھی مقدار مسنون یعنی ایک مٹھی ہو ایک مٹھی کے بقدر داڑھی کے مسنون ہونے پر وہ حدیث دلیل ہے جس کو امام ترندی نے جامع ترندی میں روایت کیا ہے عَن رَّسُولِ اللهِ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَأْخُذُ مِنَ اللَّحْيَةِ مِنْ طُولِهَا وَعَرضها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنی داڑھی کے طول اور عرض سے لیا کرتے تھے یعنی کاٹ کر کم کرتے تھے لیکن عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیث اس کے معارض ہے حدیث یہ ہے کہ احصوا الشوارب وَاعْفُوا اللحى عن مونچھیں موند و اور داڑھی بڑھاؤ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبداللہ بن عمر جو اس حدیث کے راوی ہیں ان کا خود عمل یہ تھا کہ ایک مٹھی سے زائد داڑھی کاٹ دیا کرتے تھے چنانچہ مروی ہے عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أنَّه كَانَ يَقْصُ عَلَى اللَّحْيَةِ ثُمَّ يَقُصُّ مَاتَحْتَ الْقُبَضَةِ
The author of Hidayah said: He should not apply oil with the intention of growing the beard, provided that his beard is of the sunnah measure, i.e., one fist. The evidence for the beard being sunnah to the extent of one fist is the hadith narrated by Imam Tirmidhi in Jami' Tirmidhi: from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he used to take from the length and width of his beard (i.e., he would trim it). But the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar opposes this: it is the hadith: 'Trim the moustaches and let the beards grow.' The response is that Abdullah ibn Umar, the narrator of this hadith, himself used to cut what exceeded a fist. It is narrated from ibn Umar that he would hold his beard and then cut whatever was below the grip.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on a fasting person applying oil to the beard with the intention of growing it. The author of Hidayah states that one should not apply oil for this purpose if the beard has already reached the sunnah length of one fist. The passage then reconciles conflicting hadith: the hadith of trimming the beard (from Tirmidhi) and the hadith of letting the beard grow (from ibn Umar). The commentary explains that ibn Umar himself, who narrated the 'let grow' hadith, practiced trimming what exceeded a fist, thereby clarifying that 'growing' means up to a fist. The ruling is for a fasting person: applying oil to a beard that is already at sunnah length with the intention of further growth is prohibited or discouraged? The text says 'not apply oil' (نہ لگائے) which indicates prohibition or makruh. We need to check if it's explicitly stated. The phrase seems to be a ruling from Hidayah. This lesson is a short ruling with evidence.

Key Terms
مقدار مسنون (miqdar masnun): The recommended amount, here specifically one fist length for the beard

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the sunnah length for a beard?
A) Elbow length
B) One fist
C) Shoulder length
D) As long as possible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits a fasting person from oiling the beard for growth if it already meets the sunnah length, as deduced from the Prophet's practice and the interpretation of conflicting hadith.

Ruling on Using Wet Siwak for a Fasting Person: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute with Shafi'i on siwak permissibility for fasting person at evening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using wet siwak for a fasting person in the evening and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument by analyzing the proofs.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits wet siwak anytime for a fasting person; the khaluf is concealable, unlike a martyr's blood.

This lesson examines a famous dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a fasting person may use a wet siwak in the evening. The core issue revolves around the status of the khaluf (fasting breath) – is it a praiseworthy effect to be preserved or an effect of worship to be concealed? We will walk through the proofs and responses.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that using a wet siwak in both morning and evening is permissible without dislike (jā'iz bilā karāhah). The ruling is based on clear hadith evidence.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers it disliked (makruh) in the evening because it removes the halitosis (khaluf) which he considers a praiseworthy effect of fasting.
The Shafi'i ruling is based on a hadith from Tabarani and Daraqutni.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites a hadith: 'When you fast, use siwak in the morning and do not use it in the evening…' and also uses qiyas (analogy) with the blood of a martyr, which is not washed away.
The martyr's blood is preserved as evidence of oppression; the khaluf is analogized to it.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with stronger hadith that do not restrict siwak to any time, such as 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is siwak' and the hadith about siwak at every prayer. They also argue that the khaluf is an effect of worship, which should be concealed, unlike the martyr's blood which is an effect of oppression.
Multiple authentic hadith outweigh the weak hadith cited by the Shafi'is.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis freely use siwak in the evening, while Shafi'is avoid it. This affects daily practice during Ramadan.
Each school's ruling is followed by its adherents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأسَ بِالسّوَابِ الرَّطْبِ بِالْغَدَاةِ وَالْعَشِي لِلصَّائِمِ لِقَوْلِهِ * خَيرُ خِلَالِ الصَّائِمِ السّوَاكُ مِنْ غَيْر فصل وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى يَكْرَهُ بِالعَشِى لما فِيهِ مِنَ ازَالَةِ الأثَرِ الْمَحْمُودِ وَهُوَ الْخَوفٌ فَشَابَهَ دَمُ الشَّهِيدِ قُلْنَا هُوَ اثر العِبَادَةِ وَالْألْيَقُ بِهِ الْإِخْفَاء بِخَلافِ دَمِ الشَّهِيدِ لِأَنَّةَ أَثَرُ الظَّلْمِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الرَّحِبِ الْأَحْصَر وَبَيْنَ الْمُبْلُولِ بِالْمَاءِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا

ترجمہ اور روزہ دار کے لئے صبح و شام تر مسواک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ روزہ دار کی بہترین خصلت مسواک ہے بغیر کسی تفصیل کے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ شام کے وقت مکروہہ کیونکہ اس وقت مسواک کرنے میں اثر محمود یعنی خلوف کا زائل کرنا ہے پس یہ شہد کے خون کے مشابہ ہے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ خلوف عبادت کا اثر ہے اور عبادت کے زیادہ مناسب چھپانا ہے برخلاف شہید کے خون کے یہ اس لئے کہ وہ ظلم کا اثر ہے اور اصلی تری اور پانی سے بھگونے کی ترمی کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک روزہ دار کے لئے گیلی اور پانی میں بھیگی ہوئی مسواک کرنا صبح کے وقت بھی اور شام کے وقت بھی بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک شام کے وقت روزہ دار کے لئے مسواک کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ امام شافعی کا مستدل وہ حدیث ہے جسکو طبرانی اور دار قطنی نے روایت کیا ہے نہ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسّلامُ قَالَ إِذَا صُنتُمْ فَاسْتَاكُوا بِالْغَدَاةِ وَلَا تَسْهَا كُوا بِالْعَشِيِّ فَإِنَّ الصَّائِمَ إِذَا يَبِسَتْ شَفَتَاهُ كَانَتْ لَهُ نُورًا يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ یعنی جب تم روز درکھو تو صبح کو مسواک کرو اور شام کے وقت مسواک نہ کرو کیونکہ جب روزہ دار کے ہونٹ خشک ہو جائیں گے تو قیامت کے دن اس کے لئے ایک نور ہوگا ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ روزہ دار کے منہ کی بو جسکو حدیث میں اللہ کے نزدیک مشک کی خوشبو سے بہتر کہا گیا ہے مسواک کرنے سے اس کا زائل کرنا لازم آتا ہے پس اس کو باقی رکھنے کے لئے شام کے وقت مسواک کرنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے اور یہ بوشہید کے خوان کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے پس جس طرح شہید کے خون کو زائل نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ بغیر نسل کے دفن کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح روزہ دار کے منہ کی بو کو بھی زائل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل ابن ماجہ کی حدیث خَيْرُ خِلَالِ الصَّائِمِ السّواک ہے یعنی روزہ دار کی بہترین خصلت مسواک کرنا ہے اس حدیث میں نہ صبح و شام کی کوئی تفصیل ہے اور نہ تر اور خشک کی کوئی تفصیل ہے اس لئے روزہ کی حالت میں ہر طرح کی مسواک کرنا اور ہر وقت کرنا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے لَوْلَا أَنْ أُسقَ عَلَى أُمَّتِي لَا مَرْتُهُمْ بِالسّوَابِ عِندَ كُلّ صَلوةِ یعنی اگر میں اپنی امت پر شاق اور گراں محسوس نہ کرتا تو ان کو ہر نماز کے وقت مسواک کرنے کا حکم کرتا یہ حدیث اگر چہ مسواک کے عدم وجوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے لیکن ہر نماز کے وقت مسواک کا مسنون ہونا بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے اور ہر نماز میں عموم ہے ظہر، عصر، مغرب سب کو شامل ہے اور وقت میں بھی عموم ہے یعنی روزے کے اوقات اور غیر روزے کے اوقات سب کو شامل ہے اس لئے اس حدیث سے رمضان کے زمانہ میں عصر اور مغرب کے وقت بھی مسواک کرنے کا حکم ثابت ہوگا پس ثابت ہوا کہ روزہ دار کے لئے شام شام کے وقت بھی مسواک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ۔ ہے۔
ای
قُلتُ
تیسری دلیل : مسند احمد کی یہ حدیث ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے صلوة بسوابٍ أَفْضَلُ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مِنْ سَعِينَ صلوة بِغَيْرِ سِواک، یعنی مسواک کر کے نماز پڑھنا اللہ کے نزدیک بغیر مسواک کے ستر نمازوں سے افضل ہے یہ حدیث روزہ دار کی نماز عصر پر بھی صادق آئے گی ، بشرطیکہ اس نے مسواک کر کے ادا کیا ہو اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ روزہ دار کے لئے شام کے وقت مسواک کرنا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ نیز ترندی اور ابو داؤد نے روایت کی ہے۔ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بنِ عَامِرِ بْنِ رَبِيعَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَسْتَاكُ وَهُوَ صَائِمٌ مَالَا اَعُدُّهُ وَلَا أَحْصی یعنی عبداللہ اپنے والد عامر بن ربیعہ ۔ سے روایت کرتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو بحالت روز ہ بے شمار مرتبہ مسواک کرتے ہوئے دیکھا ہے۔ ہمارا مستدل یہ حدیث بھی ہے عَنْ عَبدِ الرَّحْمنِ بن غَنَمٍ قَالَ سَأَلْتُ مُعَاذَ بن جَبَل أاُسوك وَأنَا صَائِمُ قَالَ نَعَمُ قُله أَى النَّهَارِ أَتَسَوَّى قَالَ أَى النَّهَارِ شِئْتَ عَدُوَةَ وَعَشِيَّةٌ قُلتُ إِنَّ النَّاسَ يَكْرَهُونَهُ عَشِيَةً وَيَقُولُونَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ قَالَ لَحَلُوفُ فَمِ الصَّائِمِ أَطْيَبُ عِندَ اللهِ مِنْ رِيحِ الْمِسْكِ فَقَالَ سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ لَقَدْ أَمَرَ هُم بِالسّوَاتِ وَ هُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّيفِى الصَّائِمِ لَخَلُوفَ وَإِنِ اسْتَاكَ وَمَا كَانَ بِالَّذِي يَأْمُرُهُمْ أَن يَنْسَنُوا أَفْوَاهُم عَمَداً مَافِي ذَالِكَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ شَيْ بَلْ فِيهِ شَرٌّ إِلَّا مَنْ أبلى بلاء لا يَجِدُ مِنْهُ بُدا عبد الرحمن بن غنم فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضرت معاذ بن جبل سے دریافت کیا کہ کیا میں بحالت صوم مسواک کر لیا کروں معاذ نے کہا کہ ہاں میں نے کہا کہ دن میں کس وقت مسواک کروں فرمایا کہ جس وقت تیرا جی چاہے صبح کو اور شام کو میں نے کہا کہ لوگ تو زوال کے بعد مکروہ قرار دیتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ روز بہ دار کے منہ کی بو اللہ کے نزدیک مشک کی خوشبو سے بہتر ہے فرمایا کہ سبحان اللہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لوگوں کو مسواک کرنیکا حکم دیا ہے حالانکہ بہ آپ کو معلوم تھا کہ صائم کے منہ میں خلوف ضروری ہے اگر چہ مسواک کرے اور حضور پر ایسے نہ تھے کہ لوگوں کو حکم فرماتے کہ عمدا اپنے منہ کے بدبودار کریں۔ اس میں تو کچھ بہتری نہیں ہے بلکہ برتری ہے سوائے اس کے جو کسی بلا میں مبتلا ہوکر چارہ نہ پائے۔ اس تفصیلی واقعہ سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ روزے کی حالت میں صبح وشام مسواک کرنا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔
امام شافعی کی معقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ خلوف عبادت کا اثر ہے اور عبادات میں اختفا ، اولی ہے تا کہ ریا کاری کا شبہ نہ ہو اور اختفاء اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مسواک کے ذریعہ اس بو کو ختم کر دیا جائے برخلاف شہید کے خون کے کہ وہ ظلم کا اثر ہے اپنے مقابل سے انصاف کا خواستگار ہے اس لئے اس کا باقی رکھنا ضروری ہے اس موقع پر علامہ ابن الہمام نے بہت اچھی بات کہی ہے کہ خلوف سے مراد وہ بھاپ
And there is no harm in using a wet siwak in the morning and evening for the fasting person, due to his statement: 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is siwak' without any distinction. And al-Shafi'i said: It is disliked in the evening because it removes the praiseworthy effect, which is the halitosis (khaluf), so it resembles the blood of the martyr. We say: This halitosis is an effect of worship, and concealment is more befitting for worship, contrary to the martyr's blood because it is an effect of oppression. And there is no difference between a naturally wet stick and one moistened with water, because of what we have narrated. Translation: And there is no harm in using a wet siwak in the morning and evening for the fasting person... [rest of Urdu] ... and at the end: The response to al-Shafi'i's rational proof is that halitosis is an effect of worship, and concealment is better... and Ibn al-Humam said that khaluf means that steam.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the permissibility of using a wet siwak (toothstick) for a fasting person in the evening. The Hanafi position, based on the matn of Hidayah, is that it is permissible without any aversion in both morning and evening. Imam Shafi'i considered it disliked in the evening because it removes the halitosis (khaluf) which is a praiseworthy effect of fasting, analogous to the blood of a martyr which should not be washed. The Hanafi response is that the khaluf is an effect of worship, and worship should be concealed, unlike the martyr's blood which is an effect of oppression and should be evident. The passage then provides multiple hadith proofs: (1) The general hadith 'The best characteristic of a fasting person is siwak' without time restriction; (2) The hadith 'If I did not fear burdening my Ummah, I would order them to use siwak at every prayer' implying permissibility at all prayer times including evening; (3) The hadith that prayer with siwak is better than seventy prayers without; (4) The narration of 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah seeing the Prophet using siwak countless times while fasting; (5) The narration of Mu'adh ibn Jabal who permitted siwak at any time of the day. The passage also refutes the Shafi'i hadith from Tabarani and Daraqutni that prohibits evening siwak, and provides a rational argument about concealment of worship. Finally, it mentions a saying of Ibn al-Humam clarifying the meaning of khaluf (the steam).

Key Terms
خلوف (khaluf): The bad breath that comes from a fasting person's mouth due to an empty stomach.
سواک (siwāk): A tooth-stick used for cleaning teeth; here specifically the wet or moistened one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using a wet siwak for a fasting person in the evening?
A) Permissible (jā'iz) without dislike
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahab)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a fasting person to use wet siwak at any time, as the khaluf is an effect of worship best concealed.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
7 min
Permissibility of Miswak for the Fasting Person at Any Time
Proving the permissibility of miswak for the fasting person at all times with multiple hadith and responding to Shafi'i objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on miswak for a fasting person and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by analyzing the hadith proofs and the concept of khuluf.

Core Idea
Miswak is permissible for the fasting person at any time; the khuluf remains untouched.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends the permissibility of miswak at all times for the fasting person, countering the Shafi'i objection that it is disliked after noon because it removes the praised breath. By examining multiple hadith and the rational distinction between stomach vapor (khuluf) and dental decay, you will see why the Hanafi position is relied upon. The key is that the khuluf, which is the desirable effect of fasting, is not removed by miswak—only the undesirable yellowness of teeth is removed.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
What does the Hanafi school rule regarding miswak for a fasting person? It is permissible (ja'iz) and sunnah at all times, including the evening.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
Which school objects and on what grounds? Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is disliked (makruh) after noon because it removes the khuluf (bad breath) which is praised by Allah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proofs (Dalil)
What hadith and arguments does the Hanafi school present? The primary proof is the hadith: 'Were it not that I would burden my nation, I would have commanded them to use miswak at every prayer.' This includes all prayer times, even during fasting. Also direct observation of the Prophet and the fatwa of Mu'adh ibn Jabal.
These are ahadith with zanni thubut but strong dalala.
4
Analyze the Opponent’s Proof
What is the Shafi'i evidence? They cite the hadith: 'The breath of the fasting person is more fragrant to Allah than musk.' They argue that removing this fragrance by miswak is disliked.
This hadith is also used by Hanafis, but they interpret it differently.
5
Understand the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
How does the Hanafi school reconcile the two hadith? They distinguish between khuluf (stomach vapor) and dental decay. Khuluf is not removed by miswak; only the yellowness of teeth is removed. Thus there is no conflict. Concealing the odor is better to avoid showing off, unlike the blood of a martyr.
This is the decisive point: the desired khuluf remains.

يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّيفِى الصَّائِمِ لَخَلُوفَ وَإِنِ اسْتَاكَ وَمَا كَانَ بِالَّذِي يَأْمُرُهُمْ أَن يَنْسَنُوا أَفْوَاهُم عَمَداً مَافِي ذَالِكَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ شَيْ بَلْ فِيهِ شَرٌّ إِلَّا مَنْ أبلى بلاء لا يَجِدُ مِنْهُ بُدا عبد الرحمن بن غنم فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضرت معاذ بن جبل سے دریافت کیا کہ کیا میں بحالت صوم مسواک کر لیا کروں معاذ نے کہا کہ ہاں میں نے کہا کہ دن میں کس وقت مسواک کروں فرمایا کہ جس وقت تیرا جی چاہے صبح کو اور شام کو میں نے کہا کہ لوگ تو زوال کے بعد مکروہ قرار دیتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ روز بہ دار کے منہ کی بو اللہ کے نزدیک مشک کی خوشبو سے بہتر ہے فرمایا کہ سبحان اللہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لوگوں کو مسواک کرنیکا حکم دیا ہے حالانکہ بہ آپ کو معلوم تھا کہ صائم کے منہ میں خلوف ضروری ہے اگر چہ مسواک کرے اور حضور پر ایسے نہ تھے کہ لوگوں کو حکم فرماتے کہ عمدا اپنے منہ کے بدبودار کریں۔ اس میں تو کچھ بہتری نہیں ہے بلکہ برتری ہے سوائے اس کے جو کسی بلا میں مبتلا ہوکر چارہ نہ پائے۔ اس تفصیلی واقعہ سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ روزے کی حالت میں صبح وشام مسواک کرنا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔
امام شافعی کی معقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ خلوف عبادت کا اثر ہے اور عبادات میں اختفا ، اولی ہے تا کہ ریا کاری کا شبہ نہ ہو اور اختفاء اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مسواک کے ذریعہ اس بو کو ختم کر دیا جائے برخلاف شہید کے خون کے کہ وہ ظلم کا اثر ہے اپنے مقابل سے انصاف کا خواستگار ہے اس لئے اس کا باقی رکھنا ضروری ہے اس موقع پر علامہ ابن الہمام نے بہت اچھی بات کہی ہے کہ خلوف سے مراد وہ بھاپ ہے جو معدہ کے خالی ہونے کی وجہ سے نکلتی ہے مسواک کرنے سے اس کا ازالہ نہیں ہو سکتا مسواک سے تو دانتوں کا میلا پن دور کیا جاتا ہے لہذا شام کے وقت بھی اگر مسواک کی جائے گی تو اس سے خلوف یعنی معدہ کی بھاپ جو عند اللہ مطلوب ۔ سے وہ زائل نہ ہوگی بلکہ دانتوں کا پیلا پن جو غیر مطلوب ہے وہ زائل ہو جائے گا۔ جمیل عفی عنہ۔
In the hadith there is no detail of morning and evening, nor detail of wet and dry. Therefore, during fasting, every kind of miswak and at any time is permissible. The second proof: The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Were it not that I would burden my nation, I would have commanded them to use miswak at every prayer.' This hadith indicates the non-obligation of miswak, but it also establishes that miswak at every prayer time is sunnah. 'Every prayer' is general, including Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, etc., and 'time' is also general, including fasting times and non-fasting times. So this hadith establishes the command to use miswak even at Asr and Maghrib during Ramadan. Thus it is proven that there is no harm for the fasting person in using miswak in the evening.
I said: Third proof: Musnad Ahmad has the hadith: 'Prayer with miswak is seventy times better in the sight of Allah than prayer without miswak.' This applies to the fasting person's Asr prayer if performed with miswak. This shows that using miswak in the evening is permissible without dislike. Also al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah from his father: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ using miswak while fasting — countless times.' Our evidence also includes: from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ghanm: 'I asked Mu'adh ibn Jabal: May I use miswak while fasting? He said: Yes. I asked: At what part of the day? He said: Any part you wish — morning and evening. I said: People dislike it in the evening and say that the Prophet ﷺ said: The breath of the fasting person is more fragrant to Allah than musk. He said: Subhanallah! He commanded them to use miswak while knowing that the fasting person will inevitably have bad breath even if he uses miswak. He would not command them to intentionally make their mouths foul. There is no good in that; rather it is evil, except for one who is afflicted and has no escape.' This detailed incident also shows that using miswak morning and evening while fasting is permissible without dislike.
The answer to Imam al-Shafi'i's rational argument: The bad breath (khuluf) is a result of worship, and concealment in worship is preferable to avoid suspicion of showing off. Concealment only happens when this odor is removed by miswak. This is unlike the blood of a martyr, which is the result of oppression and demands justice from the opponent, so its preservation is necessary. Here Allamah Ibn al-Humam said a very good thing: By khuluf is meant the vapor that comes out due to emptiness of the stomach. Miswak cannot remove that. Miswak only removes the yellowness of teeth. Therefore, even if miswak is used in the evening, the khuluf (stomach vapor) which is desired by Allah will not be removed, while the yellowness of teeth which is undesirable will be removed. May Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of miswak for a fasting person at any time, especially in the evening. The author presents multiple proofs: First, a general hadith about miswak at every prayer implies it is sunnah even during fasting times. Second, a hadith from Musnad Ahmad stating the superiority of prayer with miswak, which applies to Asr prayer. Third, direct observation of the Prophet ﷺ using miswak while fasting. Fourth, the incident with Mu'adh ibn Jabal showing explicit permission. The author then addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's rational argument that the bad breath of the fasting person is beloved to Allah, so removing it is disliked. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the bad breath (khuluf) which is from the stomach and not removed by miswak, and the decay of teeth which is removed. Thus miswak is permissible and recommended. The authority weight is from hadith and the Hanafi reliance on general proofs. The mufta bihi position is that miswak is permissible at all times.

Key Terms
خلوف (khuluf): The bad breath (vapor) that emanates from the stomach of a fasting person due to emptiness.
مسواك (miswak): A tooth-cleaning stick from the arak tree, used for oral hygiene and as a sunnah act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is miswak permissible for a fasting person in the evening, despite the hadith praising the fasting person's breath?
A) The hadith about breath is weak and not reliable.
B) Miswak removes only dental decay, not the stomach vapor which is the 'khuluf' praised by Allah.
C) The Prophet himself disliked miswak in the evening, but it is allowed out of necessity.
D) The hadith applies only to non-fasting days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits miswak for the fasting person at any time because miswak removes only dental decay, not the stomach vapor (khuluf) which is the praised fragrance.

Illness and Breaking the Fast: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on breaking fast due to illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on breaking the fast due to illness and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i position, using the Quranic verse as proof.

Core Idea
Fearing increased illness suffices to break the fast; the Quran’s general permission for the sick is not restricted to mortal danger.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on when a sick person may break the fast in Ramadan. The Hanafi school adopts a broader concession based on the general Quranic verse, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to cases of life or limb. We will explore the evidence and the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What precise condition permits a sick person to break the fast? The Hanafi school says fear of increased illness or prolonged recovery; the Shafi'i school requires fear of death or loss of a limb.
This is the core ikhtilaf.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
The Hanafi school relies on the general imperative in Quran 2:184, which gives permission to any sick person to break the fast. The term 'marid' (ill) is general ('amm) and binding.
Hanafi usul holds that 'amm is qat'i until takhsis.
3
Present the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas with tayammum: just as tayammum is only allowed when water poses a risk of death or limb loss, breaking the fast should also be restricted to such extreme cases.
The Shafi'i analogy connects two dispensations (rukhsas).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the qiyas
The Hanafi response is that increased illness and prolonged recovery can lead to death, so they are included in the same rationale. Moreover, the Quranic text is general and should not be restricted without a clear proof.
Hanafi school uses al-amm yufidu al-wujub and rejects the qiyas because the illa is not identical.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a person with a mild but worsening illness may break the fast in the Hanafi school, while the Shafi'i school requires him to fast unless death is feared.
Affects many believers during Ramadan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: وَمَنْ كَانَ مَرِيضًا فِي رَمَضَانَ فَخَافَ إِنْ صَامَ إِزْدَادَ مَرَضُهُ أفْطَرَ وَ قَضَى وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُى لا يُفْطِرُ هُوَ يَعْتبر خَوفَ الْهَلَاكِ أَوْ فَوَاتِ الْعُضْوِ كَمَا يُعْتَبِرُ فِى التَّيْمِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ زِيَادَةُ الْمَرَضِ وَ اِمْتِدَادُهُ قَدْ تُفْضِي إِلَى الهَلَاكِ فَيَجِبُ الاِحْتِرَازُ عَنْهُ
ترجمه فصل اور جو شخص رمضان میں بیمار ہو پھر خوف کیا کہ اگر روزہ رکھا تو اس کا مرض بڑھ جائی گا تو وہ افطار کرے اور قضا کرے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فطار نہ کرے۔ امام شافعی ہلاکت کے خوف یا عضوفوت ہونے کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں جیسا کہ تمیم میں اعتبار کرتے ہیں
اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مرض کی زیادتی اور اس کا طویل ہونا بھی بھی ہلاکت تک پہنچا دیتا ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی احتر از واجب ہے۔ تشریح اب تک روزہ کے مسائل کا ذکر تھا اس فصل میں ان اعذار کو بیان کریں گے جن کی وجہ سے روزہ نہ رکھنا مباح اور جائز ہے بقول علامہ ابن الہام کی جن اعذار سے افطار مباح ہوتا ہے وہ سات ہیں، (۱) مرض ، (۲) سفر ، (۳) حمل جبکہ روزہ عورت یا حمل کے لئے ضرر رساں ہو ، (۴) رضاعت ( دودھ پلانا ) جبکہ روزہ بچہ کے لئے ضرر رساں ہو ، (۵) بڑھاپا جبکہ وہ روزہ رکھنے پر قادر نہ ہو، (1) سخت پیاس ، (۷) سخت بھوک ، جبکہ روزے کی وجہ سے جان جانے یا نقصان عقل کا خوف ہو۔ سب سے پہلا عذر بیماری ہے لیکن رخصت افطار نفس بیماری کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مرض کی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔ ایک وہ جس میں روزہ اضافہ کرتا ہے، دوم وہ جس میں روزہ تخفیف کرتا ہے پس جس بیماری میں روزہ کی وجہ سے تخفیف ہوتی ہے یعنی روزہ اس بیماری میں فائدہ مند ہوتا ہے تو اس بیماری کے ساتھ رخصت افطار متعلق نہیں ہوتی اور روزہ کی وجہ سے جو بیماری بڑھ جاتی ہے یا روزہ کی وجہ سے بیماری طویل ہو جاتی ہے تو اس بیماری کے ساتھ رخصت افطار متعلق ہوتی ہے ماتن نے اسی کو بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص رمضان مبارک میں بیمار ہوا اور اس کو اندیشہ دامنگیر ہوا کہ روز ہ اگر رکھا تو بیماری بڑھ جائے گی تو ایسی صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک افطار کرنا جائز ہے اور صحت ہونے پر اس کی قضا کر لے حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ایسا بیار روز و نہ چھوڑے بلکہ روزہ رکھنا ضروری ہے ہاں اگر روزہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہونے کا خوف ہو یا کسی عضو کے زائل ہونے کا خوف ہو تو افطار کی اجازت ہے جس طرح کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک پانی کے موجود رہتے ہوئے اس مریض کے لئے تیم کی اجازت ہے جس کو پانی استعمال کرنے کی صورت میں جان جانے یا کسی عضو کے زائل ہونے کا اندیشہ ہوا گر یہ اندیشہ نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک تیم کی اجازت نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَّرِيضًا أَوْعَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ ايام اخر (البقرة: ۱۸۴)ہے اس کی ہر مریض کے لئے افطار کی اباحت معلوم ہوتی ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ افطار کی مشروعیت حرج دور
Section: Whoever is sick in Ramadan and fears that if he fasts his illness will increase, he breaks his fast and makes it up. Al-Shafi'i said: He does not break his fast; he only considers fear of death or loss of a limb, just as is considered in tayammum. We say: Increase of illness and its prolongation may lead to death, so it is necessary to avoid it.
Translation of the section: And whoever is sick in Ramadan and fears that if he fasts his illness will increase, then he breaks his fast and makes it up. Imam Shafi'i said: He should not break his fast. Imam Shafi'i considers fear of death or loss of a limb, just as he considers in tayammum. And we say that increase of illness and its prolongation also lead to death, so it is necessary to avoid it.
Explanation: So far the issues of fasting were mentioned. In this section, we will explain the excuses due to which not fasting is permissible and allowed. According to Allamah Ibn al-Humam, the excuses that make breaking the fast permissible are seven: (1) illness, (2) travel, (3) pregnancy when fasting harms the woman or the fetus, (4) breastfeeding when fasting harms the child, (5) old age when one is unable to fast, (6) severe thirst, (7) severe hunger, when there is fear of death or loss of intellect due to fasting. The first excuse is illness, but the concession to break the fast is not connected to the mere presence of illness; rather illness has two types: one in which fasting increases the illness, and the other in which fasting decreases it. So in the illness where fasting causes a decrease (i.e., fasting is beneficial), the concession to break is not connected; and in the illness which increases because of fasting or becomes prolonged because of fasting, the concession to break is connected. The author (al-matin) has stated this: If someone becomes sick in the blessed month of Ramadan and fears that if he fasts his illness will increase, then in such a case, according to us, breaking the fast is permissible, and he should make it up after recovery. Imam Shafi'i said that such a sick person should not leave the fast; rather fasting is obligatory for him. Yes, if there is fear of death due to fasting or fear of loss of a limb, then breaking is allowed, just as according to Imam Shafi'i, when water is present, tayammum is allowed for a sick person who fears death or loss of limb from using water. If there is no such fear, then tayammum is not allowed in his view. Our proof is the statement of Allah Almighty: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:184). This indicates the permission to break for any sick person. But since it is agreed that the legislation of breaking is to remove hardship...
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on breaking the fast due to illness. The Hanafi position: if a sick person fears that fasting will increase his illness or prolong recovery, he may break his fast and make it up later. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts this to fear of death or loss of a limb only. The author then explains the broader categories of excuses that permit breaking the fast, listing seven, and details that the concession is not for all illnesses but only those worsened by fasting. The Hanafi proof is the general Quranic verse (2:184) which gives permission to any sick person, not only those in mortal danger. The authority weight is from the Quran and the Hanafi principle of removing hardship. The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi view that fear of increased illness is sufficient grounds to break the fast.

Key Terms
مرض (marad): Illness; the text distinguishes between illness that worsens with fasting (permitting break) and illness that improves (not permitting break).
رخصت افطار (rukhsat al-iftaar): The concession to break the fast; associated with illness only when fasting increases the illness or prolongs it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum threshold for a sick person to be allowed to break his fast in Ramadan?
A) Fear of death only.
B) Fear of loss of a limb only.
C) Fear that fasting will increase the illness or prolong recovery.
D) Any illness regardless of severity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits breaking the fast for any illness that is worsened by fasting, based on the general Quranic verse, while the Shafi'i school requires fear of death or limb loss.

Sawm — Fasting

8 min
Sick Person Fasting: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on the Degree of Hardship
Presents Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i objection on breaking fast due to illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on when a sick person may break his fast, explain the proof for each, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Increase of illness, not just death, justifies breaking the fast in the Hanafi school.

In this lesson, we examine a classical inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the fasting of a sick person who fears that fasting will worsen his condition. The Hanafi school adopts a broader view of permissible hardship, while the Shafi'i school restricts the concession to cases of imminent death or loss of a limb. Understanding this difference is crucial for applying the correct ruling in contemporary medical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a sick person who fears increase of illness may break his fast and make it up later. Note that the concession applies only when fasting aggravates the illness or delays recovery, not when fasting is beneficial.
The text lists seven excuses; illness is the first, but its application depends on the type of illness.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such a person must fast unless there is fear of death or loss of a limb. He analogizes to the conditions for tayammum.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i uses qiyas: just as tayammum is permitted only when water causes death or loss of limb, breaking the fast is permitted only when fasting causes death or loss of limb.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the Quranic permission (2:184) is general for the sick. Increase or prolongation of illness can itself lead to death, so avoiding it is obligatory. The analogy to tayammum is flawed because the basis for tayammum is absence of water, not hardship from the act itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, many more sick individuals are allowed to break fast; under Shafi'i, only those near death may do so. This has practical implications for modern patients (e.g., diabetics, chronic conditions).

Source Text

فصل: وَمَنْ كَانَ مَرِيضًا فِي رَمَضَانَ فَخَافَ إِنْ صَامَ إِزْدَادَ مَرَضُهُ أفْطَرَ وَ قَضَى وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُى لا يُفْطِرُ هُوَ يَعْتبر خَوفَ الْهَلَاكِ أَوْ فَوَاتِ الْعُضْوِ كَمَا يُعْتَبِرُ فِى التَّيْمِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ زِيَادَةُ الْمَرْضِ وَ اِمْتِدَادُهُ قَدْ تُفْضِي إِلَى الهَلَاكِ فَيَجِبُ الاِحْتِرَازُ عَنْهُ
ترجمه فصل اور جو شخص رمضان میں بیمار ہو پھر خوف کیا کہ اگر روزہ رکھا تو اس کا مرض بڑھ جائی گا تو وہ افطار کرے اور قضا کرے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فطار نہ کرے۔ امام شافعی ہلاکت کے خوف یا عضوفوت ہونے کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں جیسا کہ تمیم میں اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مرض کی زیادتی اور اس کا طویل ہونا بھی بھی ہلاکت تک پہنچا دیتا ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی احتر از واجب ہے۔

روزے کی وجہ سے جان جانے یا نقصان عقل کا خوف ہو۔ سب سے پہلا عذر بیماری ہے لیکن رخصت افطار نفس بیماری کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مرض کی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔ ایک وہ جس میں روزہ اضافہ کرتا ہے، دوم وہ جس میں روزہ تخفیف کرتا ہے پس جس بیماری میں روزہ کی وجہ سے تخفیف ہوتی ہے یعنی روزہ اس بیماری میں فائدہ مند ہوتا ہے تو اس بیماری کے ساتھ رخصت افطار متعلق نہیں ہوتی اور روزہ کی وجہ سے جو بیماری بڑھ جاتی ہے یا روزہ کی وجہ سے بیماری طویل ہو جاتی ہے تو اس بیماری کے ساتھ رخصت افطار متعلق ہوتی ہے ماتن نے اسی کو بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص رمضان مبارک میں بیمار ہوا اور اس کو اندیشہ دامنگیر ہوا کہ روز ہ اگر رکھا تو بیماری بڑھ جائے گی تو ایسی صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک افطار کرنا جائز ہے اور صحت ہونے پر اس کی قضا کر لے حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ایسا بیار روز و نہ چھوڑے بلکہ روزہ رکھنا ضروری ہے ہاں اگر روزہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہونے کا خوف ہو یا کسی عضو کے زائل ہونے کا خوف ہو تو افطار کی اجازت ہے جس طرح کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک پانی کے موجود رہتے ہوئے اس مریض کے لئے تیم کی اجازت ہے جس کو پانی استعمال کرنے کی صورت میں جان جانے یا کسی عضو کے زائل ہونے کا اندیشہ ہوا گر یہ اندیشہ نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک تیم کی اجازت نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَّرِيضًا أَوْعَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ ايام اخر (البقرة: ۱۸۴)ہے اس کی ہر مریض کے لئے افطار کی اباحت معلوم ہوتی ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ افطار کی مشروعیت حرج دور کرنے کے لئے ہے اور حرج کا تحقق متعلق ہے ازدیاد مرض یا شفایابی کی تاخیر کے ساتھ اس لئے افطار کی اجازت انہی صورتوں میں ہوگی اور امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کبھی کبھی مرض کی زیادتی اور اس کا طول آدمی کی ہلاکت کا سبب بن جاتا ہے اس لئے ازدیاد مرض اور امتداد مرض سے احتراز کرنا بھی ضروری ہے
Section: And whoever is sick in Ramadan and fears that if he fasts his illness will increase, he may break the fast and make it up later. Al-Shafi'ī said: He should not break the fast. He (al-Shafi'ī) considers fear of death or loss of a limb, as he considers in tayammum. And we say: Increase of illness and its prolongation may lead to death, so it is obligatory to avoid it. Translation: Section: And a person who is sick in Ramadan and feared that if he fasts his illness will increase, he should break the fast and make it up. Imam Al-Shafi'ī said: He should not break the fast. Imam Al-Shafi'ī considers fear of death or loss of a limb, like he considers in tayammum. And we say: The increase of illness and its prolongation also leads to death, so it is obligatory to avoid it. Commentary: Until now the topics of fasting were mentioned; in this section we will mention the excuses due to which not fasting is permissible and allowed. According to 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam, the excuses that make breaking the fast permissible are seven: (1) Illness, (2) Travel, (3) Pregnancy when fasting harms the woman or the fetus, (4) Breastfeeding when fasting harms the child, (5) Old age when one is unable to fast, (6) Severe thirst, (7) Severe hunger when there is fear of death or loss of intellect. The first excuse is illness, but the concession of breaking fast is not attached to the illness itself; rather there are two kinds of illness. One in which fasting increases it, and the other in which fasting decreases it. So the illness in which fasting decreases it (i.e., fasting is beneficial) is not attached to the concession of breaking fast. And the illness that increases due to fasting, or fasting prolongs the illness, is attached to the concession of breaking fast. The author (al-Quduri) stated this. Thus he said: If a person becomes ill in the blessed month of Ramadan and fears that if he fasts his illness will increase, then in such a case, according to us, it is permissible to break the fast, and upon recovery he must make it up. Hadrat Imam al-Shafi'ī said: Such a sick person should not leave the fast; rather fasting is necessary. Yes, if due to fasting there is fear of death or loss of a limb, then breaking is allowed, just as according to Imam al-Shafi'ī, when water is available, it is allowed for a sick person to perform tayammum if using water causes fear of death or loss of a limb. If that fear is not present, then tayammum is not allowed according to him. Our proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So whoever among you is sick or on a journey, then an equal number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:184). From this the permissibility of breaking fast for every sick person is understood. But because it is agreed that the legislation of breaking fast is to remove hardship, and the realization of hardship is connected to increase of illness or delay of recovery, therefore breaking is allowed only in these cases. The response to Imam al-Shafi'ī's proof is that sometimes the increase of illness and its prolongation become a cause of death, so it is also necessary to avoid increase and prolongation of illness.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a sick person who fears that fasting will increase his illness. The Hanafi ruling is clear: such a person may break his fast and must make it up later. This is based on the general permission in the Quran (2:184) for the sick and traveler to defer fasting. However, the Hanafis qualify this general permission by noting that the concession is specifically for when fasting causes hardship (haraj). Thus, if the illness is such that fasting is beneficial (e.g., in some diseases like cholera where fasting is therapeutic), breaking the fast is not allowed. The key is whether fasting causes an increase in illness or delay in recovery. The author lists seven excuses in total that permit breaking the fast, with illness being the first. Then he presents Imam al-Shafi'i's stricter view, which only permits breaking if there is fear of death or loss of a limb, analogizing to tayammum conditions. The Hanafi response is that increase or prolongation of illness can itself lead to death, so it is obligatory to avoid that harm. The commentary also notes the list of seven excuses from Ibn al-Humam, giving a broader framework for concessions in fasting.

Key Terms
مرض (marad): Illness, specifically one that may increase or be prolonged by fasting.
خوف (khawf): Fear, a reasonable expectation based on experience or doctor's advice.
حرج (haraj): Hardship, difficulty, which the concession of breaking fast aims to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition makes it permissible for a sick person to break his fast?
A) The illness is contagious.
B) Fasting would increase the illness or delay recovery.
C) The person is unable to find a doctor.
D) The illness lasts the entire month of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sick person may break his fast if fasting would increase his illness or delay recovery, based on the Quranic concession for the sick.
