Fasting for a Traveler: Azimat vs Rukhsah in Hanafi and Shafi'i Schools
Ruling on whether fasting is better for a traveler when not harmed by it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that fasting is better (afdal) for a traveler who can fast without hardship, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith and its interpretation.

Core Idea
For a traveler without hardship, fasting is azimat (preferred) but not mandatory; Shafi'i considers breaking better.

In this lesson, we examine a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the optimal choice for a traveler in Ramadan who can fast without hardship. The Hanafi position balances the virtue of Ramadan with the concession of travel, ruling that fasting is superior. The Shafi'i school, relying on a Prophetic hadith, gives precedence to the concession. Understanding the reasoning behind each view sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting dalils.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: for a traveler who does not suffer hardship, fasting is afdal (better) but breaking is permissible (ja'iz). This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
Note that 'afdal' is a preference, not an obligation.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that breaking is better, citing the hadith: 'ليس من البر الصيام في السفر' (There is no righteousness in fasting while traveling). Understand the apparent meaning of the hadith.
Also look at other narrations where the Prophet called fasting travelers 'disobedient'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as applying to cases of severe hardship. They argue that since travel inherently involves some difficulty (mashaqqah), the hadith is restricted to hardship situations. Their positive proof is that Ramadan is the best time for fasting, so performing it during Ramadan is more virtuous.
Note the principle: azimat is preferred when possible, and rukhsah is a concession for genuine need.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Both schools allow breaking; the difference is in recommendation (afdal). Hanafi advises fasting; Shafi'i advises breaking. For a Hanafi mufti, the fatwa is that fasting is better.
The student must know which position to follow in practice.
5
Examine the critique of the transmission
The commentary notes a potential error: al-Marghinani's transmission of the Shafi'i view may be inaccurate. According to actual Shafi'i sources, if no hardship, fasting is better. This shows the importance of verifying riwayah.
This step is advanced; it highlights that not all ikhtilaf reported in fiqh books is historically accurate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسَافِرًا لَا يَسْتَضِرُّ بِالصَّوْمِ فَصَوْمُهُ أَفْضَلُّ وَإِنْ أفْطَرَ جَازَ لأنَّ السَّفَرَ لَا يَعْرَى عَن المُشَقَّةِ وَجَعَلَ نَفْسَهُ عُذرًا بِخِلافِ الْمَرَضِ فَإِنَّهُ قَدْ يَخِتُ بِالصَّوْمِ فَشَرَطَ كَوْنُهُ مُفْضِيَّا إِلَى الحَرَج وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الْفِطْرُ أَفْضَلُ لِقَوْلِهِ لَيْسَ مِنَ الْبِرِّ الصَّيَامُ فِى السَّفَرِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ رَمَضَانَ أفضلُ الْوَقْتين فَكَانَ الأدَاء فِيهِ أَوْلَى وَمَارَوَاهُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى حَالَةِ الْجُهْدِ
And if he is a traveler who does not experience hardship from fasting, then his fasting is better, and if he breaks it is permissible. Because travel is not free from hardship, and travel itself is made an excuse, unlike illness, for it may be beneficial with fasting, so it is conditioned that it leads to difficulty. And al-Shafi'i said: Breaking is better, due to his (the Prophet's) statement: 'There is no righteousness in fasting while traveling.' And our proof is that Ramadan is the better of the two times, so performing (the fast) in it is more appropriate, and what he narrated is interpreted as a case of hardship.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a traveler who can fast without hardship. The Hanafi ruling states that fasting is better (afdal) for such a person, though breaking is permissible. The reasoning is that travel inherently involves hardship, so the Shari'ah allows breaking even without actual difficulty, but since Ramadan is more virtuous than other months, performing the fast in Ramadan is preferable. Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite view, that breaking is better, based on a hadith where the Prophet said fasting in travel is not righteousness. The Hanafi response interprets that hadith as applying to cases of severe hardship. The text also notes a critique of al-Marghinani's transmission, stating that according to actual Shafi'i books, if no hardship, fasting is better, so the disagreement here may be mistaken.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azimat): The stronger or preferred course of action, as opposed to rukhsah (concession). Here, fasting is the azimat for a traveler who does not suffer hardship.
مشقت (mashaqqah): Hardship; the text uses it to justify the permissibility of breaking fast in travel even without actual hardship, because travel inherently involves some difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a traveler who can fast in Ramadan without experiencing hardship?
A) It is obligatory to fast.
B) It is better to fast, but breaking is permissible.
C) It is better to break the fast.
D) It is prohibited to fast.

Key Takeaway
For a traveler who can fast without hardship, the Hanafi school holds that fasting is better (azimat) but breaking is permissible; the Shafi'i school holds the opposite, but both agree on permissibility.

Qada for Sick and Traveler Who Die: Idrak as the Condition
Ruling on qada for sick/traveler who dies, with condition of idrak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qada for a sick person or traveler who dies, and explain the role of idrak as a condition for the obligation.

Core Idea
No qada without idrak: the opportunity to make up is a necessary condition.

This lesson examines a precise ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation of making up missed fasts when a sick person or traveler dies. The key variable is whether they ever had the opportunity (idrak) to make up the fasts after their excuse was removed. The text also corrects a mistaken report of disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two distinct situations: dying while still in the excuse state (sick or traveling) vs. dying after the excuse ends (recovery or residency). List both scenarios.
The ruling changes based on which scenario applies.
2
Apply the condition of idrak
Determine whether the person had the opportunity (idrak) to fast after the excuse removed. This is the decisive factor for the obligation of qada.
Idrak means having sufficient time after the excuse ends to make up the missed fasts before death.
3
Find the Quranic proof
The verse 'fiddatun min ayamin ukhar' (Quran 2:185) is cited. Note how it implies the condition of having other days—the obligation arises only when such days exist.
The dalil is qat'i in transmission but zanni in meaning, leading to Hanafi ruling.
4
Recognize the practical consequence
If qada becomes wajib (because idrak existed), a will for fidyah (feeding the poor) also becomes wajib as a benefit (fa'idah) of that obligation.
This ensures the missed worship is compensated even if the person dies before actually performing the qada.
5
Clarify the school's internal disagreement
Distinguish the false ikhtilaf reported by al-Tahawi (which the author dismisses) from the real ikhtilaf on vowed fasts (nadhr). Understand why the author rejects the reported dispute.
The real dispute on nadhr does not affect the main ruling on Ramadan qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَرِيضُ وَالْمُسَافِرُ وَهُمَا عَلَى حَالِهِمَا لَمْ يَلْزِمُهُمَا الْقَضَاءُ لِأَنَّهُمَا لَمْ يُدْرِكَا عِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ. وَلَوْ صَحَّ الْمَرِيضُ أَوْ أَقَامَ الْمُسَافِرُ ثُمَّ مَاتَا أَزَمَهُمَا الْقَضَاءُ بِقَدْرِ الصِّحَّةِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ لِوُجُودِ الْإِدْرَاكِ بِهَذَا الْمِقْدَارِ. وَفَائِدَتُهُ وُجُوبُ الْوَصِيَّةِ بِالْإِطْعَامِ. وَذَكَرَ الطَّحَاوِي خِلَافًا فِيهِ بَيْنَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَبَيْنَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَلَيْسَ بِصَحِيحٍ. وَإِنَّمَا الْخِلَافُ فِي النَّذْرِ وَالْفَرْقُ لَهُمَا أَنَّ النَّذَرَ سَبَبٌ فَيَظْهَرُ الْوُجُوبُ فِي حَقِّ الْخَلْفِ.
And if the sick person and the traveler die while they are in their state, qada is not incumbent upon them, because they did not reach a number of other days. And if the sick person recovers or the traveler takes up residence, then they die, qada becomes incumbent upon them to the extent of the period of health and residence, due to the existence of capacity to that extent. And its benefit is the obligation of a will for feeding (the poor). And al-Tahawi mentioned a difference of opinion therein between Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf and between Muhammad, but it is not correct. The difference is only concerning vows (nadhr), and the distinction for them is that a vow is a cause, so the obligation appears with respect to the substitute.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on qada (make-up fasting) for a sick person or a traveler who dies. If they die while still sick or traveling, no qada is required because the condition for qada—having the opportunity to make up the fasts after the excuse is removed—was never met. However, if they recover (sick person) or become a resident (traveler) and then die, qada is obligatory to the extent of the days they were healthy/resident. The benefit (fa'idah) of this obligation is that a will must be made to feed a poor person for each missed fast (fidyah). The text also addresses an error attributed to al-Tahawi regarding a supposed ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf on one side and Muhammad on the other about this issue. The correct view is that there is no disagreement here; the real difference pertains to vowed fasts (nadhr), not Ramadan make-ups.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Make-up of an obligatory act of worship missed due to a valid excuse. Here it refers to making up missed Ramadan fasts.
إدراك (idrak): The capacity or opportunity to perform an act. Here, it means having enough time after the excuse ends to make up the fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler dies while still traveling, what is the obligation regarding missed Ramadan fasts?
A) He must have made a will for fidyah.
B) No qada is obligatory because he never had the opportunity to make up.
C) The heirs must make up the fasts.
D) Fidyah must be given from his estate.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to make up missed Ramadan fasts is contingent upon having the opportunity (idrak); if that opportunity never arises before death, no qada is required.

Fasting vs. Breaking Fast for a Traveler in Ramadan
Presents arguments for and against fasting for a traveler, then clarifies the correct Hanafi view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a traveler fasting in Ramadan and explain the evidence, as well as evaluate the opposing view and its proper context.

Core Idea
Fasting in Ramadan is better for a traveler unless hardship makes it disliked.

This lesson examines the classical debate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a traveler should fast or break fast while traveling in Ramadan. The passage from Ashraf ul-Hidayah presents both sides and clarifies the correct Hanafi view, correcting a misattribution in the original Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is being disputed? Determine the core ruling about a traveler's fast in Ramadan.
The question is not whether fasting is obligatory, but whether it is better to fast or break.
2
State the position attributed to the Shafi'i school
The author of al-Hidayah initially reports that Imam al-Shafi'i holds breaking fast is better absolutely.
This is based on ahadith that seem to discourage fasting while traveling.
3
Present the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school uses the Quranic verses 2:185 and 2:184, and the principle that the original time (Ramadan) is superior to its substitute (other days).
The imperative in 'fal-yasumhu' includes travelers, and 'wa an tasumu khayrun lakum' indicates fasting is better.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing ahadith
Those ahadith are interpreted as applying only when fasting causes severe hardship; otherwise, the default preference is to fast.
The Prophet's statements are conditional, not absolute.
5
Note the correction and mufta bihi
The commentator corrects the Hidayah: the actual Shafi'i school (and Malik) agrees that fasting is better unless hardship exists. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that fasting is better.
The mufta bihi is fasting without hardship, breaking with hardship (with qada).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الصوم کے لئے رمضان میں افطار کرنا اولیٰ اور افضل ہے کیونکہ اگر روزہ رکھنا افضل ہوتا تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم روزہ رکھنے والوں کو نا فرمان کیوں فرماتے اور یہ کیوں فرماتے کہ سفر میں روزہ رکھنا نیکی کی بات نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر کے لئے رمضان کے روزے کے دو وقت ہیں ایک وقت تو خود ماہ رمضان ہے جیسا کہ فمن شهد مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ( القرة: ۱۸۵) کا عموم دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مسافر اور متقیم دونوں رمضان میں روزے رکھیں اور دوسرا وقت رمضان کی علاوہ ہے جیسا کہ اَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ (البقرة: ۱۸۵) میں مذکور ہے اور عدة من ايام اخر رمضان کا خلیفہ ہے اور خلیفہ اصل برابر نہیں ہوتا اس کے لئے غیر رمضان ، رمضان کے برابر نہیں ہوگا بلکہ رمضان کا وقت افضل ہے اور کسی عبادت کو افضل وقت میں ادا کرنا بھی افضل ہوتا ہے اس لئے رمضان میں مسافر کے لئے روزہ رکھنا افطار کرنے سے افل ہے اس کی تائید خود باری تعالیٰ کے قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے وَاَنْ تَصُو مُوا خَيْر لَكُم (البقرة : ۱۸۴) یعنی رمضان میں روزہ رکھنا نہ رکھنے سے افضل ہے یہ اس وقت کا رمضان میں فدیہ دیگر افطار کرنے کی اجازت تھی اور رہی وہ حدیثیں جن کو امام شافعی کی جانب سے پیش کیا گیا ہے ان کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ احادیث مشقت کی حالت پر محمول ہیں یعنی اگر سفر میں روزہ رکھنا انتہائی گراں ہو اور پریشانی کا باعث ہو تو ایسی حالت میں روزہ رکھنا واقعی کوئی نیکی کی بات نہیں ہے اور ایسی حالت میں روزہ رکھنا نا فرمانی اور معصیت کی بات ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ سے امام شافعی کا مذہب نقل کرنے میں تسامح ہو گیا ہے کیونکہ شوافع کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر مسافر کو روزہ بھاری معلوم نہ ہو تو روزہ ہی افضل ہے افطار نہیں ہے یہی امام مالک کا مذہب ہے اور یہی ہمارا مذہب ہے مگر چونکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسافر کے لئے مطلقا افطار افضل ہے اس لئے ہم نے اس قول کو لیکر شوافع کی دلیلیں تحریر کی ہیں۔
Ashraf ul-Hidayah, commentary on Urdu Hidayah, volume three, Book of Fasting: For a traveler, breaking fast in Ramadan is more appropriate and better. Because if fasting were better, why would the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, call those who fast disobedient? And why would he say that fasting while traveling is not an act of righteousness? Our proof is that for a traveler there are two times for the Ramadan fast: one time is the month of Ramadan itself, as the general command of 'So whoever is present during the month, let him fast' (al-Baqarah 2:185) indicates that both the traveler and the resident should fast in Ramadan. The second time is other than Ramadan, as mentioned in 'or if on a journey, then a number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:185). And 'a number of other days' is the successor (khalifa) of Ramadan. And a successor is not equal to the original. So non-Ramadan cannot be equal to Ramadan. Rather, the time of Ramadan is better. And performing any act of worship in the better time is also better. Therefore, for a traveler, fasting in Ramadan is better than breaking fast. This is also supported by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And that you fast is better for you' (al-Baqarah 2:184), meaning fasting in Ramadan is better than not fasting. This was at the time when breaking fast with ransom was permissible. As for the hadith that Imam al-Shafi'i presented, the answer is that those hadith are applicable to a state of hardship, meaning that if fasting while traveling is extremely burdensome and causes difficulty, then fasting is indeed not an act of righteousness, and in such a state fasting is disobedience and sin. (Then the commentator says:) The author of al-Hidayah made an error in reporting the school of Imam al-Shafi'i, because in the books of the Shafi'is it is mentioned that if the traveler does not find fasting heavy, then fasting is better, not breaking fast. This is also the school of Imam Malik and it is our school. However, since the author of al-Hidayah stated that for a traveler breaking fast is absolutely better, we have written the arguments of the Shafi'is in support of that statement.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether a traveler should fast or break fast in Ramadan. The author begins by presenting the argument that breaking fast is better, citing prophetic hadith that suggest otherwise. However, this is the view attributed to the Shafi'i school in the Hidayah, but the commentator later corrects this misattribution. The Hanafi proof is then given: there are two times for the fast—Ramadan itself and other days. The original time (Ramadan) is superior to its substitute (non-Ramadan), so performing the fast in the original time is better. This is supported by the Quranic verse 'And that you fast is better for you.' The response to the opposing ahadith is that they apply only when there is real hardship; otherwise, fasting is better. Finally, the commentator clarifies that according to the correct Shafi'i school (and also Imam Malik and the Hanafi school), fasting is better unless hardship exists. The Hidayah's absolute preference for breaking fast is thus not the accepted position.

Key Terms
صوم (sawm): Fasting, specifically the Ramadan fast.
افطار (iftar): Breaking the fast, i.e., not fasting on a day of Ramadan.
سفر (safar): Travel, defined in Hanafi fiqh as a journey of at least three days (approx. 48 miles).
خلیفہ (khalifah): Successor; in this context, the substitute days (other days) are the successor to the original time (Ramadan).
عدة من أيام أخر (iddatun min ayyamin ukhar): A number of other days; the Quranic phrase referring to making up missed fasts on other days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a traveler fasting in Ramadan if there is no hardship?
A) It is wajib to fast.
B) It is haram to fast.
C) Fasting is better (afdal) than breaking fast.
D) Breaking fast is better than fasting.

Key Takeaway
For a traveler, fasting in Ramadan is better than breaking fast unless genuine hardship is present.

Sawm — Fasting

When Qada Becomes Obligatory for a Sick Person or Traveler Who Dies: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains when qada/fidyah is required and rejects an intra-Hanafi dispute reported by Tahawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada/fidyah for a sick or traveling person who dies and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding partial ability using the distinction between a nadhr and Ramadan fasts.

Core Idea
Qada/fidyah for missed fasts is proportional to the days of health/residence, not the total missed, as obligation depends on ability.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses when a sick person or traveler who dies is obligated to make up missed fasts. It distinguishes two scenarios: death while still excused, and death after recovery or becoming resident. The core legal question is whether qada/fidyah is owed for all missed fasts or only for those days the person actually had the ability to fast. An intra-Hanafi dispute attributed to Imam Tahawi is addressed and rejected by the author of al-Hidayah. Understanding this clarifies the operative Hanafi position on the obligation of a will for fidyah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
First, identify when the person dies while still in the state of illness or travel and when they die after recovery or residence. The ruling depends on this distinction.
The first scenario: death in the original excuse → no qada. Second: death after excuse removed → qada proportional to ability.
2
Identify the Quranic basis
Note the verse 'a number of other days' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185) and how it establishes that qada is contingent on experiencing those other days.
The phrase 'عِدَّةً مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ' indicates that the obligation to make up fasts arises only when one has other days available.
3
Understand the benefit of the obligation
The obligation of qada after recovery or residence translates into a requirement to make a will (wasiyyah) for fidyah from one-third of the estate.
If the person dies before actually fasting, the benefit appears as the obligation to leave a will for fidyah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine Tahawi's reported difference: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad on whether fidyah covers all missed fasts or only those possible during the period of ability.
According to Tahawi, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require fidyah for all missed fasts if the person failed to fast during the ability period, while Muhammad requires only for the days they had ability.
5
Apply the tarjih
Understand why al-Hidayah rejects Tahawi's report and affirms the agreed position (proportional fidyah) and where the actual difference lies (vows vs. Ramadan).
The author states the disagreement is only in the case of a nadhr, not in Ramadan fasts. The agreed position is that fidyah is proportional to the days of health/residence.

مریض حالت مرض اور مسافر حالت سفر میں فوت ہو گیا روزہ کی قضا لازم نہیں
وَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَرِيضُ وَالْمُسَافِرُ وَهُمَا عَلَى حَالِهِمَا لَمْ يَلْزِمُهُمَا الْقَضَاءُ لِأَنَّهُمَا لَمْ يُدْرِكَا عِدَّةً مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ ترجمہ اور جبکہ مریض اور مسافر مر گئے حالانکہ وہ دونوں اپنی حالت پر ہیں تو ان کے ذمہ قضا لازم نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں نے ایام اخر سے بقدر قضا دن نہیں پائے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مریض بحالت مرض مر گیا اور مسافر بحالت سفر مر گیا تو ان کے ذمہ قضا لازم نہ ہوگی یعنی مرض اور سفر کی وجہ سے رمضان کے جو روزے قضا ہو گئے ہیں ان کی وجہ سے عند اللہ ماخوذ نہ ہوگا اور نہ ہی ان کا کوئی فدیہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ان پر قضا کا وجوب اس وقت ہوتا ہے جبکہ مرض اور سفر کے ازالہ کے بعد اتنا زمانہ پالیں جس میں روزے رکھے جاسکیں ۔ اور یہاں صورت یہ ہے کہ ان کو قضا کا وقت قطعا نہیں مل سکا اس لئے ان پر قضا لازم نہ ہوگی۔
مریض تندرست، مسافر مقیم ہو گیا پھر دونوں فوت ہو گئے تو قضا لازم ہے
وَلَوْ صَحَّ الْمَرِيضُ أَوْ أَقَامَ الْمُسَافِرُ ثُمَّ مَاتَا لَزِمَهُمَا الْقَضَاءُ بِقَدْرِ الصِّحَّةِ وَالْإِقَامَةِ لِوُجُودِ الْإِدْرَاكِ بِهَٰذَا الْمِقْدَارِ وَفَائِدَتُهُ وُجُوبُ الْوَصِيَّةِ بِالْإِطْعَامِ وَذَكَرَ الطَّحَاوِي خِلَافًا فِيهِ بَيْنَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَبَيْنَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَلَيْسَ بِصَحِيحٍ وَإِنَّمَا الْخِلَافُ فِي النَّذْرِ وَالْفَرْقُ لَهُمَا أَنَّ النَّذْرَ سَبَبٌ فَيَظْهَرُ الْوُجُوبُ فِي حَقِّ الْخَلْفِ وَفِي هَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ السَّبَبُ إِدْرَاكُ الْعِدَّةِ فَيَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِ مَا أَدْرَكَ
ترجمہ اور اگر بیمار تندرست ہو گیا اور مسافر مقیم ہو گیا پھر دونوں مر گئے تو ان پر بقدر صحت اور بقدر اقامت قضا لازم ہوگی کیونکہ ایام اخر اسی مقدار پائے گئے ہیں اور اس کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ طعام فدیہ دینے کی وصیت ان پر واجب ہے اور امام طحاوی نے اس حکم میں ابوحنیفہ ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ صحیح نہیں ہے اور اختلاف نذر کے مسئلہ میں ہے اور شیخین کے مذہب پر فرق یہ ہے کہ نذرسبب ہے تو خلیفہ کے حق میں وجوب ظاہر ہوگا اور اس مسئلہ میں سبب ادراک عدت ہے یعنی ایام اخر کا پانا ہے تو جس قدر ایام اخر پائے گا اس قدر وجوب قضا مقدر ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر بیمار تندرست ہو گیا اور مسافر مقیم ہو گیا پھر وہ مرگیا تو ان پر قضا کرنا لازم ہوگا پس اگر تندرست ہونے کے بعد اور مقیم ہونے کے بعد اتنے دن زندہ رہا جتنے دن کے روزے فوت ہوئے تھے تو فوت شدہ تمام روزوں کی قضا لازم ہے اور اگر چند دن زندہ رہا تو بقدر صحت اور بقدر اقامت روزوں کی قضا واجب ہو گی مثلا مرض یا سفر کی وجہ سے بیس روزے فوت ہو گئے پھر تندرست ہونے کے بعد یا مقیم ہونے کے بعد دس دن زندہ رہ کر کسی اور سبب سے مر گیا تو اس پر دس دن کے روزوں کی قضا کرنا واجب ہوگا کیونکہ مریض اور مسافر کے بارے میں قرآن پاک کا ارشاد ہے فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ یعنی جتنی دن بیمار رہا سفر کی وجہ سے رمضان کے روزے نہیں رکھ سکا اتنے ہی دن کی قضا واجب ہوگی اور جتنے دنوں کی قضا واجب ہے اتنے دن زندہ رہنا بھی ضروری ہے لیکن جب یہ شخص جس کے بیس روزے مرض یا سفر کی وجہ سے فوت ہو گئے ہیں صحت اور اقامت کے بعد زندہ ہی دس دن رہا تو دس دن ہی کے روزوں کی قضا واجب ہوگی کیونکہ اس سے زائد کی قضا پر قدرت ثابت نہیں ہوئی مگر یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ تندرست ہونے کے بعد اور مقیم ہونے کے بعد دس دن زندہ تو بلا شبہ رہا لیکن لا علاج بیماریوں کی وجہ سے مر گیا تو اب قضا ادا کرنے سے کیا فائدہ ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وجوب قضا کا فائدہ وجوب وصیت کی شکل میں ظاہر ہو گا یعنی مرتے وقت اس پر یہ وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا کہ میرے تہائی مال میں سے مقدار واجب روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کر دینا چنانچہ اگر یہ وصیت کی اور ورثہ نے وصیت کے مطابق فدیہ دے دیا تو ان شاء اللہ یہ عنداللہ ماخوذ نہ ہوگا اور اگر یہ وصیت نہ کی تو گنہگار ہوگا اور قیامت میں ماخوذ ہوگا بہر حال ظاہر مذہب کے مطابق بقدر صحت اور بقدر اقامت فدیہ کا لازم ہونا امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا متفق علیہ فیصلہ ہے لیکن حضرت امام طحاوی نے ان تینوں حضرات کے درمیان اختلاف ذکر کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا ہے کہ اگر رخصت افطار کا عذر یعنی مرض اور سفر زائل ہو گیا اور فوت شدہ روزوں میں سے بعض کی قضا پر قادر ہوا اور بعض کی قضا پر قادر نہ ہوا مثلا عذر زائل ہونے کے بعد دس دن زندہ رہا حالانکہ فوت شدہ روزے بیس ہیں پس اگر اس نے قدرت کی مقدار یعنی دس روزوں کی قضا کر لی اور اس میں کوئی کوتاہی نہیں کی پھر مر گیا تو بقیہ دس روزوں کی قضا اس پر لازم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس نے ان دس روزوں کی قضا کا وقت نہیں پایا ہے اور جب وقت نہیں پایا تو ان کی قضا بھی واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر قدرت کی مقدار یعنی دس دن جن میں زندہ رہا ہے ان میں بھی روزے نہیں رکھے حتی کہ اسی حال میں مر گیا تو ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس پر پورے بیس روزوں کی قضا واجب ہوگی یعنی ان کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر فقط ماقدر علیہ یعنی دس دن کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا اور باقی دس دن جن کو اس نے پایا ہی نہیں ان کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام طحاوی کا یہ اختلاف بیان کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ اس
If a sick person dies in his sickness, or a traveler dies in his travel, qada is not obligatory upon them because they did not experience a number of other days. Explanation: If a sick person dies while sick and a traveler dies while traveling, qada is not obligatory upon them, meaning they will not be taken to account for the missed fasts due to illness or travel, nor is any fidyah obligatory upon them. Because the obligation of qada arises only after the removal of the excuse (illness/travel) and having sufficient time to fast. In this case, they did not have any time for qada, so it is not obligatory. If the sick person recovers or the traveler becomes resident, then they die, qada is obligatory to the extent of the period of health and residence, because they experienced qada time to that extent. The benefit of this obligation is the obligation of making a will for fidyah (feeding the poor). Al-Tahawi mentioned a difference of opinion in this between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Muhammad on the other, but it is not correct. The difference is only in the case of a vow (nadhr). The distinction for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that a vow is a cause, so obligation becomes apparent for the successor; while in this case the cause is the experiencing of the number of days, so it is proportional to what was experienced. Explanation: If the sick person recovers and the traveler becomes resident, then they die, qada is obligatory upon them. If after recovery/residence they live as many days as the number of missed fasts, then qada of all missed fasts is obligatory. If they lived only a few days, qada is obligatory to the extent of health/residence. For example, twenty fasts were missed due to illness or travel, then after recovery/residence they lived ten days and died of some other cause, then qada of ten days is obligatory. Because the Quran says 'a number of other days' meaning as many days as missed, qada is obligatory. And living the number of days for which qada is obligatory is necessary. But if after recovery/residence they lived only ten days, qada of only ten days is obligatory because beyond that they had no ability. A question arises: What benefit is there in qada if they lived ten days but died? The answer is that the benefit of the obligation of qada appears in the form of the obligation of making a will: at the time of death, they must will that fidyah for the fasts be given from one-third of their wealth. If they make such a will and the heirs give fidyah, then by the will of Allah they will not be taken to account. If they do not make the will, they will be sinful and will be taken to account on the Day of Judgment. In any case, according to the apparent madhhab, the obligation of fidyah proportional to health/residence is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. However, Imam al-Tahawi mentioned a difference among the three imams: He said that if the excuse for breaking fast (illness/travel) is removed and the person becomes able to make up some missed fasts but not others—for example, after the excuse removal he lived ten days although twenty fasts were missed—then if he made up the ten fasts (to the extent of his ability) without negligence and then died, the remaining ten fasts are not obligatory for him because he did not have time for them. And if he did not make up the ten fasts during those ten days and died in that state, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, qada for all twenty fasts is obligatory, i.e., making a will for fidyah is necessary. Imam Muhammad said that only the ten fasts he could have made up require a will for fidyah; the remaining ten for which he had no time require no will. The author of al-Hidayah says that al-Tahawi's report of this difference is not correct, but rather...
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on qada (making up missed fasts) for a sick person or traveler who dies. It is divided into two cases: (1) If they die while still in the state of illness or travel, qada is not obligatory because they never had the opportunity to make up the fasts. (2) If they recover from illness or become resident, they become obligated to make up the missed fasts. If they die after some time, qada is obligatory to the extent of the days they lived in health/residence. The benefit of this obligation is that they must make a will for fidyah (feeding the poor) from their estate. The passage then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Tahawi reported a difference among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. According to Tahawi, if a person had twenty missed fasts, recovered, lived ten days but did not fast during those ten days and died, then Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say fidyah is required for all twenty, while Muhammad says only for the ten days possible. The author of al-Hidayah (and the commentator) reject Tahawi's report, stating that the real difference is only in the case of a vow (nadhr), not in Ramadan fasts. The established Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) is that fidyah is required proportional to the days of health/residence.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up missed obligatory fasts after the Ramadan month.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation for missed fasts by feeding the poor (one meal per fast).
وصیت (wasiyyah): Will or testament; the obligation to instruct that fidyah be given from one's wealth.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to fast voluntarily; its obligation arises from the vow itself.
ادارک عدت (idrak al-iddah): Experiencing the number of days; i.e., having the opportunity to fast on other days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, if a traveler becomes a resident and lives for 5 days after missing 10 fasts, then dies, how many days of fidyah are required?
A) 0 days
B) 5 days
C) 10 days
D) 15 days

Key Takeaway
The obligation of qada/fidyah for missed Ramadan fasts depends on the ability to make them up; if death occurs before opportunity, no obligation arises; if after partial opportunity, only proportional fidyah is due.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Qada and Wasiyyah After Recovery – Scope of Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute resolution on qada and wasiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada and wasiyyah for a person who recovers from illness/travel and dies without making up all missed fasts, and explain why the obligation is proportional to days lived.

Core Idea
Qada is only wajib for days one actually lives after recovery; fidya covers only those days.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: a person misses Ramadan fasts due to a valid excuse, recovers, lives only a few days, and then dies. How many fasts must be made up? Is a will for fidya required for all missed fasts or only some? The Hanafi school's answer is precise and rooted in the Quranic principle of ability. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and the correction of a reported intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage to determine the hukm: after recovery, qada is wajib only for the number of days the person lived. If not made up, a will (wasiyyah) for fidya is also wajib for those same days.
The text uses 'wajib' in a general sense; technically qada is fard, but the discussion uses wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 'فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ' (a number of other days) is cited. The verse implies that the obligation is a like-for-like replacement, contingent on having the ability to fast those days.
The dalil is dalalatan zanni (probative in meaning) but thubutan qati (certain in transmission).
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Tahawi reported a disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on whether qada of all missed fasts is wajib or only those one could have made. The author of al-Hidayah refutes this, stating the three imams actually agree on the proportional obligation.
The real disagreement is in the case of nadhr (vows), not qada of Ramadan.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If a person misses 20 fasts, lives 10 days, and dies: according to the mufta bihi view, only 10 days' qada/fidya is owed. If the reported opposition were accepted, all 20 would be owed.
The practical consequence is significant for estate planning and fulfillment of obligations.

کتاب الصوم
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم مسئلہ میں شیخین کا قول وہی ہے جس کو امام محمد نے اختیار کیا ہے ہاں نذر کے مسئلہ میں شیخیں اور امام محمد نے اختلاف کیا ہے یعنی مریض نے اگر یوں کہا کہ میں اللہ کے لئے ایک ماہ کے روزوں کی نذر مانتا ہوں پھر وہ تندرست ہونے سے پہلے مر گیا تو اس پر بالکل قضا واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ ایک دن تندرست رہا پھر اچانک مر گیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک پورے ایک ماہ کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر بقد صحت روزوں کے فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہے حضرت امام محمد نے بندے کے واجب کرنے کو اللہ کے واجب کرنے پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی جس طرح قضار مضان کے روزوں میں بقدر صحت قضا کرنا لازم ہے اور قضاء نہ کرنے کی صورت میں فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہے اس طرح نذر کے روزے بقدر صحت واجب ہوں گے اور روزہ نہ رکھنے کی صورت میں فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کر نالازم ہوگا اور شیخین کے نزدیک قضار مضان اور نذر کے روزوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ نذر کے روزے واجب ہونے کا سبب نذر ہے اور نذر موجود ہے اور مانع یعنی مرض زائل ہو گیا پس جب سب یعنی نذر موجود ہے اور مانع یعنی مرض زائل ہو گیا تو بالیقیین روزوں کا وجوب ظاہر ہوگا اور جب وجوب متحقق ہو گیا اور ادا کرنا پایا گیا تو اس کے خلیفہ یعنی فدیہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا یعنی پورے ماہ کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا اور قضا رمضان کے مسئلہ میں قضا کا سبب ایام اخر کا پانا ہے اور ایام اخر پورے طور پر پائے نہیں گئے بلکہ بعض ایام پائے گئے تو جس قدر ایام پائے گئے اس قدر قضاء کے روزے واجب ہوں گے اور قضا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں انہی روزوں کے فدیہ کی وصیت کر نالازم ہوگا اور مابقی کی قضا واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
Book of Fasting. In this matter, the cause is reaching the [number of] days, so it is determined according to what was reached. Translation: And if the sick person recovers and the traveler becomes resident, then both die, then qada is obligatory upon them according to the amount of health and residence, because the remaining days were found in that amount. And its benefit is that the will to give food as fidya is obligatory upon them. Imam al-Tahawi mentioned a disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad in this ruling, but it is not correct; the disagreement is in the matter of nadhr. And according to the two shaykhs, the difference is that nadhr is the cause, so the obligation becomes apparent regarding the substitute, while in this matter the cause is the reaching of the remaining days, so as many remaining days as are reached, the obligation of qada is determined accordingly. Explanation: The issue is that if a sick person recovers and a traveler becomes resident, then he dies, then qada is obligatory upon him. If after recovery and residence he lived as many days as the fasts missed, then qada of all missed fasts is obligatory. If he lived only a few days, then qada is wajib according to the amount of health and residence. For example, twenty fasts were missed due to illness or travel, then after recovery or residence he lived ten days and died from another cause, then qada of ten days is wajib upon him, because regarding the sick and traveler, the Holy Quran says: 'a number of other days' meaning however many days he was ill or unable to fast due to travel, that many days qada is wajib, and it is also necessary that he lives that many days. But when this person, whose fasts were missed due to illness or travel, lived only ten days after health and residence, then qada of only ten days is wajib, because ability to make up more than that was not established. But here there is a question: he undoubtedly lived ten days after recovery and residence, but he died without making them up, so what benefit is there in qada being obligatory? The answer is that the benefit of the obligation of qada appears in the form of the obligation of the will: at the time of death, it becomes necessary for him to make a will that from one-third of his wealth, the fidya for the wajib amount of fasts should be given. So if he makes this will and the heirs give the fidya according to the will, then insha'Allah he will not be held accountable before Allah. If he does not make the will, he will be sinful and will be held accountable on the Day of Judgment. In any case, according to the apparent madhhab, the obligation of fidya proportional to health and residence is an agreed upon ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two shaykhs. However, Imam al-Tahawi mentioned a disagreement among these three. He said: if the permission for breaking fast (i.e., illness or travel) is removed, and he was able to make qada of some of the missed fasts but not others, for example, after the removal of the excuse, he lived ten days while the missed fasts were twenty. Then if he made qada of the amount he was able to (i.e., ten fasts) and did not delay, then died, qada of the remaining ten fasts is not obligatory upon him because he did not reach the time for their qada. If he did not fast during the ten days he lived, and died in that state, then according to [Abu Hanifa?] the qada of all twenty fasts is wajib upon him, meaning the will to give fidya for all twenty is necessary. Imam Muhammad said: only the will to give fidya for what he was able to (i.e., ten fasts) is necessary, and the will to give fidya for the remaining ten days which he never reached is not necessary. The author of al-Hidayah says: Imam al-Tahawi's mention of this disagreement is not correct; rather, in this matter the statement of the two shaykhs is the same as that chosen by Imam Muhammad. Yes, in the matter of nadhr, the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad disagreed: if a sick person said, 'I vow to fast one month for Allah,' and then he died before recovering, then no qada is wajib at all. If he lived one day after recovery and then suddenly died, then according to the two shaykhs, it is necessary to make a will to give fidya for the entire month, while Imam Muhammad said: only the will to give fidya proportional to the days of health is necessary. Imam Muhammad analogized the obligation made by a servant to the obligation made by Allah: just as in qada of Ramadan fasts, qada is necessary proportional to health, and if not done, a will for fidya is necessary, similarly for nadhr fasts, they become wajib proportional to health, and if not fasted, a will for fidya is necessary. According to the two shaykhs, the difference between qada of Ramadan and nadhr fasts is: the cause of wajib for nadhr fasts is the nadhr, and the nadhr exists, and the impediment (illness) is removed. So since the cause (nadhr) exists and the impediment is removed, the wajib of the fasts becomes certain, and when the wajib is established and performance is found impossible, then recourse is to its substitute (fidya), so making a will for fidya for the entire month is necessary. In the matter of qada of Ramadan, the cause of qada is the reaching of the remaining days, and the remaining days were not fully reached; only some days were reached, so qada fasts are wajib only for as many days as were reached, and if not made up, a will for fidya for only those days is necessary, and qada of the rest is not wajib.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a person who missed Ramadan fasts due to illness or travel, then recovers or becomes resident, but dies before making up all the missed fasts. The central question is the extent of the obligation to make up fasts and the requirement to leave a will for fidya (expiation) after death. The passage begins by stating the general rule that the obligation of qada (making up fasts) is proportional to the number of days one lived after the excuse was removed. The Quranic verse 'a number of other days' (فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ) indicates that the obligation is to fast an equivalent number of days, but this is only binding if one actually has the opportunity (ability) to do so. Thus, if a person lived only ten days after recovering, only ten days of qada are obligatory. If he failed to fast those ten days, he must make a will that fidya be given from his wealth for those ten days. The passage then addresses a disagreement reported by Imam al-Tahawi, who claimed that Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani differed on whether qada of all missed fasts is obligatory or only those one had time to make up. The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) refutes this, stating that the three imams actually agree in this matter; the real disagreement is in the case of voluntary vows (nadhr). In the nadhr case, if someone vowed to fast a month, then recovered and lived one day before dying, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the entire month's fidya is owed, while Muhammad holds it is proportional to days lived. The reasoning is that in nadhr, the cause (the vow) is fully present and the impediment is removed, so the full obligation stands. In qada of Ramadan, the cause is reaching the days, which only partially occurred. This clarification is important for understanding the nuanced application of qada and fidya obligations in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed religious obligations, here specifically missed Ramadan fasts.
فدیہ (fidya): Expiation for missed fasts that cannot be made up due to death or incapacity; here it is a financial compensation from the deceased's estate.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will made by a person regarding their property, here specifically to instruct heirs to give fidya on their behalf.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform a specific act of worship, here fasting. The passage contrasts nadhr with qada of Ramadan.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs, i.e., Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (sometimes also including Muhammad, but here used for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person missed 30 days of Ramadan due to travel. He returned home and lived 15 days before dying without making up any fasts. According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the obligation?
A) Qada of all 30 days is obligatory, and if not done, wasiyyah for all 30.
B) Qada of 15 days is obligatory, and if not done, wasiyyah for 15 days is necessary.
C) No qada or wasiyyah is required because he died.
D) Qada of 30 days is obligatory, but wasiyyah for only 15.

Key Takeaway
Qada of missed Ramadan fasts is wajib only for days one actually lives after the excuse ends; if not made up, a will for fidya is required for those days alone.

Qada of Ramadan: Separate or Consecutive?
States that qada can be separate or consecutive, with consecutive recommended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing qada fasts separately versus consecutively, and explain why consecutiveness is recommended but not obligatory.

Core Idea
Qada of Ramadan: separate or consecutive – both valid; consecutive is recommended to hasten obligation.

Making up missed Ramadan fasts is an obligation, but how should one schedule them? The Hanafi school, based on the absolute wording of the Quran, grants flexibility. However, there is a recommended method that expedites fulfilling the duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qada (making up missed Ramadan fasts). The ruling for the manner is that both separate (farq) and consecutive (mutaba'ah) are valid. The qada itself is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the absolute Quranic text (إطلاق النص) from Surah al-Baqarah 2:184: 'فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ' (a number of other days). The command does not specify any order.
dalil is Quranic, thubut qati, dalala zanni (since it does not explicitly mention the method).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of specification in the verse means that either method is permissible. The absolute nature allows flexibility.
4
Note the recommendation
The passage adds that consecutive (mutaba'ah) is mustahab (recommended) to hasten the removal of the wajib obligation.
Recommendation is for spiritual benefit, not legal requirement.
5
Contrast with expiatory fasts
Sahib al-Inayah's expansion mentions expiatory fasts (kaffarah for killing and zihar) that must be consecutive, highlighting the difference from qada.
This contrast reinforces that qada does not require consecutiveness.

Source Text

تشریح صاحب عنایہ کہتے ہیں کہ کتاب اللہ میں آٹھ قسم کے روزوں کا ذکر ہے (1) صوم رمضان باری تعالی کا قول ہے فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليضمه یعنی جو کوئی پائے تم میں سے اس مہینہ کو تو ضرور روزہ رکھے۔ (پ ۷۲) (۲) ( صوم کفار قتل چنانچہ ارشاد ہے وَإِن كَانَ منْ قَوْم بينكم وبينهم ميثاق فديةٌ مُسلَّمةَ إِلَى اهْلِهِ وَتَحْرِير رقبة مؤمنة فمن لم يجد فَصيام شهرين متتابعين توبة من الله یعنی اگر وہ تھا ایسی قوم میں ہے کہ تم میں اور ان میں عہدے تو خون بہا پہنچائے ۔ اس کی گھر والوں کو اور آزاد کرنے گردن ایک مسلمان کی کچھ حسن کو میسر نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے دوماہ کے پے درپے گناہ بنوانے کو اللہ سے۔ (پدر۱۰) (۳) کفارہ ظہار باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے والدين بظاهرون من تسآنهم ثم يعوذونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مَنْ قبل ان يتما ساد الكُمْ تُو َعظون به والله بما تعملون خبير ، فمن لم يجد فصيامُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ مِنْ قَبْل أَنْ
Qada of Ramadan is valid both separately and consecutively. And the qada of Ramadan: if he wishes, he may separate it, and if he wishes, he may do it consecutively, due to the absoluteness of the text. But the preferred (mustahab) is consecutive, to hasten the removal of the obligation. Translation: And qada of Ramadan, if he wishes, he may do it separately, and if he wishes, consecutively, because the text is absolute. But the recommended is consecutive to hasten the dropping of the wajib. Explanation: Sahib al-Inayah says: Eight types of fasts are mentioned in the Book of Allah: (1) Sawm Ramadan: Allah says 'So whoever among you sights the month, let him fast it.' (2) Sawm of expiation for killing: ...
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents a straightforward ruling: when making up missed Ramadan fasts, one may either fast them on separate days (e.g., sporadically) or consecutively (without interruption). This flexibility is based on the absolute wording of the Quranic command to fast 'a number of other days' (فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ), which does not specify any order. Therefore, both methods are legally valid. However, it is recommended (mustahab) to fast them consecutively because this hastens the fulfillment of the obligation and removes the responsibility sooner. The commentator, Sahib al-Inayah, then notes that in the Book of Allah, eight types of fasts are mentioned, starting with Ramadan fasts and including expiatory fasts for killing and zihar, which require consecutive fasting. This underscores that for qada of Ramadan, consecutiveness is not required, unlike some other obligations. The lesson emphasizes the distinction between what is legally permissible and what is recommended for spiritual benefit.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed Ramadan fasts. The passage addresses the method of performing them.
متابعة (mutaba'ah): Consecutive performance (fasting day after day without interruption).
فرق (farq): Separate performance (fasting on non-consecutive days).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not valid; they must be done consecutively.
B) It is valid but makruh.
C) It is valid and permissible; consecutive is recommended.
D) It is only valid if done before the next Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits qada of Ramadan to be performed either separately or consecutively; consecutive is recommended but not obligatory.

Dispute on Nadhr Fasts: Full Month or Proportional Fidya?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation of fidya for missed nadhr fasts after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the obligation of fidya for missed nadhr fasts when a sick person recovers partially and then dies, and identify the basis of each position.

Core Idea
Cause fully present = full obligation; partial cause = proportional obligation.

This lesson dives into a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement about the extent of fidya (compensation) for missed nadhr (vow) fasts when a person falls ill, recovers only briefly, and then dies. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the entire month of vowed fasts becomes obligatory because the cause (the vow) was fully present and the barrier (illness) was removed. Imam Muhammad, however, analogizes to the qada of Ramadan fasts, where obligation is proportional to the days of health. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in identifying the cause (sabab) and barrier (mani’) in fiqh reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputed ruling
Read the passage: a sick person vows to fast a month, recovers for one day, then dies. The dispute is whether fidya must be willed for the entire month or only for the day(s) of health. Identify both positions.
The Shaykhayn say full month; Imam Muhammad says proportional to healthy days.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad’s qiyas (analogy)
Imam Muhammad draws an analogy to qada of Ramadan fasts. In Ramadan, if a person becomes healthy for some days and then dies, qada (and thus fidya) is only for the days they could have fasted. He argues the same principle applies to nadhr.
The qiyas is based on the idea that obligation is proportional to capacity (bi qadr al-wus').
3
Understand the Shaykhayn’s counter-argument
The Shaykhayn distinguish nadhr from Ramadan qada. In nadhr, the cause (the vow) is fully present from the moment it is uttered, and the barrier (illness) is completely removed upon recovery. Therefore, the full obligation is established. In contrast, the cause for Ramadan qada is reaching the later days, which only happened partially.
Key distinction: cause of obligation (sabab) vs. cause of qada (which is partial).
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under the Shaykhayn, the estate must pay fidya for the full month; under Imam Muhammad, only for the days of health. This affects inheritance and the deceased’s obligations.
The mufta bihi in the school is typically the Shaykhayn's position.
5
Reflect on the usul principle at play
This dispute highlights the usul principle that when the cause (sabab) is fully present and the barrier (mani’) is completely removed, the obligation is complete. Conversely, if the cause is only partially realized, the obligation is proportional.
This relates to the concept of 'illa (effective cause) and its scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس مسئلہ میں شیخین کا قول وہی ہے جس کو امام محمد نے اختیار کیا ہے ہاں نذر کے مسئلہ میں شیخیں اور امام محمد نے اختلاف کیا ہے یعنی مریض نے اگر یوں کہا کہ میں اللہ کے لئے ایک ماہ کے روزوں کی نذر مانتا ہوں پھر وہ تندرست ہونے سے پہلے مر گیا تو اس پر بالکل قضا واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ ایک دن تندرست رہا پھر اچانک مر گیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک پورے ایک ماہ کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا ضروری ہوگا اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر بقد صحت روزوں کے فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہے حضرت امام محمد نے بندے کے واجب کرنے کو اللہ کے واجب کرنے پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی جس طرح قضار مضان کے روزوں میں بقدر صحت قضا کرنا لازم ہے اور قضاء نہ کرنے کی صورت میں فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہے اس طرح نذر کے روزے بقدر صحت واجب ہوں گے اور روزہ نہ رکھنے کی صورت میں فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کر نالازم ہوگا اور شیخین کے نزدیک قضار مضان اور نذر کے روزوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ نذر کے روزے واجب ہونے کا سبب نذر ہے اور نذر موجود ہے اور مانع یعنی مرض زائل ہو گیا پس جب سب یعنی نذر موجود ہے اور مانع یعنی مرض زائل ہو گیا تو بالیقیین روزوں کا وجوب ظاہر ہوگا اور جب وجوب متحقق ہو گیا اور ادا کرنا پایا گیا تو اس کے خلیفہ یعنی فدیہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا یعنی پورے ماہ کے روزوں کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا اور قضا رمضان کے مسئلہ میں قضا کا سبب ایام اخر کا پانا ہے اور ایام اخر پورے طور پر پائے نہیں گئے بلکہ بعض ایام پائے گئے تو جس قدر ایام پائے گئے اس قدر قضاء کے روزے واجب ہوں گے اور قضا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں انہی روزوں کے فدیہ کی وصیت کر نالازم ہوگا اور مابقی کی قضا واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
In this issue, the statement of the Shaykhayn is the same as the one chosen by Imam Muhammad. However, in the issue of nadhr (vow), the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad differed. That is, if a sick person said, 'I vow to fast one month for the sake of Allah,' then he died before becoming healthy, then no qada is obligatory upon him at all. And if he remained healthy for one day and then suddenly died, then according to the Shaykhayn, it will be necessary to make a will to pay fidya for the entire month of fasts. Imam Muhammad said that it is necessary to make a will to pay fidya for the fasts equivalent to the days of health. Imam Muhammad analogized the wajib of the slave to the wajib of Allah. That is, just as in the qada of Ramadan fasts, it is necessary to make qada according to the days of health, and in case of not making qada, it is necessary to make a will for fidya, similarly, nadhr fasts will be obligatory according to the days of health, and in case of not fasting, it will be necessary to make a will to give fidya. According to the Shaykhayn, the reason for the difference between qada of Ramadan and nadhr fasts is that the cause of obligation of nadhr fasts is the nadhr itself, and the nadhr is present, and the barrier (sickness) has been removed. So when all (i.e., the nadhr is present and the barrier is removed), the obligation of fast is clearly established. And when the obligation is established and performance was not done, one refers to its substitute, i.e., fidya. So it will be necessary to make a will to pay fidya for the entire month. In the issue of qada of Ramadan, the cause of qada is reaching the later days, and the later days were not reached entirely, but some days were reached. So for the days reached, qada fasting is obligatory, and in case of not making qada, it is necessary to make a will for fidya of those specific days. Qada for the remaining days is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of fidya for missed nadhr (vow) fasts when a sick person dies after recovering partially. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that if the person recovers even for one day, the entire month of vowed fasts becomes wajib, and fidya must be willed for all. Imam Muhammad analogizes nadhr fasts to qada of Ramadan fasts: only the days of health are due, and fidya is only for those days. The basis of Imam Muhammad's qiyas is that both are obligations created by a cause (nadhr or Ramadan), and the barrier (sickness) determines the extent. The Shaykhayn distinguish by saying that the cause of nadhr (the vow) is fully present and the barrier is removed, so the full obligation is established; whereas in Ramadan qada, the cause (reaching the later days) is only partial. This dispute shows the importance of identifying the cause (sabab) and barrier (mani') in determining the scope of obligation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but typical Hanafi fatwa follows the Shaykhayn in this matter.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, such as fasting.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two masters: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf.
فدیہ (fidya): Monetary compensation for missed obligatory fasts when qada is not possible.
قضا (qada): Making up missed obligatory acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a person vows to fast a month, recovers for 10 days, then dies, how much fidya must be willed?
A) Fidya for the full month of 30 days.
B) Fidya for only 10 days.
C) No fidya at all because he died.
D) Fidya for 20 days.

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn require full month fidya for nadhr fasts after any recovery, while Imam Muhammad requires only proportional fidya—the key is whether the cause (sabab) of obligation is fully present or only partial.

Hanafi Ruling on Consecutive Qada of Ramadan and the Principle of Eight Fasts
Enumeration of eight Quranic fasts and a principle for consecutive observance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qada of Ramadan may be performed separately or consecutively and apply the principle that consecutiveness is required only when freeing a slave ('itq raqaba) is an alternative in the same verse.

Core Idea
Qada of Ramadan is flexible; consecutiveness is recommended, not required, unless the text also offers freeing a slave.

In this passage, the Hanafi school clarifies that making up missed Ramadan fasts does not require consecutive days. While it is recommended to fast them without interruption to discharge the obligation quickly, it is equally valid to separate them. The basis is the absolute (mutlaq) Quranic text. Furthermore, the commentator enumerates eight types of fasts from the Quran and derives a general principle: wherever the option of freeing a slave is mentioned in the same verse, the fasting alternative must be consecutive; otherwise, consecutiveness is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position on whether qada of Ramadan must be fasted consecutively or can be separated. The text says 'in shaa farraqahu wa in shaa taba'ahu' (if he wishes he may separate it, and if he wishes he may make it consecutive).
This indicates both options are valid.
2
Understand the Dalil
The reason is the absolute nature of the Quranic text (nass mutlaq) which does not require consecutiveness. The verse for qada (al-Baqarah 2:185) says 'fa 'iddatun min ayyamin ukhara' without specifying mutaba'ah.
A mutlaq text remains unrestricted until a restricting evidence (muqayyid) is found.
3
Review the Eight Fasts
Memorize the eight types listed: (1) Ramadan, (2) Kaffara for killing (qatl), (3) Kaffara for zihar, (4) Kaffara for oath (yamin), (5) Qada of Ramadan, (6) Tamattu'/Qiran Hajj, (7) Shaving head (halaq), (8) Hunting compensation (jaza' sayd). Note which have the option of freeing a slave ('itq raqaba) and which do not.
First four (1-4) include 'itq raqaba as an alternative; last four (5-8) do not.
4
Apply the Principle
Apply the rule stated by the mashayikh: where 'itq raqaba is an alternative, fasting must be consecutive (tabi'); where not, consecutiveness is optional (with consecutiveness being mustahabb for qada).
For example, kaffara zihar offers freeing a slave, so the fasting option must be two consecutive months; qada of Ramadan does not offer freeing a slave, so fasting may be separated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( صوم کفار قتل چنانچہ ارشاد ہے وَإِن كَانَ منْ قَوْم بينكم وبينهم ميثاق فديةٌ مُسلَّمةَ إِلَى اهْلِهِ وَتَحْرِير رقبة مؤمنة فمن لم يجد فَصيام شهرين متتابعين توبة من الله یعنی اگر وہ تھا ایسی قوم میں ہے کہ تم میں اور ان میں عہدے تو خون بہا پہنچائے ۔ اس کی گھر والوں کو اور آزاد کرنے گردن ایک مسلمان کی کچھ حسن کو میسر نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے دوماہ کے پے درپے گناہ بنوانے کو اللہ سے۔ (پدر۱۰) (۳) کفارہ ظہار باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے والدين بظاهرُون من تسآنهم ثم يعوذونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مَنْ قبل ان يتما ساد الكُمْ تُو َعظُون به والله بما تعملون خبير، فمن لم يجد فصيامُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ مِنْ قَبْل أَنْ يَتَمَاسَّا فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَاطْعَام ستين مسكينا، یعنی جو لوگ ماں کہہ بیٹھیں اپنی عورتوں کو پھر کرنا چاہیں وہی کام جس کو کہا ہے تو آزاد کرنا چاہئے ایک بردہ پہلے اس سے کہ آپس میں ہاتھ لگائیں اس سے تم کو نصیحت ہوگی اور اللہ خبر رکھتا ہے جو کچھ تم کرتے ہو پھر جو کوئی نہ پائے تو روزے ہیں دو ماہ کے لگاتار پہلے اس سے کہ آپس میں چھو میں پھر جو کوئی یہ نہ کر سکے تو کھانا دینا ہے ساتھ محتاجوں کا ۔ (پ ۱/۲۸) (۴ کفارہ یمین باری تعالیٰ کا قول ہے وَلكِنْ تُؤَاخِذْ كُم بِمَا عَقَدَتُمُ الْأَيْمَانَ فَكَفَّارَتْهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ فَمَنْ لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ ذَالِكَ كَفَّارَةُ أَيْمَانِكُمْ اذَا خَلَفْتُمْ وَاحْفَظُوا اَيْمَانَكُمْ یعنی لیکن پکڑتا ہے اس پر جس قسم کو تم نے مضبوط باندھا سو اس کا کفارہ کھانا دینا ہے دس محتاجوں کو اوسط درجہ کا کھانا جو دیتے ہو تم اپنے گھر والوں کو یا کپڑا پہنا دینا دس محتاجوں کو یا ایک گردن آزاد کرنی پھر جس کو میسر نہ ہو تو روزے رکھتے ہیں تین دن کے یہ کفارہ ہے تمہاری قسموں کا جب قسم کھا بیٹھو اور حفاظت رکھو اپنی قسموں کی ۔ (پ ۲٫۷) قضائے رمضان باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے وَمَن كَانَ مَرِيضًا أَوْ عَلى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّام اخر یعنی جو کوئی ہو بیمار یا مسافر تو اس کو گنتی پوری کرنی چاہئے اور دنوں سے۔ (پ ۷/۲) ( صوم متعہ ( حج تمتع اور قران کے روزے) باری تعالیٰ کا قول ہے فَمَنْ تَمَتَعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَقِّ وَسَعَةٍ إِذَارَ جَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةُ كَامِلَةً یعنی جو کوئی فائدہ اٹھائے عمرہ کو ملا کر حج کے ساتھ تو اس پر ہے جو کچھ میسر ہو قربانی سے پھر جس کو قربانی نہ ملے تو روزے رکھے تین حج کے دنوں میں اور سات روزے جب لوٹو ، یہ دس روزے ہوئے پورے۔ (پ ۲ (۸) کنار حلق راس ... ارشاد باری تعالی ہے فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم رِيضًا أَوبِه أَذًى مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِّنْ صِيَامٍ أَو صَدَقَةٍ اؤٹس یعنی پھر جو کوئی تم میں سے بیمار ہو یا اس کو تکلیف ہو سر کی تو بدلا دیوے روزے یا خیرات یا قربانی۔ (پ ۲ رکوع ۸) ( عموم جزائے صید چنانچہ ارشاد ہے یا يهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوالَا تَقَتَلُوا الصَّيدِ وَانتُم حُرُمُ وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُم مَّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاء يْسَاتِهَا مثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَاعَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ هَديَّا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ اَوْ كَفَّارَةً طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ أَو عَدْلُ ذَالِكَ صِيَامًا ليَذُوقَ وَبَالَ أَمرِه یعنی اے ایمان والو! نہ مارو شکار جس وقت تم ہو ا حرام میں اور جو کوئی تم میں اس کو مارے جان کر تو اس پر بدلا ہے اس مازے ہوئے کے برابر مویشی میں سے جو تجویز کریں دو آدمی معتبر تم میں سے اس طرح سے کہ وہ جانور بدلے کا بطور نیاز پہنچا یا جائے کہ بہ تک یا اس پر کفارہ ہے چند محتاجوں کو کھلانا یا اس کے برابر روزے تا کہ چھکے سزا اپنے کام کی۔ (پ رکوع ۳ ) ان میں سے اول کے چار میں تابع اور بلا ناغہ ادا کرنے کی شرط ہے اور آخر کے چار میں اختیار ہے چاہے ان کو متفرق طور پر ادا کرے اور چاہے تابع کے ساتھ بلاناغہ ادا کرے۔ صوم رمضان کے اندر تابع اور تسلسل کے واجب ہونے میں کوئی کلام نہیں ہے اور اس کے علاوہ میں مشائخ نے ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جس جگہ عتق رقبہ مشروع ہے وہاں روزے کے اندر تابع شرط ہے اور جہاں معتق رقبہ مشروع نہیں ہے وہاں روزے کے اندر تقابع شرط نہیں ہے پس اس ضابطہ کے تحت قرآن پاک میں جہاں قضاء صوم رمضان کا ذکر ہے
Qada of Ramadan is valid both separately and consecutively. And the qada of Ramadan: if he wishes he may separate it and if he wishes he may make it consecutive due to the absolute nature of the text, but the recommended is consecutive to hasten in dropping the obligation. Commentary: The author of al-Inayah says that eight types of fasts are mentioned in the Book of Allah: (1) Fasting of Ramadan: Allah's saying 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it.' (2) Fasting of expiation for killing: The verse 'And if he belonged to a people with whom you have a treaty, then a blood money delivered to his family and the freeing of a believing slave. And whoever does not find [the means], then fasting of two months consecutive as a repentance from Allah.' (3) Expiation for zihar: Allah's saying 'And those who pronounce zihar among you of their wives and then go back on what they said, then [the penalty is] freeing a slave before they touch one another. ... And whoever does not find [the means], then fasting of two months consecutive before they touch each other. And whoever is unable, then feeding sixty poor persons.' (4) Expiation for an oath: Allah's saying 'But He will take you to account for the oaths which you have sworn, so its expiation is feeding ten poor persons from the average of what you feed your families or clothing them or freeing a slave. And whoever does not find [the means], then fasting of three days. That is the expiation of your oaths when you have sworn. And guard your oaths.' (5) Qada of Ramadan: Allah's saying 'And whoever is sick or on a journey, then a number of other days.' (6) Fasting of tamattu' and qiran: Allah's saying 'So whoever enjoys the Umrah to Hajj, then [he must offer] what is easy of the sacrificial animal. And whoever cannot find [a sacrificial animal], then fasting of three days in Hajj and seven when you return; those are ten complete.' (7) Fasting of shaving the head: Allah's saying 'So whoever among you is ill or has an ailment of the head, then a ransom of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' (8) General recompense for hunting: Allah's saying 'O you who believe! Do not kill game while you are in ihram. And whoever among you kills it intentionally, then the penalty is an equivalent from the grazing animals as judged by two just men among you as an offering reaching the Kaaba, or an expiation of feeding poor persons or the equivalent of that in fasting, that he may taste the consequence of his deed.' Among these, the first four require consecutive and uninterrupted performance, and in the last four, there is choice: if he wishes, he may perform them separately, and if he wishes, consecutively without interruption. In fasting of Ramadan, there is no dispute about the obligation of consecutive and continuous observance. And besides that, the scholars have stated a principle: wherever freeing a slave is prescribed, there consecutive observance in fasting is a condition; and wherever freeing a slave is not prescribed, consecutive observance in fasting is not a condition. So under this principle, in the Holy Quran where qada of Ramadan is mentioned...
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling that qada of Ramadan fasts can be performed consecutively or separately, as the Quranic text is absolute (mutlaq) without requiring either. However, it is mustahabb (recommended) to perform them consecutively to discharge the obligation quickly. The commentator then enumerates eight types of fasts from the Quran with their verses. The first four (Ramadan, expiation for killing, zihar, and oath) require consecutive fasting (tawabi') because they involve an alternative of freeing a slave. The last four (qada of Ramadan, tamattu'/qiran, shaving head, hunting recompense) do not require consecutiveness. The scholars derive a general principle: wherever the obligation of freeing a slave ('itq raqaba) is prescribed as an alternative in the same verse, the fasting option must be consecutive; otherwise, it is not required. This principle helps determine the rule for various fasting obligations. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the principle is clear.

Key Terms
متابعت (mutaba'ah): Performing fasts consecutively without interruption.
نص مطلق (nass mutlaq): An absolute text of the Quran or Sunnah that does not specify a restriction.
عتق رقبہ ('itq raqaba): Freeing a slave; an alternative expiation in certain kaffarat.
تابع (tabi'): Consecutive, unbroken sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle stated in the passage, which of the following fasts requires consecutive observance?
A) Qada of Ramadan
B) Fasting for tamattu' Hajj
C) Expiation for zihar
D) Fasting for shaving the head

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows qada of Ramadan to be performed separately or consecutively, and consecutiveness is required only when the verse also offers freeing a slave as an alternative.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Qada of Ramadan Need Not Be Consecutive
Refuting objections that qada must be consecutive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on consecutiveness in qada of Ramadan, identify the primary and secondary proofs, and evaluate the objections.

Core Idea
Qada of Ramadan does not require consecutive fasting; the Qur'anic text is absolute and a hadith analogy permits separate repayment.

This lesson addresses a common concern: must missed Ramadan fasts be made up consecutively? The Hanafi school holds that consecutiveness is not a condition, though it is recommended. We will examine the evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and then see how the Hanafi jurists refute two key objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position on consecutiveness (tataabu') in qada of Ramadan. Is it wajib or mustahabb?
The ruling is found at the end of the passage: continuity is not a condition but is mustahabb.
2
Examine the Primary Proof
Analyze the Qur'anic verse 'fa'iddatun min ayyamin ukhara' (2:184). Why does its absoluteness support separate performance?
The verse does not mention consecutiveness, so it is not a condition.
3
Analyze the First Objection and Refutation
The first objection argues that qada, as a substitute for the consecutive Ramadan fasts, must itself be consecutive. How does the Prophet's hadith on debt repayment refute this?
The hadith analogizes qada to repaying a debt in installments, showing consecutiveness is not required.
4
Analyze the Second Objection and Refutation
The second objection cites Ubayy ibn Ka'b's qira'ah adding 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive). Why is this qira'ah not accepted as a binding addition?
The qira'ah is at the level of khabar wahid, which cannot add to the established Qur'anic text.
5
Conclude with the Recommended Practice
Although continuity is not obligatory, the author recommends it for hastening the fulfillment of the obligation. Understand the difference between wajib and mustahabb.
The ruling balances flexibility with encouragement to act promptly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس جگہ عتق رقبہ کی مشروعیت بیان نہیں کی گئی ہے یعنی ایسا نہیں ہے کہ قضاء رمضان کی جگہ عتق رقبہ کافی ہو جائے لہذا قضاء رمضان کے روزوں میں متابعت اور تسلسل واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص ( فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ اُخَرَ ) مطلق ہے پس اسکے اطلاق کی وجہ سے نہ تابع شرط ہے اور نہ عدم تابع بلکہ اختیار ہو گا خواہ تابع کے ساتھ ادا کرے خواہ بغیر تابع کے ادا کرے۔
یہاں دو سوال ہیں ایک یہ کہ قضاء ادا کا خلیفہ ہوتا ہے اور ادا صوم رمضان میں تابع واجب ہے لہذا اس کے خلیفہ یعنی قضا ، صوم رمضان میں بھی تتابع واجب ہونا چاہیے دوسرا سوال یہ ہے کہ حضرت ابی بن کعب کی قرآت ہے فَعِدَةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أَخَرَ متتابعات پس جس طرح کفارہ یمین میں عبداللہ بن مسعودؓ کی قرآت متابعات کا اعتبار کیا ہے اسی طرح قضاء رمضان میں ابی بن کعب کی قرآت متتابعات کا اعتبار کرنا چاہنے پہلے سوال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم سے ایک صاحب نے قضا ، رمضان کو متفرق طور پر ادا کرنے کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تھا تو آپ نے فرمایا ذَالِکَ إِلَيْكَ اَرانَيْتَ لَوَكَانَ عَلى أَحَدِكُمْ دَيْنُ فَقَضَاء الدرهم والدرهمين ألم يَكُن فَضَاء قَالَ نَعَمْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلامُ فَالله أحق أن يَعْفُوَ وَيَغْفِرُ یعنی آپ نے فرمایا کہ تجھ کو اس کا اختیار ہے پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اچھا یہ بتلا ؤ اگر تم میں سے کسی پر قرضہ ہو اور وہ ایک ایک درہم اور دودو در ہم ادا کرے تو کیا یہ ادا ئیگی نہیں ہوگی سائل نے کہا کہ بلاشبہ ادا ئیگی ہو جائی گی پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اللہ زیادہ لائق ہے کہ وہ اپنا حق معاف کر دے اور درگذر کر دے مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب بندہ اپنا قرضہ متفرق طور سے وصول کر سکتا ہے تو اللہ کا قرضہ اگر متفرق طور سے ادا کیا گیا تو کیوں ادا نہیں ہو گا اب آپ ملاحظہ کریں کہ اگر معاملہ وہ ہوتا جو تم نے ذکر کیا ہے یعنی قضاء رمضان میں تابع کا شرط ہونا تو رسول خدا یہ جواب نہ دیتے جو سائل کو دیا ہے دوسرے سوال کا جواب یہ کیسے ابی ابن کعب کی قرات اس درجہ مشہور نہیں ہے جس درجہ میں ابن مسعود کی قرآت مشہور ہے پس ابی بن کعب کی قرآت خبر واحد کے مرتبہ میں ہوئی اور خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی نہیں کی جاتی ہے اس لئے ابی بن کعب کی قرآت متابعات سے کتاب ! فَعِدَّةٌ یعنی فعد لا من ايام اخر پر زیادتی نہیں کی جائے گی صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قضاء رمضان میں تابع اگر چہ شرط نہیں ہے لیکن مستحب ضرور ہے تا کہ واجب ادا کرنے میں مسارعت ہو جائے۔
Here the legislation of freeing a slave is not mentioned, meaning it is not the case that freeing a slave suffices in place of qada of Ramadan. Therefore, continuity (mutaba'at) and consecutiveness are not obligatory in the qada of Ramadan fasts. The second proof is that the text (فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ اُخَرَ) is absolute, so due to its absoluteness, neither is continuity a condition nor is discontinuity; rather, there is choice: whether one performs it with continuity or without continuity. There are two questions here: First, that qada is a successor of ada (original performance), and in ada of Ramadan fasts, continuity is obligatory, so in its successor, i.e., qada, continuity should also be obligatory. Second, that the qira'ah of Sayyiduna Ubayy ibn Ka'b is فَعِدَةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أَخَرَ متتابعات, so just as in kaffarah yamin, the qira'ah of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (ر) 'mutabi'at' is considered, similarly, in qada of Ramadan, the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b 'mutatabi'at' should be considered. The answer to the first question is that once a person asked the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) about performing qada of Ramadan separately, so he said: That is up to you. He then said: Tell me, if one of you had a debt and he repaid it one dirham and two dirhams at a time, would that not be repayment? The questioner said: Yes, indeed. He (ﷺ) said: Allah is more deserving that He should pardon and forgive. The meaning is that when a servant can recover his debt in separate installments, then why should Allah's debt not be accepted if paid separately? Now you see that if the matter were as you mentioned, i.e., continuity being a condition in qada of Ramadan, then the Messenger of Allah would not have given this answer to the questioner. The answer to the second question is that the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b is not as famous as the qira'ah of Ibn Mas'ud. Thus, the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b is at the level of khabar wahid, and with khabar wahid, no addition is made to the Book of Allah. Therefore, from the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b 'mutatabi'at', no addition will be made to the Book (فَعِدَّةٌ). The author of Hidayah says: Although continuity is not a condition in qada of Ramadan, it is certainly mustahabb, so that there is haste in performing the obligatory act.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the issue of whether missed Ramadan fasts (qada) must be made up consecutively. The author first clarifies that the previous discussion about freeing a slave does not apply here; qada is not replaced by expiation. The primary evidence is the Qur'anic verse 'a number of other days,' which is absolute, allowing either consecutive or separate performance. Two objections are then raised and answered. The first objection argues that because the original Ramadan fasts are consecutive, their substitute (qada) should also be consecutive. The refutation is based on a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) analogized qada to repaying a debt in installments, implying no obligation of continuity. The second objection cites the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b adding 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive). The response is that this qira'ah is not as widely transmitted as the qira'ah of Ibn Mas'ud in kaffarah yamin; it is at the level of khabar wahid, which cannot add to the Qur'anic text. Therefore, the addition is not accepted. The passage concludes that while continuity is not obligatory, it is recommended (mustahabb) to hasten in fulfilling the obligation.

Key Terms
تتابع (tataabu'): Consecutiveness of fasts without interruption.
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed obligatory fasts after their prescribed time.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith transmitted by a single chain or a limited number of narrators, below the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it obligatory to perform the qada of Ramadan fasts consecutively?
A) Yes, it is obligatory because the original fasts are consecutive.
B) No, it is not obligatory, but it is recommended (mustahabb).
C) No, it is neither obligatory nor recommended.
D) Yes, it is obligatory based on the qira'ah of Ubayy ibn Ka'b.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, missed Ramadan fasts may be made up separately; consecutiveness is recommended but not required.
