Delaying Qada Until Next Ramadan: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on delaying qada to next Ramadan with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying qada to the next Ramadan, explain why no fidyah is required, and contrast the Hanafi position with that of the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Core Idea
Delaying qada to the next Ramadan does not incur fidyah because the obligation is on delay, not on immediacy.

The passage addresses a common scenario: a person owes missed Ramadan fasts but has not yet made them up when the next Ramadan arrives. The Hanafi school provides a clear sequence — fast the current Ramadan first, then make up the previous ones — and explains why no additional expiation (fidyah) is needed. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this ruling and contrasts it with the view of the other three schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school? Identify the sequence: fast the current Ramadan first, then make up the previous fasts. Note that no fidyah is required.
The obligation of qada is on delay (ala al-tarakhi).
2
Identify the opposing schools and their view
Which schools disagree? What is their ruling? They require both qada and fidyah for delay without excuse.
Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold this view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What evidence do the opposing schools cite? They rely on the hadith of Aisha (r) that qada should be completed by Sha'ban, implying a time limit.
This suggests that delaying beyond the interval between Ramadans is a violation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the opponent's evidence? The absolute command in the Quran does not specify a deadline; the hadith is about promptness, not a condition for fidyah. Fidyah is only for permanent incapacity (shaykh fani).
The Hanafi usul principle: absolute commands indicate delay (tarkhi), not immediacy (fawr).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? A Hanafi does not pay fidyah; a Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali must pay fidyah per missed fast if delay is without excuse.
This illustrates how usul differences lead to different fiqh rulings.

Source Text

اتنا قضا کو مؤخر کیا کہ دوسرا رمضان شروع ہو گیا تو دوسرے رمضان کے روزہ کو مقدم کرے اس کے بعد دوسرے روزوں کی قضاء کرے
وَإِنْ أَخَرَهُ حَتَّى دَخَلَ رَمَضَانَ آخَرُ صَامَ الثَّانِي لِأَنَّهُ فِي وَقَتِهِ وَقَضَى الأَوَّلَ بَعْدَهُ لِأَنَّهُ وَقْتُ الْقَضَاءِ وَلَا فِدْيَةٌ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ وُجُوبَ الْقَضَاءِ عَلَى التَّرَاحِي حَتَّى كَانَ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَطَوَّعَ
ترجمہ اور اگر قضاء کو مؤخر کیا یہاں تک کہ دوسرا رمضان آ گیا تو دوسرے رمضان کا روزہ ادا کرے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت میں ہے اور اول کی قضاء اس کے بعد کرے کیونکہ یہ زمانہ قضاء کا ہے اور اس پر فدیہ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ قضاء علی التراخی واجب ہے حتی کہ اس کے لئے نفل روزہ جائز ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس شخص پر رمضان کی قضا واجب ہے اگر اس نے قضاء کو مؤخر کیا یہاں تک کہ دوسرا رمضان آ گیا ہے تو دوسرے رمضان کے روزے رکھے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت میں ہیں اور اس دوسرے رمضان کا روزہ اس پر متعین ہے اس لئے اس میں کسی دوسرے روزہ کی گنجائش نہ ہوگی اور گذشتہ رمضان کے روزوں کی قضاء اس دوسرے رمضان کے بعد کرے ۔ کیونکہ یہ زمانہ بھی قضاء کا ہے اور اس تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس پر فدیہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی امام مالک اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اگر بغیر عذر تا خیر کی تو قضا بھی کرے اور ہر روزے کے بدلہ فدیہ بھی دے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء دور مضانوں کی درمیان کے ساتھ موقت ہے جیسا کہ حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے کہ رمضان میں پیش آمد ایام حیض یعنی رمضان کے فوت شدہ روزوں کی قضاء کو زیادہ سے زیادہ شعبان تک مؤخر کیا جا سکتا ہے لیکن جب شعبان تک قضاء نہیں کی بلکہ دوسرا رمضان آ گیا تو گویا اس نے قضاء کو اس کے وقت سے مؤخر کر دیا پس قضا ء کو اس کے وقت سے مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے فدیہ واجب کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے قضاء کا امر مطلق فرمایا ہے اور امر مطلق کا موجب علی الفور نہیں ہوتا بلکہ علی التراخی ہوتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے رمضان گزرنے کے بعد قضاء رمضان سے پہلے نفلی روزے رکھ لئے تو بالاتفاق جائز ہے اگر رمضان کی قضاء علی الفور واجب ہوتی تو بغیر قضاء رمضان کے نفلی روزے جائز نہ ہوتے پس جب قضاء رمضان علی التراخی واجب ہے تو زندگی میں مرنے سے پہلے پہلے جب چاہے قضاء کرلے پوری زندگی قضا کا وقت ہے۔
If he delays the qada until the next Ramadan enters, he fasts the second (Ramadan) because it is in its time, and he makes up the first after it because that is the time for qada. No fidyah is upon him because the obligation of qada is on delay (ala al-tarakhi), such that he may perform voluntary fasts. Translation: And if he delays the qada until another Ramadan comes, he performs the fast of the second Ramadan because it is in its time, and he performs qada of the first after it because that is the time for qada. No fidyah is upon him because the obligation of qada is on delay (ala al-tarakhi), such that voluntary fasts are permissible for him. Explanation of the issue: The person upon whom qada of Ramadan is obligatory, if he delayed the qada until the next Ramadan came, then he observes the fasts of the second Ramadan because they are in their time, and that second Ramadan is specified for him, so there is no room for any other fast in it. He makes up the missed fasts of the previous Ramadan after this second Ramadan, because this time is also for qada. And due to this delay, no fidyah is obligatory upon him. According to Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, if he delayed without an excuse, he still performs qada and also gives fidyah for each fast. Their evidence is that qada is temporally bound to the interval between Ramadans, as narrated from Aisha (r) that the qada of missed Ramadan fasts due to menstruation can be delayed at most until Sha'ban. But if he did not perform qada by Sha'ban and the next Ramadan came, it is as if he delayed the qada beyond its time; therefore, fidyah becomes obligatory due to delaying qada from its time. Our evidence is that Allah Most High commanded qada in absolute terms, and an absolute command does not necessitate immediacy (ala al-fawr) but rather indicates delay (ala al-tarakhi). This is why if someone, after Ramadan passes, performs voluntary fasts before performing qada of Ramadan, it is unanimously permissible. If qada of Ramadan were obligatory immediately (ala al-fawr), voluntary fasts would not be permissible before completing qada. Since qada of Ramadan is obligatory on delay (ala al-tarakhi), then during his life before death, whenever he wishes, he may perform qada; his entire life is the time for qada.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about delaying the qada of Ramadan until the next Ramadan. The Hanafi ruling: the person must first fast the present Ramadan because it is in its time, then make up the previous Ramadan's fasts. No fidyah (expiation) is required because the obligation of qada is on delay (ala al-tarakhi), meaning it can be done at any time before death. Evidence: the absolute command 'a number of other days' indicates delay, not immediacy; voluntary fasts are allowed before qada. The opposing view (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) holds that if one delays without excuse until the next Ramadan, fidyah is required for each missed fast. They cite the hadith of Aisha that qada should be done by Sha'ban, implying a time limit. The Hanafi response: the absolute command does not set a deadline; fidyah is only for the elderly who are permanently incapable, not for delaying.

Key Terms
علی التراخی (ala al-tarakhi): The obligation can be fulfilled at any time without immediate requirement.
فدیہ (fidyah): Monetary or food expiation for missed fasts when one is permanently unable to fast (e.g., elderly).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do if they have not made up missed Ramadan fasts and the next Ramadan arrives?
A) Fast the current Ramadan and then make up the previous ones, with no fidyah.
B) Fast the current Ramadan and make up the previous ones, and pay fidyah for each delayed fast.
C) Skip the current Ramadan to make up the previous ones first.
D) Only fast the current Ramadan and the previous ones are waived.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that qada of Ramadan is wajib on delay (ala al-tarakhi); delaying to the next Ramadan does not incur fidyah — one must fast the current Ramadan first, then make up the missed fasts.

Pregnant and Breastfeeding Women Breaking Fast: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on fidyah for pregnant/breastfeeding women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on fidyah for pregnant/breastfeeding women who break fast, and explain the Hanafi rationale based on the distinction between the shaykh fani and the child.

Core Idea
Fidyah for the shaykh fani is an exception; it cannot be analogized to a child who never had an obligation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the ruling for pregnant and breastfeeding women who break their Ramadan fast due to fear for themselves or their child. While all schools agree they must make up the fasts, a dispute arises regarding whether fidyah (compensatory feeding) is also required. The Hanafi school, represented in the text, firmly rejects fidyah, countering the Shafi'i analogy to the shaykh fani (elderly person). Understanding the precise legal reasoning, particularly the concept of khilaf al-qiyas (exception to analogy), is essential to grasp the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as presented in the passage: the pregnant/breastfeeding woman breaks the fast and makes up (qada) later; no kaffarah and no fidyah are required.
The ruling is based on removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) and the excuse being valid.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i agrees on breaking fast and qada, but adds fidyah when the fear is for the child, not for herself.
The dispute is specifically about fidyah, not about the permissibility of breaking fast.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school uses qiyas (analogy) to the shaykh fani: just as the elderly pay fidyah for missed fasts due to permanent incapacity, so too should the woman who cannot fast due to fear for her child.
The analogy assumes the woman's situation is similar to the shaykh fani's.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The fidyah for the shaykh fani is itself an exception to the general rule (khilaf al-qiyas), so it cannot be extended by qiyas. (2) The analogy fails because the shaykh fani became incapable after the obligation was established, while the child never had any obligation.
Thus, the 'illah (effective cause) is different.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, the woman only makes up the missed fasts. Under Shafi'i (if fear is for child), she also must pay fidyah (feed a poor person per day). The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
The difference affects financial obligation on the woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَالْحَامِلُ وَالْمُرضِعُ إِذَا خَافَتَا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمَا وَ وَلَدَيْهِمَا أَفَطَرَنَا وَ قَضَتَا دَفَعًا لِلْحَرج وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ عَلَيْهِمَا لِأَنَّهُ إقْطَارٌ بِعَذَرٍ وَلَا فِدْيَةٌ عَلَيْهَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي فِيمَا إِذَا خَافَتْ عَلَى الْوَلَدِ هُوَ يَعْتَبِرُهُ بِالشَّيْخ الفَانِى وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْفِدْيَةَ بِخِلَافِ الْقِيَاسِ فِي الشَّيْخ الفَانِى وَالْفِطْرُ بِسَبَبِ الْوَلَدِ لَيْسَ فِي مَعْنَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ عَاجَزَ بَعْدَ الْوُجُوبِ وَالْوَلَدُ لَا وجُوبَ عَلَيْهِ أَصْلاً

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت اور دودھ پلانے والی عورت کو اگر روزہ کی وجہ سے اپنی جانوں کا خوف ہو یا اپنے بچوں کا خوف ہو یعنی حاملہ کو پیٹ کے بچہ کا خوف ہو اور دودھ پلانے والی کو دودھ پیتے بچہ کا خوف ہو تو یہ دونوں افطار کر لیں اور بعد میں ان روزوں کی قضاء کرین البتہ ان پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا افطار کی اجازت تو حرج دور کرنے کے لئے دی گئی ہے اور کفارہ اس لئے واجب نہیں ہے کہ ان دونوں کا افطار کرنا عذر کی وجہ سے ہے اور عذر کی وجہ سے افطار کرنا جنایت نہیں ہوتا پس جب افطار جنایت نہیں ہے تو اسکی وجہ سے کفارہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا ہمارے نزدیک ان دونوں پر فدیہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر حاملہ یا مرضعہ نے اپنے بچہ کے ضائع ہونے کے خوف کی وجہ سے روزہ افطار کیا ہے تو ان پر قضاء کے ساتھ فدیہ بھی واجب ہوگا حضرت امام شافعی اس کو شیخ فانی پر قیاس کرتے یعنی جس طرح شیخ فانی پر فدیہ واجب ہوتا ہے اس طرح ان پر بھی فدیہ واجب ہو گا صاحب عنایہ نے امام شافعی کی جانب سے ایک
The pregnant woman and the breastfeeding woman, if they fear for themselves or their children, they break the fast and make up (the fasts), to remove hardship. There is no kaffarah upon them because it is breaking fast due to an excuse. And there is no fidyah upon her, contrary to Shafi'i in the case when she fears for the child; he analogizes her to the shaykh fani (elderly). Our evidence is that fidyah is contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas) in the case of the shaykh fani, and breaking fast due to the child is not similar in meaning because (the shaykh fani) became incapable after obligation, while the child had no obligation at all. Translation: And the pregnant woman and the breastfeeding woman, when both fear for their lives or for their children, both break the fast and make it up in order to remove hardship. There is no kaffarah upon them because this breaking of fast is due to an excuse. And there is no fidyah upon them. Imam Shafi'i differs in the case when she fears for the child. Imam Shafi'i analogizes her to the shaykh fani. Our evidence is that fidyah is contrary to analogy in the case of the shaykh fani, and breaking fast due to the child is not similar in meaning because the shaykh fani became incapable after the obligation, while the child had no obligation at all from the start. Explanation of the issue: If a pregnant woman or a breastfeeding woman fears for her own life due to fasting, or fears for her child—meaning the pregnant woman fears for the fetus, and the breastfeeding woman fears for the nursing child—then both break the fast and later make up those fasts. However, no kaffarah is obligatory upon them. Permission to break fast is given to remove hardship. Kaffarah is not obligatory because their breaking fast is due to an excuse, and breaking fast due to an excuse is not a sin. So when breaking fast is not a sin, kaffarah is not obligatory due to it. According to us, no fidyah is obligatory upon them either. Imam Shafi'i says: If a pregnant or breastfeeding woman broke her fast due to fear of harming her child, then along with qada, fidyah is also obligatory. Imam Shafi'i analogizes her to the shaykh fani, meaning just as fidyah is obligatory upon the shaykh fani, similarly fidyah will be obligatory upon them. The author of al-Inayah says, from Imam Shafi'i's side, one...
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning pregnant and breastfeeding women who break their fast due to fear for themselves or their child. The Hanafi position: they break the fast and later make up the missed days; no kaffarah and no fidyah. The reason is that breaking the fast is due to a valid excuse (darurah), not a sin. Imam Shafi'i agrees on breaking the fast and qada, but he adds that if the fear is for the child (not for herself), then fidyah is also required, analogizing the woman to the shaykh fani (an elderly person who cannot fast and must pay fidyah). The Hanafi rebuttal: the analogy fails because the shaykh fani became incapable after the obligation of fasting was established upon him, whereas the child never had any obligation. Moreover, fidyah for the shaykh fani is itself an exception to the general rule (khilaf al-qiyas), so it cannot be extended by qiyas to other cases. The passage concludes with a reference to al-Inayah continuing the rebuttal, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
شيخ فاني (shaykh fani): An elderly person who is permanently incapable of fasting and must pay fidyah (feeding a poor person per missed fast).
کفارہ (kaffarah): An expiatory fast (60 days) or other penalty for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensatory payment (feeding a poor person) for each missed fast, applicable to those permanently unable to fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a pregnant woman who breaks her fast due to fear for her child do?
A) She must pay kaffarah and make up the fasts.
B) She must make up the fasts and pay fidyah.
C) She must only make up the fasts; no kaffarah or fidyah.
D) She does not need to do anything; the fasts are waived.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require fidyah from pregnant or breastfeeding women who break fast, as the child never had an obligation, unlike the shaykh fani who became incapable after obligation.

The Hanafi Ruling on Fidyah for Delayed Qada of Ramadan Fasts
Dispute on whether delaying qada requires fidyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether fidyah is required for delaying qada of Ramadan fasts until the next Ramadan and explain the Hanafi proof based on the principle of al-amr bi al-mutlaq yufid al-tarākhī.

Core Idea
No fidyah for delayed qada; the absolute command for qada permits delay until death.

This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute about a common scenario: someone misses Ramadan fasts and delays making them up until the next Ramadan. Is fidyah required? The Hanafi school says no, based on the absolute nature of the command for qada. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools disagree. In this lesson, we will follow the Hanafi reasoning and see why the mufta bihi position is that no fidyah is necessary.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding fidyah for delaying qada. Note that it is not required; qada is on ease (alā al-tarākhī).
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools hold that fidyah is wajib if delay is without excuse. Their proof is the hadith of Aisha indicating that qada should be done before the next Ramadan.
The hadith is mentioned but not quoted verbatim in the passage.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opponent's hadith
The Hanafi response is that the hadith only recommends timing, not obligation. The absolute command in the Qur'an allows delay, so the hadith does not override that.
The Hanafi usul principle gives priority to the mutlaq command over hadith that is not definitively indicative of obligation.
4
Understand the Hanafi usul principle at work
The key principle is that an absolute command (amr mutlaq) indicates delayed compliance (al-tarākhī), not immediate (al-faur). This is a fundamental difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i usul.
Hanafi: al-amr bi al-mutlaq yufid al-tarākhī; Shafi'i: al-amr yufid al-faur.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi – no fidyah, full life to make up; other schools – fidyah wajib if delay beyond next Ramadan without excuse.
This difference matters in fatwa – the mufti must know which view is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گذشتہ رمضان کے روزوں کی قضاء اس دوسرے رمضان کے بعد کرے ۔ کیونکہ یہ زمانہ بھی قضاء کا ہے اور اس تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس پر فدیہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی امام مالک اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اگر بغیر عذر تا خیر کی تو قضا بھی کرے اور ہر روزے کے بدلہ فدیہ بھی دے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء دور مضانوں کی درمیان کے ساتھ موقت ہے جیسا کہ حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے کہ رمضان میں پیش آمد ایام حیض یعنی رمضان کے فوت شدہ روزوں کی قضاء کو زیادہ سے زیادہ شعبان تک مؤخر کیا جا سکتا ہے لیکن جب شعبان تک قضاء نہیں کی بلکہ دوسرا رمضان آ گیا تو گویا اس نے قضاء کو اس کے وقت سے مؤخر کر دیا پس قضا ء کو اس کے وقت سے مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے فدیہ واجب کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے قضاء کا امر مطلق فرمایا ہے اور امر مطلق کا موجب علی الفور نہیں ہوتا بلکہ علی التراخی ہوتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے رمضان گزرنے کے بعد قضاء رمضان سے پہلے نفلی روزے رکھ لئے تو بالاتفاق جائز ہے اگر رمضان کی قضاء علی الفور واجب ہوتی تو بغیر قضاء رمضان کے نفلی روزے جائز نہ ہوتے پس جب قضاء رمضان علی التراخی واجب ہے تو زندگی میں مرنے سے پہلے پہلے جب چاہے قضاء کرلے پوری زندگی قضا کا وقت ہے۔
The qada of the past Ramadan's fasts should be made after this second Ramadan. Because this time is also for qada, and due to this delay, fidyah will not be obligatory upon him. According to Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, if he delayed without an excuse, he must perform qada and also give fidyah for each fast. Their proof is that qada is time-bound between two Ramadans, as narrated from Aisha that the qada of missed fasts due to menstruation can be delayed until Sha'ban at most. But if he did not make qada by Sha'ban and the next Ramadan came, then he delayed it from its time, so fidyah becomes obligatory. Our proof is that Allah Ta'ala commanded qada absolutely, and an absolute command does not indicate immediate compliance (faur) but rather delayed (al-tarākhī). For this reason, if someone missed Ramadan and gave supererogatory fasts before making qada, it is unanimously permissible; if qada were immediate, supererogatory fasts would not be allowed. Thus, since qada is delayed, one can make it at any time before death; the whole life is the time for qada.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of fidyah when one delays making up missed Ramadan fasts until the next Ramadan. The Hanafi position is that no fidyah is required; qada is on ease (tarākhī) and can be done at any time before death. The opposing schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) argue that qada must be done before the next Ramadan, and delay without excuse necessitates fidyah. The Hanafis respond by noting that the Quranic command for qada is absolute, and an absolute command in their usul indicates permissibility to delay (al-amr bi al-mutlaq yaffi al-tarākhī). They support this by the ruling that supererogatory fasts are allowed before qada, which would not be the case if qada were immediate. The hadith of Aisha only recommends delay until Sha'ban but does not make it binding. Hence, the Hanafi view is that no fidyah is needed. The mufta bihi position is that of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قضاء (qadā): Making up missed obligatory acts of worship after their time has passed.
علی التراخی (alā al-tarākhī): A principle in Hanafi usul that an absolute command implies permissibility of delayed compliance, not immediate.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensatory payment given instead of fasting by those permanently unable to fast, e.g. elderly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on paying fidyah if one delays making up missed Ramadan fasts until the next Ramadan without an excuse?
A) Fidyah is wajib for each delayed fast.
B) Fidyah is not wajib; qada can be delayed at any time.
C) Fidyah is wajib only if the delay is intentional.
D) Fidyah is wajib but only for women.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, delaying qada of Ramadan fasts until after the next Ramadan does not incur fidyah because the command for qada is absolute, allowing delay for one's entire lifetime.

Pregnant and Nursing Women Breaking Fast: Fidyah or Not?
Dispute on whether fidyah applies to pregnant/nursing women who break fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for pregnant/nursing women who break fast and explain why the Shafi‘i analogy to the elderly fails.

Core Idea
Fidyah for the elderly is an exception; analogizing temporary excuses to permanent inability is invalid.

The Hanafi school permits pregnant and nursing women to break fast out of fear for themselves or their child, requiring only qada later. But should they also pay fidyah like the elderly who cannot fast? The Hanafis say no, while Imam Shafi‘i says yes. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and why the analogy to the elderly (shaykh fani) is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage to see the two distinct situations: when the women fear for themselves vs. when they fear for the child. Note that the dispute is only about the latter.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules: no kaffarah, no fidyah; only qada is wajib. The reason: breaking due to an excuse is not sinful, so no expiation.
3
Understand the Shafi‘i argument
Imam Shafi‘i analogizes the women to the elderly (shaykh fani) who must pay fidyah. He sees a common benefit (the child) as the illa.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: (a) fidyah for the elderly is a textual exception, not open to qiyas; (b) the elderly was obligated then became incapable, while the child never had an obligation at all – so the analogy fails.
This is a classic Hanafi usul move: restricting exceptions to their textual scope.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Hanafi: no fidyah; Shafi‘i: fidyah wajib when fear is for the child. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text

اور بچہ کی وجہ سے افطار کرنا اس کے معنی میں نہیں ہے کیونکہ شیخ فانی وجوب کے بعد عاجز ہوا ہے اور بچہ پر سرے سے وجوب ہی نہیں ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاملہ عورت اور دودھ پلانے والی عورت کو اگر روزہ کی بھی نہیں ہے تو شیخ فانی کا حکم حاملہ اور مرضعہ کے حق میں دلالہ بھی ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
Pregnant and nursing women, if they fear for themselves or their children, they break the fast and make it up, to remove hardship. There is no kaffarah upon them because this breaking is due to an excuse, and no fidyah upon them, contrary to al-Shafi'i when they fear for the child—he analogizes them to the elderly shaykh fani. Our proof is that fidyah is contrary to qiyas for the shaykh fani, and breaking fast due to the child is not analogous because the shaykh fani became incapable after obligation, while the child had no obligation at all. Translation: And a pregnant woman and a breastfeeding woman, when both fear for their own lives or their children, they break the fast and make it up, to remove hardship. There is no kaffarah upon them because this breaking is due to an excuse, and no fidyah upon them. Imam Shafi'i has a disagreement in this case when they fear for the child; he analogizes them to the senile old man. Our proof is that fidyah for the senile old man is contrary to qiyas, and breaking fast due to the child is not analogous because the senile old man became incapable after obligation, and the child had no obligation at all. Explanation: The matter is that a pregnant woman and a nursing woman, if they fear for their lives due to fasting, or fear for their children (pregnant woman fears for the fetus, nursing woman fears for the nursing child), then both break the fast and later make up those fasts. However, no kaffarah is obligatory upon them; the permission to break was given to remove hardship, and kaffarah is not obligatory because their breaking is due to an excuse, and breaking due to an excuse is not a crime. So when breaking is not a crime, kaffarah is not obligatory. According to us, no fidyah is obligatory upon them either. Imam Shafi'i says that if a pregnant or nursing woman broke the fast due to fear of harm to her child, then fidyah is also obligatory along with qada. Imam Shafi'i analogizes them to the senile old man—just as fidyah is obligatory on the senile old man, similarly it would be obligatory on them. The author of 'Uyūn (?) stated a proof from Imam Shafi'i: that in the breaking of the fast by the pregnant and nursing women, there is benefit both for themselves and for their children. So considering their own benefit, qada is made obligatory, and considering the benefit of the children, fidyah is made obligatory. Our proof is that fidyah for the senile old man is proven by text contrary to qiyas, so it is not correct to analogize another case to it. And the breaking of fast by the pregnant or nursing woman due to the child is not similar to the senile old man because the senile old man became incapable after the obligation of fasting, while the child never had any obligation at all. Since breaking due to the child is not in the same category as the senile old man, the ruling of the senile old man cannot be applied to the pregnant and nursing woman.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding whether pregnant and nursing women who break the fast due to fear for themselves or their child must pay fidyah in addition to qada. The Hanafi position is clear: they break the fast out of necessity, make it up later, but no kaffarah or fidyah is required. The reason is that breaking the fast due to an excuse is not a sin, so no expiation. Imam Shafi'i analogizes these women to the elderly person (shaykh fani) who cannot fast and must pay fidyah. The Hanafi response is that fidyah for the elderly is an exception to qiyas, proven only by a specific Quranic verse, and therefore cannot be extended analogically. Furthermore, the situation is fundamentally different: the elderly person was obligated to fast and then became incapable, while the child (for whose sake the woman breaks) was never obligated. Hence, the analogy fails. The Hanafi view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
حاملہ (ḥāmilah): Pregnant woman.
مرضعہ (murḍiʿah): Woman who is breastfeeding a child.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation payment for missed fasts when one cannot fast permanently.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on fidyah for a pregnant woman who breaks her fast due to fear for her fetus?
A) She must give fidyah for each day.
B) She must give fidyah only if she also fears for herself.
C) She does not owe fidyah; only qada.
D) She owes fidyah like an elderly person.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, pregnant and nursing women who break fast due to fear for self or child owe only qada, not fidyah, because fidyah is a textual exception limited to permanent incapacity.

Ruling on the Elderly (Shaykh Fani) Who Cannot Fast
Definition and ruling of shaykh fani: fidyah is wajib, not qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the shaykh fani and explain the Quranic proof and the refutation of the Maliki/Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The permanently incapable elderly must pay fidyah – permanent excuse substitutes the obligation, not qada.

This lesson addresses a common question: what should an elderly person who can never fast do? The Hanafi school answers with a clear ruling: fidyah is wajib. But not all schools agree. By studying this passage from Al-Hidayah, you will understand the proof from the Quran and how the Hanafis defend their position against the objections of Imam Malik and a view of Imam Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for the shaykh fani as given in the text: he does not fast but gives fidyah each day.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam Malik and one opinion of Imam Shafi'i hold that no fidyah is owed.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand their reasoning: if fasting is not obligatory on the shaykh fani, its substitute cannot be obligatory.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi school responds: the obligation of fasting arises from witnessing the month, which applies to all; the permanent excuse does not remove obligation but substitutes it with fidyah, analogous to the deceased.
The key difference is permanent vs. temporary excuse.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi says fidyah wajib; Maliki/Shafi'i says no fidyah.

Source Text

فَدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مِسْكَيْن قِيلَ مَعَاهُ لَا يُطِيقُونَهُ وَلَوْ قَدَرَ عَلى الصّوْمِ يَبْطُلُ حُكم الْفِدَاءِ لِأَنَّ شَرْطَ الْخَلِيفَةِ إِسْتِمْرَارُ الْعِجْرَ ترجمہ اور وہ بوڑھا کھوسٹ جو روز و ر کھنے پر قادر نہیں ہے وہ افطار کرے اور مردان کے واسطے ایک مسکین کوکھانا دے جیسا کہ کفارات میں دیا جاتا ہے اور اصل اس بارے میں باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَعَلَى الذِينَ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مِسکین ہے کیا گیا ہے کہ اس کے معنی لا يطيقُونَہ کے ہیں اور اگر روزہ پر قادر ہو گیا تو فدیہ کا حکم باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ خلیفہ ہونے کی شرط دائمی بجز ہے۔ تشریح شیخ فانی سے مراد وہ بوڑھا کھوسٹ آدمی ہے جو روز و ر کھنے پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ اور فانی اس لئے کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ فتاء سے قریب ہو گیا یا یہ کہ اس کی قوت فناء ہو گئی ہے شیخ فانی کے بارے میں ہمارا مذہب یہ ہے کہ وہ روزہ نہ رکھے اور ہر روزہ کے بدلے فدیہ دیدے جیسا کہ کفارات میں فدیہ دیا جاتا ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر فدیہ واجب نہیں ہے یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے مبینہ میں اصل تو روزہ تھا لیکن شیخ فانی پر روزہ واجب نہیں ہے پس جب روزہ واجب نہیں ہے تو اس کا خلیفہ یعنی فدیہ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ روزہ رمضان واجب ہونے کا سبب شہود شہر ہے اور شہود شہر جس طرح قادر علی الصوم کے حق میں پایا گیا اسی طرح شیخ فانی کے حق میں بھی پایا گیا لیکن بڑھاپے کے عذر کی وجہ سے اس کے واسطے افطار کو مباح کر دیا گیا ہے اور عذر بھی ایسا ہے جس کے زائل ہونے کا امکان نہیں ہے اگر عذر کے زوال کا امکان ہوتا تو قضاء واجب کر دی جاتی جیسے مریض اور مسافر پر قضا واجب ہوتی ہے پس جب شیخ خانی روزہ رکھنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اور عذر کے عدم زوال کی وجہ سے قضاء بھی واجب نہیں کی جاسکتی تو فدیہ واجب ہوگا جیسے کسی پر روزہ واجب ہو اور وہ مر گیا تو اس پر فدیہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس بارے میں اصل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مِسْكِين ہے مفسرین نے کہا کہ اس کے معنی لَا يُطِيقُونَہ کے ہیں یعنی جو لوگ روزہ کی طاقت نہ رکھتے ہوں یعنی شیخ فانی ہوں ان پر فدیہ واجب ہے جیسے باری تعالى كا قول بين اللهُ لَكُمْ أَنْ تَضِلُّو اعنى أَن لَّا تَضِلُّوا اللہ تمہارے واسطے بیان کرتا ہے تا کہ تم نہ بجنک سکو اس آیت سے استدلال پر ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ جب یہ آیت نازل ہوئی تو مالدار لوگ روزہ نہیں رکھتے تھے بلکہ روزوں کا فدیہ دیتے تھے اور فقرا ء روزے رکھتے تھے اور
The senile old man who is unable to stand (fast) breaks the fast and feeds one poor person for each day, as fed in expiations. The basis for this is the saying of Allah Ta'ala: 'And upon those who are able to fast, a fidyah of feeding a poor person.' It is said that its meaning is 'those who are not able' (la yutiqunahu). And if he becomes able to fast, the ruling of fidyah becomes invalid because the condition of the substitute is the continuance of incapacity. Translation: And that decrepit old man who is not able to fast breaks his fast and feeds one poor person, as fed in expiations. The basis in this matter is the saying of Allah Ta'ala: 'And upon those who are able, a fidyah of feeding a poor person.' It is said that its meaning is 'those who are not able.' And if he becomes able to fast, the ruling of fidyah becomes invalid because the condition of the substitute is the continuance of incapacity. Explanation: Shaykh fani refers to that decrepit old man who does not have the ability to fast. He is called fani because he is close to annihilation (fana) or because his strength has perished. Our madhhab regarding shaykh fani is that he should not fast and should give fidyah for each day, as fidyah is given in expiations. Imam Malik said that fidyah is not wajib upon him, and this is also one saying of Imam Shafi'i. Imam Malik's proof is that the original obligation in Ramadan is fasting, but fasting is not wajib upon the shaykh fani; so when fasting is not wajib, its substitute (fidyah) should not be wajib either. Our response is that the cause for fasting being wajib is witnessing the month (shahud al-shahr), and this cause applies to the shaykh fani as well as to one who is able. However, due to the excuse of old age, breaking the fast is made permissible for him, and this excuse is one that has no possibility of removal. If removal were possible, qada would be made obligatory, as for the sick and traveler. So when the shaykh fani is not able to fast and qada cannot be made obligatory due to the permanence of the excuse, then fidyah becomes wajib, just as when fasting becomes obligatory on someone who dies, fidyah becomes wajib upon them. The author of Hidayah says that the basis for this is the verse: 'And upon those who are able, a fidyah...' The commentators said its meaning is 'those who are not able,' i.e., the shaykh fani, so fidyah is wajib. Just as Allah says 'Allah makes clear for you that you not stray' meaning 'lest you stray.' There is an objection regarding this verse: when it was revealed, the wealthy people did not fast but gave fidyah, while the poor fasted... (text cuts off)
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage defines the shaykh fani (incapacitated elderly person) and the Hanafi ruling that he must give fidyah instead of fasting, and no qada is required because his condition is permanent. The basis is the Quranic verse (2:184) interpreted by the Hanafi school as referring to those who cannot fast, not those who can. The passage also presents a dispute with Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i (in one view), who argue that fidyah is not wajib because the shaykh fani is not obliged to fast, so no substitute is needed. The Hanafi response is that the obligation of fasting is triggered by witnessing the month, which applies to everyone, but the excuse of permanent incapacity replaces the obligation with fidyah. If the incapacity were temporary, qada would be required, but here it is permanent, so fidyah substitutes. The author of Al-Hidayah explains the verse and notes a historical context that the early Muslims had a choice between fasting and fidyah, but the verse was later abrogated except for the permanently unable. The passage ends with an objection about the abrogation, but it is incomplete.

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fānī): An elderly person who is physically incapable of fasting due to advanced age or debility, with no hope of recovery.
فدیہ (fidyah): Feeding one poor person per missed fast as a substitute.
قضاء (qadā): Making up missed obligatory fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for an elderly man who is permanently unable to fast?
A) He must fast when he can and make up missed days later.
B) He is excused and owes nothing.
C) He must give fidyah (feed a poor person for each missed day).
D) He must fast regardless of ability.

Key Takeaway
A permanently incapable elderly person must give fidyah, not make up fasts, because the excuse is permanent.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Fidyah for the Decrepit Elderly (Shaykh Fani): Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Defines shaykh fani and rules on fidyah with Hanafi evidence against Malik and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for a shaykh fani, explain the evidence from Quran 2:184, and evaluate the Malik/Shafi'i objection using the concept of sabab (cause) of obligation.

Core Idea
Fidyah is wajib because the cause of obligation (witnessing the month) remains, even if the act itself is excused.

The passage from Al-Hidayah tackles a nuanced fiqh issue: what happens when an elderly person is permanently unable to fast? The Hanafi school rules that fidyah (feeding a needy person per day) becomes wajib, but Imam Malik and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i disagree. Understanding the reasoning behind this difference requires a careful analysis of the Quranic verse, the nature of excuses, and the concept of substitutes in Islamic law. In this lesson, we will dissect the Hanafi argument and its defense against the opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Define the shaykh fani and the basic ruling
Identify the exact definition given in the text: a decrepit old person who cannot fast and has no hope of recovery. State the Hanafi ruling: he does not fast and gives fidyah (feeding one needy person per day).
Note the quantity is same as kaffarah.
2
Examine the primary dalil from Quran
Locate the verse (2:184) and understand the interpretive move: the phrase 'yutīqūnahu' is taken to mean 'lā yutīqūnahu' (those who cannot fast), based on Arabic usage. Identify the thubut (qati) and dalala (zanni) to see why it yields wujub, not fard.
Similar linguistic example: 'an tadillū' meaning 'allā tadillū'.
3
Analyze the Malik/Shafi'i objection
State their proof: fasting is not obligatory on shaykh fani, so the substitute (fidyah) cannot be obligatory either. Understand their logical sequence: no asl → no khalifah.
This is the core inter-madhhab dispute.
4
Trace the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes between the cause (sabab) of obligation and the excuse that permits breaking the fast. The sabab (witnessing the month) is present for all; the excuse only removes the obligation to fast, but since it is permanent, qada is impossible, so fidyah substitutes. Compare with the case of a deceased person who had missed fasts.
Also address the abrogation objection: verse either specific to shaykh fani or remained in effect for the permanently unable after abrogation for others.
5
Apply the condition of permanent inability
The text concludes with a crucial sub‑ruling: if the shaykh fani later becomes able to fast, the fidyah becomes void and qada is obligatory. Recognize that the condition for fidyah is the continuity of inability.
This shows the substitute is contingent on the excuse being permanent.

گیا اور جب دائمی بھر نہیں پایا گیا تو فدیہ کا وجوب بھی ثابت نہیں ہوا اور جب فدیہ واجب نہیں ہوا تو ادا کیا ہوا فدیہ کان لم یکن کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا اور روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔
And the decrepit old man who cannot stand (to fast) breaks his fast and feeds a needy person for each day, as is fed in expiations. The basis for this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And upon those who are able to fast (i.e., find it difficult) – a ransom, feeding a needy person.' It is said its meaning is 'those who cannot fast.' And if he becomes able to fast, the ruling of the ransom becomes void, because the condition for the substitute is the continuity of inability. Explanation: By shaykh fani is meant the old, decrepit person who is not able to fast. It is called fani because he has approached annihilation or his strength has perished. Our school regarding shaykh fani is that he should not fast and give fidyah for each day, as fidyah is given in expiations. Imam Malik said that fidyah is not obligatory upon him, and this is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Malik's evidence is that originally fasting was the obligation in the month of Ramadan, but fasting is not obligatory upon shaykh fani. So when fasting is not obligatory, then its substitute, i.e., fidyah, should also not be obligatory. Our response is that the cause for the obligation of Ramadan fasts is witnessing the month, and witnessing the month is realized for the one able to fast just as it is realized for shaykh fani. However, due to the excuse of old age, breaking the fast is made permissible for him, and this excuse is one whose removal is not possible. If removal of the excuse were possible, qada would have been made obligatory, just as qada is obligatory upon the sick and traveler. So when shaykh fani is not able to fast and due to the permanent nature of the excuse qada cannot be made obligatory, then fidyah becomes obligatory, just as if a person had fasting obligatory upon him and died, then fidyah is obligatory upon him. The author of Hidayah says that the basis in this matter is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And upon those who are able – a ransom, feeding a needy person.' The commentators said its meaning is 'those who cannot fast,' i.e., shaykh fani, upon them fidyah is obligatory, like Allah's saying 'Allah makes clear to you that you not go astray.' An objection is raised on this argument: When this verse was revealed, wealthy people would not fast but would give fidyah, and poor people would fast. The reason was that in early Islam a person had a choice to fast or give fidyah. Then this choice was abrogated by Allah's saying 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it.' And using abrogated text as evidence is not permissible. The answer is that if this verse was revealed concerning shaykh fani, as the predecessors held, then there is no harm in using it as evidence. And if it was revealed concerning the choice between fasting and fidyah, then we say it was abrogated regarding the one able to fast, but remains in effect regarding shaykh fani, just as it was before abrogation. The author of Hidayah says: If shaykh fani gave fidyah without fasting and then became able to fast, the ruling of fidyah becomes void, because the condition for the substitute (i.e., fidyah) being obligatory is the continuity of inability. But when this person becomes able to fast, the continuity is not realized, so the obligation of fidyah is not proven. And when fidyah is not obligatory, the fidyah given becomes as if it never was, and qada of the fast becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah defines the shaykh fani (decrepit elderly person) and gives the Hanafi ruling on his obligation when unable to fast. The passage begins by stating the basic ruling: such a person does not fast and instead feeds a needy person for each missed day, with the same quantity as in kaffarah (expiation). The primary evidence is the Quranic verse 'And upon those who are able (yutīqūnahu), a ransom, feeding a needy person' (2:184), which the early commentators interpreted as 'those who cannot fast' (lā yutīqūnahu). The author then adds a condition: if the person later becomes able to fast, the fidyah becomes void because the substitute obligation (fidyah) requires permanent inability as a condition. The passage then presents a dispute with Imam Malik and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who hold that fidyah is not obligatory for shaykh fani because the original obligation of fasting itself is not upon him. The Hanafi response, following Abu Hanifa, is that the cause for obligation – witnessing the month – is present in both the capable and the incapable. The incapacity merely permits breaking the fast; if the incapacity is permanent, qada is impossible, so fidyah substitutes for it. The author then addresses an objection: the verse was abrogated by the later verse 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (2:185). The Hanafi answer is that the verse was either revealed specifically for shaykh fani (thus never abrogated for him) or, if it was about choice, it remained in effect for those permanently unable after abrogation for others. Finally, the passage concludes with a sub-ruling: if a shaykh fani gives fidyah and later regains ability, the fidyah is nullified and qada becomes obligatory because the condition of permanent inability was not fulfilled.

Key Terms
شيخ فاني (shaykh fānī): An elderly person who has become decrepit and is physically unable to fast, with no hope of recovery.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation for a missed obligatory fast, consisting of feeding one needy person per day (half sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley).
خلیفہ (khalīfah): Substitute; here referring to fidyah as the substitute for the missed fast, contingent on the continuity of the excuse.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the factor that triggers the legal obligation. Here, witnessing the month of Ramadan is the cause for the obligation of fasting.
عذر (‘udhr): Excuse; a valid reason that permits breaking a religious obligation without penalty, such as old age, illness, travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for fidyah to be obligatory upon a shaykh fani?
A) The person must be elderly and weak, even if the weakness is temporary.
B) The person must be permanently unable to fast, with no hope of recovery.
C) The person must have a medical certificate stating inability to fast.
D) The person must be wealthy enough to afford feeding the needy.

Key Takeaway
Fidyah is wajib for a shaykh fani because the cause of obligation (witnessing Ramadan) remains, and permanent inability shifts the obligation to a substitute.

The Necessity of a Will for Fidyah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on fidyah requiring a will, with Shafi'i opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires a will for fidyah on behalf of a deceased person and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Fidyah is an act of worship — without the deceased's will, the heir cannot perform it because worship requires personal choice.

When a Muslim dies with missed Ramadan fasts, can the heir give fidyah on their behalf? The Hanafi school holds that this is only possible if the deceased made a will, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and the practical consequence of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the text: if a person dies with missed Ramadan fasts and makes a will for fidyah, the heir must feed one poor person per missed day with specified amounts.
The text compares the deceased to the shaykh fani (elderly incapable of fasting).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i does not require a will; he analogizes fidyah to financial debts.
The text mentions that al-Shafi'i 'considers it by analogy to the debts of people.'
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: both fidyah and debts are financial rights in which deputyship (niyabah) is valid.
The Shafi'i view makes fidyah automatically transferable to the heir without the deceased's consent.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi counter: fidyah is an act of worship, not a financial debt, and worship requires the individual's own choice (ikhtiyar), which can only be expressed through a will.
Inheritance is compulsory and does not reflect the deceased's intention.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Hanafi, if no will exists, the heir has no obligation to give fidyah; under Shafi'i, the heir must give it regardless.
This difference affects estate planning and the discharge of religious obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And whoever dies while upon him is the qada of Ramadan, and he makes a will for it, his heir feeds for him for each day a needy person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, because he became incapable of performing (the fasts) at the end of his life, so he became like the shaykh fani. Then, according to us, a will is necessary, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And upon this (analogy) is zakat. And he (al-Shafi'i) considers it by analogy to the debts of people, because all of that is a financial right in which deputyship is effective. And our (Hanafi) evidence is that it is an act of worship, and choice is necessary therein, and that is in the will, not in inheritance, because inheritance is compulsory. Then it is a voluntary donation initially, so it is considered from the third (of the estate). And prayer is like fasting by istihsan of the mashayikh, and every prayer is considered equivalent to a day's fast; that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the ruling on a person who dies with missed Ramadan fasts (qada) and leaves a will regarding fidyah. The ruling states that the heir (wali) must feed one needy person for each missed day, with the same quantities as shaykh fani (half sa' of wheat, or one sa' of dates/barley). The reason given is that the deceased became unable to fast at the end of his life, thus analogous to the shaykh fani, for whom fidyah is prescribed. A critical condition is that the deceased must have made a will (wasiyyah) for this fidyah. This is the Hanafi position, and it differs from Imam al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'i school analogizes this to financial debts owed to people (duyun al-'ibad), where the heir can discharge the debt without a will because it is a financial right where deputyship (niyabah) is valid. The Hanafi response is that fidyah is an act of worship ('ibadah), and worship requires the intention and choice of the person being obligated. A will provides that choice; inheritance is compulsory (jabri) and cannot substitute for the deceased's personal intention. Therefore, without a will, the heir is not obliged to give fidyah. The passage further notes that the same dispute applies to zakat (if a person dies with unpaid zakat and makes a will). The mashayikh (early Hanafi scholars) applied istihsan to draw an analogy between prayer and fasting (i.e., both are acts of worship that cannot be performed by proxy without a will). The correct view is that each prayer is like a day's fast in this regard. This passage emphasizes the Hanafi principle that acts of worship cannot be performed by another person on behalf of the deceased unless explicitly authorized by the deceased's will.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will made by the deceased before death, authorizing the heir to perform a charitable act on their behalf.
نیابت (niyābah): Deputyship; the ability of one person to act on behalf of another in performing an obligation.
دیون العباد (duyūn al-‘ibād): Debts owed to people (financial obligations to others).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must a deceased person have made a will for the heir to give fidyah on their behalf?
A) Because it is a financial debt that needs documentation.
B) Because it is an act of worship that requires the deceased's own choice and intention.
C) Because the heir cannot give charity without the deceased's permission.
D) Because the Quran explicitly commands a will for all financial obligations.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fidyah for missed fasts of a deceased person is only obligatory on the heir if the deceased made a will, because worship requires personal choice.

Fidyah Void When Permanent Incapacity Ceases
Explains abrogation of fasting option and ruling for shaykh fani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a shaykh fani who pays fidyah and later regains fasting ability, and explain the role of permanent incapacity as a condition.

Core Idea
Fidyah is void if permanent incapacity ceases; qada becomes wajib.

This passage explains a specific ruling for the elderly who are permanently unable to fast. In early Islam, there was a choice between fasting and fidyah, but that was abrogated for those able to fast. However, for the shaykh fani, the original concession remains. Crucially, if a shaykh fani pays fidyah but later recovers the ability to fast, the fidyah becomes void and they must make up the fast (qada). This introduces a key condition: permanent incapacity is required for fidyah to be obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a shaykh fani who does not fast and pays fidyah, then regains ability. The ruling: fidyah is void, qada is wajib.
The ruling hinges on the condition of permanence.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (2:185) 'faman shahida minkumu al-shahra falyasumhu' is cited as proof for fasting obligation, abrogating the earlier option for those able.
The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in indication regarding the shaykh fani.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyasumhu' indicates wujub of fasting. For the shaykh fani, this imperative is inapplicable due to incapacity, so the original concession (fidyah) remains.
Abrogation only applies to those capable, not the permanently incapacitated.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may argue that the verse entirely abrogated the fidyah option for everyone. The Hanafi response distinguishes between capable and permanently incapacitated.
The Hanafi position is that the verse remains in effect for shaykh fani.
5
Derive the specific ruling
Since the obligation of fidyah is conditional on permanent incapacity ('adam al-qudra da'iman), when capacity returns the condition fails, so fidyah is void and qada becomes wajib.
This is a conditional ruling, not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجہ اس کی یہ تھی کہ ابتداء اسلام میں آدمی کو اختیار ہوتا تھا کہ وہ روزہ رکھے یا فدیہ دے پھر اس کے بعد یہ اختیار باری تعالیٰ کے قول فمن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرُ فَلْيَصُمُهُ کی وجہ سے منسوخ ہو گیا ہے اور منسوخ سے استدلال کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ آیت شیخ فانی کے حق میں نازل ہوئی ہے جیسے کہ اسلاف کی رائے ہے تو اس آیت سے استدلال کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اگر روز ہو اور قدید کے درمیان اختیار کے سلسلہ میں نازل ہوئی ہے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قادر علی الصوم کے حق میں منسوخ ہو گئی ہے لیکن شیخ فانی کے حق میں اپنے حال پر باقی ہے جیسا کہ منسوخ ہونے سے پہلے تھی۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر شیخ فانی نے روزہ نہ رکھ کر فدیہ ادا کر دیا پھر وہ روزے پر قادر ہو گیا تو فدیہ کا حکم باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ خلیفہ یعنی قد یہ [؟] واجب ہونے کی شرط دائمی [؟] ہے لیکن جب یہ شخص روزے پر قادر ہو گیا تو دائمی [؟] نہیں پایا گیا اور جب دائمی [؟] نہیں پایا گیا تو فدیہ کا وجوب بھی ثابت نہیں ہوا اور جب فدیہ واجب نہیں ہوا تو ادا کیا ہوا فدیہ کان لم یکن کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا اور روزہ کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔
The reason for this was that in early Islam, a person had the choice to fast or pay fidyah. Then this choice was abrogated by the verse 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it.' Arguing from an abrogated verse is not permissible. The answer is that if this verse was revealed concerning the shaykh fani (elderly person) as the predecessors held, then there is no harm in arguing from it. But if it was revealed concerning the choice between fasting and dried meat, we say it was abrogated for the one able to fast, but remains in effect for the shaykh fani as before abrogation. The author of al-Hidayah says: If a shaykh fani did not fast and paid fidyah, then later became able to fast, the ruling of the fidyah becomes void because the condition for its obligation is permanent incapacity. When the person became able to fast, permanent incapacity was not found, so the obligation of fidyah is not established. When fidyah was not obligated, the paid fidyah is considered as if not paid, and qada of the fast becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a shaykh fani (elderly person permanently incapable of fasting) who pays fidyah and later regains capacity. The author first discusses the abrogation of the original option to fast or pay fidyah (based on Surah al-Baqarah verse 185) and clarifies that this abrogation does not affect the shaykh fani, who remains liable for fidyah. Then the ruling: if such a person pays fidyah but subsequently becomes able to fast, the fidyah is void. The reason given is that the obligation of fidyah is contingent on permanent incapacity ('adam al-qudra da'iman). Once capacity returns, the condition no longer holds, so the fidyah was never properly obligated. Consequently, the fidyah is treated as if not paid, and the person must make up the fast (qada).

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): An elderly person who is permanently incapable of fasting.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation paid for missed fasts, typically feeding a poor person.
قضاء (qada): Making up missed obligatory fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a shaykh fani pays fidyah for a missed fast and then regains the ability to fast?
A) The fidyah remains valid and no qada is required.
B) The fidyah becomes void and qada is required.
C) Both the fidyah and qada are required.
D) The fidyah becomes a voluntary charity and qada is not required.

Key Takeaway
Fidyah is only wājib when permanent incapacity exists; if capacity returns, fidyah is void and qada of the fast becomes wājib.

Fidyah for Deceased and the Necessity of a Will
Inter-madhhab dispute on fidyah for deceased and necessity of will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of a will for fidyah payment, explain the Hanafi proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i/Maliki position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A will is necessary for heirs to pay fidyah because worship requires choice; inheritance is compulsory.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani presents the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for a deceased person who had missed Ramadan fasts. The key point of contention with Imam al-Shafi'i is whether a will is required for the heirs to be obliged to pay. The Hanafi school distinguishes acts of worship (ibadat) from financial debts, arguing that personal choice is essential for worship, and only a will provides that choice. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the proofs, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: if the deceased made a will for fidyah, the heirs must pay; if no will, they are not obliged. Payment is from one-third of the estate.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Malik) hold that a will is not necessary; heirs must pay fidyah and zakah regardless, from the entire estate.
Opposing school: Shafi'i/Malik
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They analogize (qiyas) fidyah/zakah to debts of people (duyun al-'ibad), arguing both are financial rights in which deputyship operates.
Their dalil: qiyas to debts
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: fidyah/zakah are acts of worship (ibadat) requiring personal choice (ikhtiyar), which is only present in a will, not in compulsory inheritance (jabriyyah). Therefore, analogy to debts is invalid.
Hanafi dalil: ibadat require choice
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi, if no will, heirs do not pay fidyah/zakah (though deceased may be sinful). In Shafi'i/Malik, heirs must pay regardless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس پر قضاء رمضان تھی وصیت کر کے فوت ہوا تو ولی اس کی جانب سے ہردن مسکین کو صدقہ فطر کے برابر قیمت دے
وَمَنَ مَاتَ وَعَلَيْهِ قَضَاءُ رَمَضَانَ فَأَوْصَى بِهِ أَطْعَمَ عَنْهُ وَلِيهِ لِكُلِّ يَوْمٍ مِسْكِينًا نِصْفَ صَاعٍ مِنْ بُرٍّ أَوْ صَاعًا مِنْ تَمْرٍ أَوْ شَعِيرٍ لِأَنَّهُ عَجَزَ عَنِ الْأَدَاءِ فِي آخِرِ عُمُرِهِ فَصَارَ كَالشَّيْخِ الْفَانِي ثُمَّ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْوَصِيَّةِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ وَعَلَى هَذَا الزَّكَاةُ وَهُوَ يُعْتَبِرُهُ بِدُيُونِ الْعِبَادِ إِذْ كُلُّ ذَلِكَ حَقٌّ مَالِيٌّ يَجْرِي فِيهِ النِّيَابَةُ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ عِبَادَةٌ وَلَا بُدَّ فِيهِ مِنَ الِاخْتِيَارِ وَذَلِكَ فِي الْوَصِيَّةِ دُونَ الْوَرَاثَةِ لِأَنَّهَا جَبْرِيَّةٌ ثُمَّ هُوَ تَبَرُّعٌ ابْتِدَاءً حَتَّى يُعْتَبَرَ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ وَالصَّلَاةُ كَالْقَوْمِ بِاسْتِحْسَانِ الْمَشَايِخِ وَكُلُّ صَلَاةٍ تُعْتَبَرُ بِصَوْمِ يَوْمٍ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
ر جو شخص مرنے لگا اور اس پر قضا رمضان واجب ہے پھر اس نے فدیہ کی وصیت کی تو اس کا ولی اس کی طرف سے ہر دن ایک مسکین کو نصف صاع گندم یا ایک صاع کھجور یا ایک صاع جو دے کیونکہ وہ اپنی عمر کے آخر میں روزہ ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا تو وہ شیخ فانی کے مانند ہو گیا پھر ہمارے نزدیک وصیت کرنا ضروری ہے امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اور زکوۃ بھی اسی اختلاف پر ہے امام شافعی اس قرینہ کو بندوں کے قرضوں پر قیاس کرتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ سب مالی حق ہیں جن میں نیابت جاری ہوتی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فدیہ دینا ایک عبادت ہے اور اس پر اختیار ضروری ہے اور یہ بات وصیت کرنے کی صورت میں حاصل ہے نہ کہ وراثت میں کیونکہ وراثت تو جبری ہے پھر وصیت کرنا ابتداء میں تبرع ہے حتی کہ تہائی مال سے اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور مشائخ کے استحسان سے نماز روزے کے مانند ہے اور ہر نماز ایک دن کے روزے کے برابر معتبر ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک ایسا آدمی جس پر قضاء رمضان کے روزے واجب ہیں مرنے کے قریب ہو گیا اس نے اپنے ورثہ کو فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کی تو اس کا ولی اس کی طرف سے ہر روزے کے واسطے ایک محتاج کو گندم کا آدھا صاع دیدے یا جو یا کھجور کا ایک صاع دیدے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب شخص آخری عمر میں قضاء کے روزے رکھنے سے عاجز ہو گیا تو شیخ فانی کے مانند ہو گیا پس جس طرح شیخ فانی پر ہر روزہ کا فدیہ واجب ہے اسی طرح اس پر بھی ہر روز کا فدیہ واجب ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے نزدیک وارث پر فدیہ کی ادائیگی کو لازم کرنے کے لئے مرنے والے کا وصیت کرنا ضروری ہے چنانچہ مرنے والے نے اگر وصیت نہ کی تو وارث پر اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنا لازم نہ ہو گا لیکن حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک وصیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ وارثوں پر اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنا لازم ہے خواہ مرنے والے نے وصیت کی ہو یا وصیت نہ کی ہو، یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے یہی اختلاف زکوۃ کے مسئلہ میں ہے عینی اگر کسی پر زکوۃ واجب ہے مگر ادا نہیں کی اور مر گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے مرنے سے پہلے اپنے وارثوں کو اپنی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کی ہے تب تو وارثوں کو اس کی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا کرنا لازم ہوگا ورنہ نہیں اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وارثوں پر اس کی طرف سے ہر حال میں زکوۃ ادا کرنا لازم ہے خواہ اس نے وصیت کی ہو یا وصیت نہ کی ہو۔ دوسرا اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک فدیہ ادا کرنے یا زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کو ایک تہائی مال سے نافذ کیا جائے گا اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک پورے مال سے نافذ کیا جائے گا یعنی امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک مرنے والے کی طرف سے فدیہ یا زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں اگر پورا مال ترکہ کا دینا پڑا تو پورا مال دیدیا جائے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک مال متروکہ کا صرف ایک تہائی دیا جا سکتا ہے پورا فدیہ یا پوری زکوۃ ادا ہو یا نہ ادا ہو۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فدیہ اور زکوۃ یعنی اللہ کے دین کو بندوں کے دین پر قیاس کیا ہے اور علت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مالی حق ہے اور دونوں میں نیابت جاری ہوتی ہے پس جس طرح مرنے والے کے پورے مال سے بندوں کا قرضہ ادا کیا جاتا ہے اگر چہ مرنے والے نے اس کی وصیت نہ کی ہو اسی طرح اس کے پورے مال سے اللہ کا قرضہ یعنی فدیہ اور زکوۃ ادا کی جائے گی اگر چہ اس نے وصیت نہ کی ہو۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فدیہ اور زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے اور جو چیز عبادت ہوتی ہے اس میں بندہ کا اختیار ضروری ہے اب ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ جب مرنے والے نے فدیہ یا زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کی ہے تو اس کا اختیار پایا گیا لیکن جب بغیر وصیت کے مر گیا تو مال وراثت میں اس کا اختیار باقی نہیں رہا کیونکہ مرنے کے بعد کوئی اختیار باقی نہیں رہتا اور مرنے کے بعد اختیار اس لئے باقی نہیں رہتا کہ وراثت خود ایک جبری (غیر اختیاری) چیز ہے چنانچہ اگر کوئی شخص مرتے وقت یہ کہے کہ میں ان وارثوں کو اپنا وارث نہیں مانتا تو اس کے مرنے کے بعد وہ لوگ وارث ہوں گے اور اگر کسی ایک وارث نے باقی دوسرے ورثہ کو کہا کہ تم تقسیم کر لو میں مال کا وارث نہیں ہوں گا تو یہ شخص اس کہنے سے وارث ہونے سے نہیں نکلے گا معلوم ہوا کہ وراثت جبری اور غیر اختیاری چیز ہے لہذا اگر مرنے والے نے وصیت کی ہوگی تو وارثوں پر تہائی مال سے اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنا لازم ہو گا ورنہ لازم نہ ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مرنے والے کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی یا زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا ابتداءً تبرع ہے اگر چہ آخرت میں اس چیز کا قائم مقام ہوگی جو میت پر واجب ہے یعنی روزہ اور زکوۃ کا قائم مقام ہوگی اور ابتداء تبرع اس لئے ہے کہ روزہ مکلف کا فعل ہوتا ہے اور موت کی وجہ سے تمام افعال ساقط ہو گئے ہیں پس گویا روزہ دنیا کے حق میں اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گیا اور جب دنیاوی حق میں روزہ ساقط ہو گیا تو ادائے فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا بھی تبرع ہو گا لیکن آخرت میں یہ فدیہ واجب یعنی روزہ کا عوض ہوگا بہر حال جب وصیت کرنا ابتداءً تبرع ہے تو اس کا نفاذ بھی تہائی مال سے ہوگا کیونکہ وصیت کا نفاذ تہائی مال سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور مشائخ نے استحساناً فرمایا ہے کہ نماز، روزے کے مانند ہے یعنی جس طرح موت کے بعد روزہ کا فدیہ دیا جا سکتا ہے اس طرح نماز
One upon whom qada of Ramadan was due, died after making a will, so his guardian gives on his behalf for each day a half sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley to a poor person. Because he became unable to perform it at the end of life, so he became like the shaykh fani. Then a will is necessary according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And on this is zakah. He (al-Shafi'i) analogizes it to debts of people, because all that is a financial right in which deputyship operates. Our proof is that it is an act of worship and choice is necessary in it, and that is found in the will not in inheritance because inheritance is compulsory. Then it is a donation initially, so it is considered from one-third. And prayer is like fasting by istihsan of the mashayikh; every prayer is considered equivalent to a day's fast – that is correct. A person who is near death and has qada of Ramadan, then he makes a will for fidyah: his guardian gives for each day half sa' wheat or one sa' dates or barley to a poor person. Because he became unable to fast at the end of his life, so he is like the shaykh fani. Then according to us, making a will is necessary; Imam al-Shafi'i differs. Zakath is also on this difference. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes this provision to debts of people, because all these are financial rights in which deputyship operates. Our proof is that giving fidyah is an act of worship, and choice is necessary in it. This is found in the will, not in inheritance because inheritance is compulsory. Then making a will is initially a donation, so it is considered from one-third of the estate. And by istihsan of the mashayikh, prayer is like fasting; every prayer is considered equivalent to a day's fast – that is correct. Explanation of the case: A person upon whom qada of Ramadan is due is near death; he makes a will to his heirs to give fidyah. Then his guardian gives for each fast a needy person half sa' wheat or one sa' barley or dates. The proof: when this person becomes unable at the end of life, he becomes like the shaykh fani, so fidyah is wajib for each day. The author of al-Hidayah says: According to us, the will of the deceased is necessary to obligate the heirs to pay fidyah; if no will, the heirs are not obligated. But Imam Shafi'i holds a will is not necessary; the heirs must pay whether or not a will was made – this is also Imam Malik's view. This difference also applies to zakah. If someone had zakah payable but did not pay and died, according to us if he made a will, the heirs must pay; if not, no obligation. According to Shafi'i and Malik, the heirs must pay in any case. A second difference: according to us, the will for fidyah or zakah is executed from one-third of the estate; according to them from the entire estate. Imam Shafi'i analogizes the debt to Allah to debts to people, since both are financial rights involving deputyship. Our proof: fidyah and zakah are worship, requiring choice. Choice is present with a will, not inheritance which is compulsory. So without a will, no payment is required. Also, the will is initially a donation, so it is from one-third. The author says the will to pay fidyah or zakah is initially a donation, though in the afterlife it becomes a substitute for what was obligatory. Initially a donation because fasting is an act of the mukallaf, and all actions cease with death; so the fast falls from the liability in worldly terms, making the will a donation. But in the afterlife, this fidyah becomes a compensation for the missed fast. Since the will is a donation, it is executed from one-third. The mashayikh ruled by istihsan that prayer is like fasting.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the obligation of a deceased person's fidyah for missed Ramadan fasts. The Arabic matn states: if someone dies with qada due and makes a will, the guardian feeds a poor person per day. The author then explains that the deceased is like a shaykh fani (elderly incapable of fasting) because of end-of-life incapacity. The Hanafi position requires a will (wasiyyah) for the heirs to be obliged to pay fidyah, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who analogizes it to debts, which are paid from the estate without a will. The Hanafi response distinguishes fidyah and zakah as acts of worship (ibadat) requiring personal choice (ikhtiyar), which is absent in compulsory inheritance but present in a will. Therefore, without a will, no obligation on heirs. Additionally, the will is executed from one-third of the estate (since it is a donation), not the whole estate like debts. The passage also mentions that the mashayikh (senior scholars) ruled by istihsan that prayers are analogized to fasting in this ruling: each missed prayer (when unable to perform) may be compensated by feeding a poor person, though the main text focuses on fasting.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation for missed fasts (or prayers) paid by feeding poor.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will or bequest made by the deceased.
عبادت (ibadah): Acts of worship requiring intention and personal performance.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a secondary source of law in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for heirs to be obligated to pay fidyah for a deceased person's missed Ramadan fasts?
A) A will (wasiyyah) from the deceased.
B) No special requirement; it is always obligatory.
C) The consent of the heirs.
D) The deceased must have explicitly stated the intention during life.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, fidyah for missed fasts is an act of worship requiring the deceased's choice, so a will is needed to obligate heirs; without it, the heirs are not responsible.

Sawm — Fasting

Fidyah and Zakat on Behalf of the Deceased: The Hanafi Requirement of a Will and One-Third Limit
Inter-madhhab dispute on requirement of wasiyyah and one-third limit for fidyah/zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for obligatory fidyah/zakat payment by heirs and contrast them with the Shafi'i/Maliki position using the concept of worship vs. financial rights.

Core Idea
Without a will, fidyah and zakat are not obligatory on heirs because worship requires personal choice, and inheritance is compulsory.

This passage examines a key difference between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools regarding the payment of fidyah for missed fasts and zakat on behalf of a deceased person. The Hanafi school holds that a will (wasiyyah) is required and that payment is limited to one-third of the estate, while the opposing schools require payment from the entire estate regardless of a will. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is essential for correctly applying these rulings in estate planning and fulfilling the deceased's obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two conditions for obligatory payment on heirs: the deceased must have made a wasiyyah, and payment is limited to one-third of the estate.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold that no wasiyyah is needed; payment is required from the entire estate in all cases.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing schools use qiyas on debts due to people: both are financial rights and deputyship (niyabah) is valid, so payment must be from the whole estate without a will.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes fidyah/zakat as acts of worship ('ibadah) requiring personal choice (ikhtiyar). After death, inheritance is compulsory (jabri), so without a will the heirs cannot be compelled to make a worship-related payment.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Hanafi fiqh, heirs may refuse payment if there is no will; in Shafi'i/Maliki, heirs must pay regardless.
