کتاب الصوم
فانی پر ہر روزہ کا فدیہ واجب ہے اسی طرح اس پر بھی ہر روز کا فدیہ واجب ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے نزدیک وارث پر فدیہ کی ادائیگی کو لازم کرنے کے لئے مرنے والے کا وصیت کرنا ضروری ہے چنانچہ مرنے والے نے اگر وصیت نہ کی تو وارث پر اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنا لازم نہ ہو گا لیکن حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک وصیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ وارثوں پر اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنا لازم ہے خواہ مرنے والے نے وصیت کی ہو یا وصیت نہ کی ہو ، یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے یہی اختلاف زکوۃ کے مسئلہ میں ہے عینی اگر کسی پر زکوۃ واجب ہے مگر ادا نہیں کی اور مر گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے مرنے سے پہلے اپنے وارثوں کو اپنی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کی ہے تب تو وارثوں کو اسکی طرف سے زکوۃ ادا کرنا لازم ہوگا ورنہ نہیں اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک وارثوں پر اس کی طرف سے ہر حال میں زکوۃ ادا کرنا لازم ہے خواہ اس نے وصیت کی ہو یا وصیت نہ کی ہو۔ دوسرا اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک فدیہ ادا کرنے یا ز کوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کو ایک تہائی مال سے نافذ کیا جائے گا اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک پورے مال سے نافذ کیا جائے گا یعنی امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک مرنے والے کی طرف سے فدیہ یاز کوۃ ادا کرنے میں اگر پورا مال ترکہ کا دینا پڑا تو پورا مال دیدیا جائے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک مال متروکہ کا صرف ایک تہائی دیا جا سکتا ہے پورا فدیہ یا پوری زکوۃ ادا ہو یانہ ادا ہو۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فدیہ اور ز کوۃ یعنی اللہ کے دین کو بندوں کے دین پر قیاس کیا ہے اور علت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مالی حق ہے اور دونوں میں نیابت جاری ہوتی ہے پس جس طرح مرنے والے کے پورے مال سے بندوں کا قرضہ ادا کیا جاتا ہے اگر چہ مرنے والے نے اس کی وصیت نہ کی ہو اسی طرح اس کے پورے مال سے اللہ کا قرضہ یعنی فدیہ اور زکوۃ ادا کی جائے گی اگر چہ اس نے وصیت نہ کی ہو ۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فدیہ اور زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے اور جو چیز عبادت ہوتی ہے اس میں بندہ کا اختیار ضروری ہے اب ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ جب مرنے والے نے فدیہ یا ز کوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کی ہے تو اس کا اختیار پایا گیا لیکن جب بغیر وصیت کے مر گیا تو مال وارثت میں اس کا اختیار باقی نہیں رہا کیونکہ مرنے کے بعد کوئی اختیار باقی نہیں رہتا اور مرنے کے بعد اختیار اس لئے باقی نہیں رہتا کہ وارشت خود ایک جبری ( غیر اختیاری ) چیز ہے چنانچہ اگر کوئی شخص مرتے وقت یہ کہے کہ میں ان وارثوں کو اپنا وارث نہیں مانتا تو اس کے مرنے کے بعد وہ لوگ وارث ہوں گے اور اگر کسی ایک وارث نے باقی دوسرے ورثہ کو کہا کہ تم تقسیم کر لو میں مال کا وارث نہیں ہوا ۔ تو یہ شخص اس کہنے سے وارث ہونے سے نہیں نکلے گا معلوم ہوا کہ وراثت جبری اور غیر اختیاری چیز ہے لہذا اگر مرنے والے نے وصیت کی ہوگی تو وارثوں پر تہائی مال سے اس کی طرف سے فدیہ ادا کرنالازم ہو گا ورنہ لازم نہ ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مرنے والے کا فدیہ ادا کرنے کی یا ز کوۃ ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا ابتداء تو تبرع ہے اگر چہ آخرت میں اس چیز کا قائم مقام ہوگی جو میت پر واجب ہے یعنی روزہ اور زکوۃ کا قائم مقام ہوگی اور ابتداء تبرع اس لئے ہے کہ روزہ مکلف کا فعل ہوتا ہے اور موت کی وجہ سے تمام افعال ساقط ہو گئے ہیں پس گویا روزہ دنیا کے حق میں اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گیا اور جب دنیاوی حق میں روزہ ساقط ہو جائی گا تو ادائے فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا بھی تبرع ہو گا لیکن آخرت میں یہ فدیہ واجب یعنی روزہ کا عوض ہوگا بہر حال جب وصیت کرنا ابتداء تبرع ہے تو اس کا نفاذ بھی تہائی مال سے ہوگا کیونکہ وصیت کا نفاذ تہائی مال سے ہوتا ہے۔
The book of fasting. For a deceased person, fidyah for each fast is obligatory. Similarly, for each day fidyah is obligatory. The author of Hidayah says: In our view, for making payment of fidyah necessary upon the heir, the deceased must have made a will. If the deceased did not make a will, the heir is not obligated to pay fidyah on his behalf. But according to Imam Shafi'i, making a will is not necessary; rather, the heirs are obligated to pay fidyah on his behalf whether the deceased made a will or not. This is also the statement of Imam Malik. The same difference exists in the matter of zakat: if zakat was obligatory on someone but he did not pay it and died, in our view the ruling is that if he made a will to his heirs to pay zakat on his behalf before death, then the heirs are obligated to pay zakat on his behalf; otherwise not. And according to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, the heirs are obligated to pay zakat on his behalf in all cases, whether he made a will or not. The second difference is that in our view, the will to pay fidyah or zakat will be executed from one-third of the estate, while according to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i it will be executed from the entire estate. That is, if paying fidyah or zakat on behalf of the deceased requires giving the entire estate, it will be given. And in our view, only one-third of the estate can be given, whether the full fidyah or zakat is paid or not. Imam Shafi'i analogized the debt due to Allah (fidyah and zakat) to the debt due to people, and the common cause is that both are financial rights and deputyship is valid in both. So just as the debt of people is paid from the entire estate of the deceased even if he did not make a will, similarly the debt due to Allah, i.e. fidyah and zakat, will be paid from his entire estate even if he did not make a will. Our proof is that fidyah and zakat are acts of worship, and in worship the choice of the servant is necessary. We see that when the deceased made a will to pay fidyah or zakat, his choice is found; but if he died without a will, his choice over the inherited property does not remain, because after death no choice remains. And choice does not remain after death because inheritance itself is a compulsory (non-optional) thing. So if a person says at the time of death, 'I do not consider these heirs as my heirs,' after his death they will still be heirs. And if one heir says to the other heirs, 'You divide it, I do not want to be an heir,' he does not cease being an heir by saying so. It is known that inheritance is compulsory and non-optional. Therefore, if the deceased made a will, it will be obligatory upon the heirs to pay fidyah on his behalf from one-third of the estate; otherwise it is not obligatory. The author of Hidayah says that the deceased's will to pay fidyah or zakat is initially a voluntary gift (tabarru'), although in the afterlife it will take the place of what was obligatory upon the deceased, i.e., it will take the place of fasting and zakat. And it is initially a voluntary gift because fasting is an act of the obligated person, and due to death all acts are waived. So fasting is waived from his liability in this world. And when fasting is waived from liability in this world, then making a will to pay fidyah is also a voluntary gift. But in the afterlife this fidyah will be obligatory, i.e., a substitute for fasting. In any case, when making a will is initially a voluntary gift, its execution will be from one-third of the estate, because a will is executed from one-third of the estate.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools regarding the payment of fidyah for missed fasts and zakat on behalf of a deceased person. The Hanafi position is that two conditions are necessary for the heirs to be obligated: (1) the deceased must have explicitly made a will (wasiyyah) directing the payment, and (2) the payment is limited to one-third of the estate. Without a will, the heirs are not obligated at all. The Shafi'i/Maliki position is that the will is not necessary; the heirs must pay from the entire estate regardless. The author explains the reasoning: Imam Shafi'i analogizes the debt to Allah (fidyah/zakat) to debts owed to people, where payment from the entire estate is obligatory without a will. The common cause ('illa) is that both are financial rights and deputyship (niyabah) is valid. The Hanafi response distinguishes: fidyah and zakat are acts of worship ('ibadah), which require the personal choice (ikhtiyar) of the individual. Worship cannot be compelled from another without the deceased's expressed will. After death, inheritance is compulsory (jabri), meaning the heirs take property without the deceased's consent, so without a will their payment is not an act of the deceased. The author further explains that the wasiyyah is initially a voluntary donation (tabarru') because the obligation of fasting is lifted from the deceased upon death; thus the fidyah is a substitute only in the afterlife, not a direct debt against the estate. Therefore, it is executed like any other will: from one-third of the estate only.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation paid for missed obligatory fasts or prayers, typically feeding a poor person for each missed day.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will or bequest made by a person regarding disposition of up to one-third of their estate after death.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act of charity or gift without expectation of return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person dies without making a will, are his heirs obligated to pay fidyah for his missed fasts?
A) Yes, from the entire estate.
B) Yes, but only from one-third of the estate.
C) No, they are not obligated.
D) Only if the missed fasts were for a specific vow.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fidyah and zakat are not treated as debts that automatically bind the estate; they require a will and are limited to one-third because they are acts of worship that require the deceased's choice.

Fidyah for Missed Prayers: Istihsan Overriding Qiyas
Hanafi ruling on fidyah for missed prayers with istihsan vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for missed prayers, explain the role of istihsan and qiyas in deriving this ruling, and determine the correct fidyah amount per prayer.

Core Idea
For missed prayers, istihsan permits fidyah where qiyas would forbid it, reflecting mercy in the Hanafi school.

This lesson explores a unique Hanafi ruling: paying fidyah (monetary compensation) for missed prayers on behalf of a deceased person. Strict analogy (qiyas) would forbid it, but the later mashaa'ikh applied istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it, drawing an analogy with fasting. Understanding this illustrates how Hanafi usul al-fiqh employs istihsan to achieve practical mercy without abandoning the logical framework of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving fidyah for missed obligatory prayers of a deceased person. The Hanafi mashaa'ikh rule it permissible (ja'iz) by istihsan.
Fidyah is not wajib; it becomes due only if the deceased willed it.
2
Locate the proofs (dalil)
The primary proof is istihsan, not a direct nass. The passage contrasts two methods: qiyas (analogy with prayer itself) would forbid, but istihsan (analogy with fasting) permits.
The qiyas here is qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) that becomes the basis for istihsan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of istihsan
The mashaa'ikh consider prayer and fasting both as badani ibadah (physical worship). Since fidyah is permitted for fasting after death (by nass and ijma), the same is extended to prayer via istihsan.
Istihsan overrides the literal qiyas that would deny substitution.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars held that all prayers of one day equal one fast, but the author rejects this as the correct position.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the mufta bihi is one prayer = one fast.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author states 'this is the correct statement' (yihi sahih qawl), affirming that one fard prayer equals one fast in fidyah amount.
Authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa).

Source Text

اور مشائخ نے استحسانا فرمایا ہے کہ نماز، روزے کے مانند ہے یعنی جس طرح موت کے بعد روزہ کا فدیہ دیا جا سکتا ہے اس طرح نماز کا فدیہ دینا بھی جائز ہے لیکن قیاس یہ ہے کہ نماز کا فدیہ جائز نہ ہو کیونکہ نماز جس طرح زندگی میں مال کے ساتھ ادا نہیں کی جاتی اسی طرح مرنے کے بعد بھی ادا نہیں کی جائے گی اور استحسانا اس لئے جائز قرار دیا ہے کہ بدنی عبادت ہونے میں نماز روزے کے مشابہ ہے یہ خیال رہے کہ ایک فرض نماز ایک روزہ کے برابر ہے ایک فرض نماز کا وہی فدیہ ہو گا جو ایک روزہ کا ہوتا ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ ایک دن کی نمازیں ایک روزہ کے برابر ہیں لیکن یہ قول صحیح نہیں ہے۔
And the mashaa'ikh (scholars) have ruled by istihsan that prayer is like fasting, i.e., just as fidyah can be given for fasting after death, similarly giving fidyah for prayer is permissible. But the qiyas is that fidyah for prayer is not permissible, because just as prayer is not performed with wealth in life, similarly it will not be performed after death. And it is declared permissible by istihsan because in being a physical act of worship, prayer resembles fasting. It should be noted that one obligatory prayer is equivalent to one fast. The fidyah for one obligatory prayer is the same as for one fast. This is the correct statement. Some have said that the prayers of one day are equivalent to one fast, but this statement is not correct.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for missed prayers, introduced by the mashaa'ikh (later Hanafi scholars). The principle of qiyas (analogy) would suggest that fidyah for prayers is not allowed because prayer, unlike fasting, cannot be compensated with money during life. However, the scholars applied istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it, reasoning that prayer and fasting are both physical acts of worship (ibadaat badaniyyah), so they are analogous in this context. The nass (established ruling) for fasting is extended to prayer by istihsan. The passage also clarifies the measure: one missed obligatory prayer (fard salah) requires the same fidyah as one missed fast—i.e., feeding one poor person for each missed prayer. This is the correct position; the view that all prayers of a day equal one fast is rejected.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas when strict analogy leads to a result that contradicts general principles of mercy or ease.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction based on a common effective cause between a new case and an established case.
بدنی عبادت (badani ibadah): An act of worship involving physical exertion of the body, such as prayer, fasting, pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mashaa'ikh, what is the fidyah amount for one missed obligatory prayer?
A) Same as for one missed fast (feeding one poor person).
B) Double the fidyah of one fast.
C) Half the fidyah of one fast.
D) The prayers of a whole day equal one fast.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan allows fidyah for missed prayers by analogy with fasting, overriding the strict qiyas that would forbid it; one missed prayer equals one fast in fidyah.

Guardian Cannot Fast or Pray for Deceased
Dispute on whether a guardian can fulfill missed fasts/prayers for a deceased person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a guardian fasting or praying for a deceased person, explain the Hanafi proof (hadith of Ibn Umar), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Physical acts of worship are personal; they cannot be delegated to a guardian after death.

When someone dies with missed fasts or prayers, can a guardian step in and perform them on their behalf? The Hanafi school says no—fasting and praying are deeply personal acts of devotion that cannot be transferred. This lesson explores the Hanafi position, its primary evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and the Shafi'i view based on the hadith of Aisha, showing how the Hanafis reconcile the apparent conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the guardian cannot fast or pray on behalf of the deceased, and any such act is invalid and not counted.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Shafi'i holds that the guardian may physically fast for the deceased (but not pray). Recognize the difference.
Shafi'i's view is limited to fasting, not prayer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i reliance is on the hadith of Aisha: 'Whoever dies with fasts due, his guardian should fast on his behalf.' Understand the literal reading.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts by: 1) citing the hadith of Ibn Umar as a general prohibition; 2) reasoning that the purpose of fasting (subduing the nafs ammarah) is personal; 3) interpreting the hadith of Aisha to mean fidyah (feeding the poor) if the deceased made a will.
The Hanafi interpretation is istihsan-based to reconcile conflicting hadiths.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says guardian only pays fidyah if willed; Shafi'i says guardian can physically fast. No physical fasting in Hanafi.

ولی میت کی طرف سے روزہ نہیں رکھ سکتا اور نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا
وَلَا يَصُومُ عَنْهُ الْوَلِي وَلَا يُصَلَّى لِقَوْلِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَا يَصُومُ أَحَدٌ عَنْ أَحَدٍ وَلَا يُصَلَّى أَحَدُ عَنْ أَحَدٍ ترجمہ اور میت کی طرف سے اس کا ولی نہ روزہ رکھے گا اور نہ نماز پڑھے گا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ کوئی کسی کی طرف سے نہ روز ور کھے گا اور نہ نماز پڑھے گا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ میت کے ذمہ اگر روزے ہوں یا نمازیں ہوں اور پھر میت کے ولی نے میت کی طرف سے روزہ رکھایا نماز پڑھی تو یہ روزہ اور نماز میت کی جانب سے شمار نہ ہوگا حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ولی میت کے لئے میت کی طرف سے روزہ رکھنا جائز ہے اور ان کا مستدل حضرت عائشہ کی یہ حدیث ہے انهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسَّلامُ قَالَ مَنْ مَاتَ وَعَلَيْهِ الصَّيَامَ صَامَ عَنْهُ وليه، حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو شخص مر گیا اور اس پر روزہ ہے تو اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی روزہ رکھے اور ہماری دلیل ابن عمر کی حدیث ب لَا يَصُومُ أحَدَّعَنْ أَحَدٍ وَلا يُصَلّى أحدَ عَنْ اُحد یعنی نہ کوئی کسی کے بدلے روزو رکھے گا اور نہ کوئی کسی کے بدلے نماز پڑھے گا دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عبادت صوم سے مقصود نفس امارہ کو مغلوب کرنا ہے اور یہ مقصود دوسرے کے فعل سے حاصل نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے دوسرے کسی کو میت کی جانب سے روزہ رکھنے کی ابھی اجازت نہ ہوگی اور حدیث عائشہ صام عنه ولیہ کا مطلب فعل ما يقوم الصوم من الاطعام اذا اوصى بدالک یعنی میت کا ولی روزے کے قائم مقام کام کرے یعنی فدیہ دے بشر طیکہ میت نے فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کی ہو۔
And the guardian cannot fast on behalf of the deceased, nor can he pray. (Arabic): 'And the guardian does not fast on his behalf, nor is prayer offered on his behalf, because of his saying (peace be upon him): No one fasts on behalf of another, and no one prays on behalf of another.' Translation: The guardian of the deceased will neither fast nor pray on his behalf, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: No one will fast on behalf of another, and no one will pray on behalf of another. Explanation of the issue: If there are fasts or prayers due upon the deceased, and then the guardian of the deceased fasts or prays on his behalf, these fasts and prayers will not be counted on behalf of the deceased. Imam Shafi'i said that it is permissible for the guardian to fast on behalf of the deceased, and his proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever dies and has fasts due, his guardian should fast on his behalf.' And our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'No one fasts on behalf of another, and no one prays on behalf of another.' The second proof is that the purpose of the worship of fasting is to subdue the commanding soul, and this purpose cannot be achieved by the act of another. Therefore, it is not permissible for anyone else to fast on behalf of the deceased. And the meaning of the hadith of Aisha 'his guardian should fast on his behalf' is that the guardian should do something that takes the place of fasting, i.e., give fidyah, provided that the deceased made a will for it.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents a legal dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding whether a guardian can physically perform missed fasts or prayers on behalf of a deceased person. The Hanafi position is clear: it is not allowed. The ruling is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'No one fasts on behalf of another, and no one prays on behalf of another.' The Hanafis interpret the purpose of fasting as personal discipline over the nafs ammarah (commanding soul), which cannot be achieved by proxy. They reconcile the apparent contrary hadith of Aisha ('the guardian should fast on his behalf') by interpreting it to mean providing fidyah (feeding the poor), not actual fasting, and only if the deceased made a will. Imam Shafi'i, on the other hand, takes the hadith of Aisha literally and allows a guardian to physically fast for the deceased. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi stance that physical acts of worship are personal and cannot be delegated after death, though financial substitutes (fidyah) are allowed by will.

Key Terms
ولی (wali): The guardian or legal heir responsible for the deceased's affairs.
نفس امارہ (nafs ammarah): The commanding soul that inclines to evil; subduing it is the purpose of fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct interpretation of the hadith 'Whoever dies with fasts due, his guardian should fast on his behalf'?
A) It means the guardian should physically fast for the deceased.
B) It means the guardian should feed the poor (fidyah) if the deceased willed it.
C) It means the guardian should make dua for the deceased.
D) It means the obligation drops entirely.

Key Takeaway
Physical acts of worship like fasting and prayer are personal obligations that cannot be fulfilled by proxy; only financial substitutes (fidyah) are valid if willed.

Sawm — Fasting
advanced
12 min
The Obligation of Qada for a Broken Nafl Fast: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents Hanafi ruling, refutes Shafi'i proofs, discusses hospitality excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qada for a broken nafl fast, explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proofs, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Once a voluntary fast is started, it becomes binding to complete; breaking it requires Qada.

When you begin an act of worship with the intention of earning reward, does that act become binding? The Hanafi school says yes—once you start a voluntary fast, you must complete it, and if you break it, you must make it up. The Shafi'i school disagrees, viewing the entire fast as voluntary until its end. This lesson unpacks that dispute, the proofs on each side, and a key exception for hospitality.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: qada is wajib upon breaking a nafl fast after starting it. Understand the basis: completion becomes obligatory when the act is begun.
The Hanafi proof texts are Quran 47:33 and the hadith of Aisha and Hafsah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i and other positions
Contrast with Shafi'i/Hanbali (no qada) and Maliki (qada only if broken without excuse). Recognize the root difference: is breaking a nafl fast without excuse permissible (mubah) or not?
Shafi'is consider it mubah; Hanafis consider it a transgression (jinayah).
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof sequentially
Examine the Shafi'i dalils: hadith of Umm Hani', hadith of Aisha in Muslim, verse 9:91, and analogy with charity. Understand why each is presented.
The charity analogy makes an important distinction between divisible and indivisible acts.
4
Analyze the Hanafi responses
See how the Hanafis reinterpret or rebut each Shafi'i proof. Note the key response: the hadith of Umm Hani' refers to starting, not breaking; the Muslim hadith is an exception for hospitality; the verse applies to completed acts; the charity analogy fails because fasting is a unitary act.
The strongest Hanafi proof is the explicit command in the Aisha/Hafsah hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
What does this mean for a Muslim today? A Hanafi must make up a broken nafl fast; a Shafi'i does not. Also note the intra-Hanafi detail on hospitality as an excuse.
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that hospitality is a valid excuse to break, but qada is still required.

اور موطا امام مالک میں بیان کیا ہے عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ أصْبَحْتُ أَنَا وَحَفْصَةٌ صَائِمَتَيْنِ مُتَطَوِعَتَيْنِ فَاهَدَى إِلَيْنَا طَعَامِ فَافْطَرْنَا عَلَيه فَدَخَلَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ ہمارے سامنے طعام آیا پس ہم نے روزہ افطار کر ڈالا تو ہمارے پاس رسول اللہ تشریف لائے تو حفصہ نے مجھ سے سبقت تو کر کے آپ سے اس واقعہ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کی جگہ ایک دن قضاء کر لو۔ یہ حدیث صاف دلالت کرتی ہے کر نفلی روزہ فاسد کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قضا واجب ہے اس حدیث میں وَ كَانَتْ إبنة أبيها کا لفظ حضرت عائشہ کا ہے اس لفظ میں حفصہ کی دلیری اور بہادری کا ذکر ہے حضرت عائشہ نے حضرت حفصہ کے سبقت کرنے کی وجہ سے فرمایا کہ آخر وہ اپنے باپ کی بیٹی ہے۔" مراد یہ ہے کہ حضرت حفصہ ، حضرت عمر کی بیٹی ہے اور حضرت عمر انتہائی جری اور بہادر انسان ہیں۔ لہذا ان کی بیٹی بھی ویسی ہی جرمی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ام ہانی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں افطار کے معنی روز و تو رنے کے نہیں ہیں بلکہ روزہ نہ رکھنے کے ہیں یعنی جو شخص نفلی روزہ کا ارادہ کرے وہ اپنی ذات کا خود حاکم ہے چاہے روزہ رکھے اور چاہئے نہ رکھے ۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث عائشہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں صرف اتناذکر ہے کہ حلوائے جیس کا ہدیہ آنے پر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے روزہ توڑا ہے اور عذر ضیافت کی وجہ سے روزہ توڑنا جائز ہے اس سے زیادہ وجوب قضاء یا عدم وجوب قضاء اس روایت سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا لیکن وہ حدیث عائشہ جس کو ہم نے اپنی تائید میں ذکر کیا ہے وہ وجوب قضاء پر صراحت دلالت کرتی ہے لہذا اس کو اسی حدیث پر محمول کیا جائے گا جس میں وجوب قضا کی زیادتی موجود ہے آخر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ عذر کی وجہ سے نفلی روز و تو ڑ نا بالاتفاق مباح ہے لیکن با اعذر توڑنے میں دوروایتیں ہیں۔ ایک اباحت کی ، دوم عدم اباحت کی ، عدم اباحت پر دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ضیافت بھی عذر ہے یعنی اگر کوئی کسی کی دعوت کرے اور وہ نفلی روزے سے ہو تو وہ اس نفلی روزہ کو اگر ضیافت اور دعوت کی وجہ سے تو ڑنا چاہئے تو تو ڑ سکتا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت ہے کہ ضیافت عذر نہیں ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے إِذَا دُعِيَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَجِبْ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْطِرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَائِمًا فَلْيَصِلُ یعنی اگر تم میں سے کسی کی دعوت کی جائے تو قبول کر لے پھر وہ اگر روزہ دارنہ ہو تو کھالے اور اگر روزہ دار ہو تو داعی کو دعائے خیر دیدے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ضیافت عذر نہیں ہے اس لئے روزہ توڑنے کی اجازت نہیں دی گئی ہے۔ اور قول اول کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اُنه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوة والسّلامُ كَانَ فِى ضِيَافَةِ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ فَامْتَنَعَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الأكلِ وَقَالَ إِنِّى صَائِمٌ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسّلام إِنَّما دَعَاكَ اَخُوكَ لِتَكْر مُهُ فَافْطِرُ وَاقْضِ يَوْماً مَّكَانَهُ۔ یعنی نبی اعظم ایک انصاری کی دعوت میں شریک تھے ایک صاحب کھانے سے رک گئے اور کہا کہ میرا روزہ ہے جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تیرے بھائی نے تجھ کو دعوت دی ہے تجھ کو اس کا اکرام کرنا چاہے تم افطار کر لو اور اس کی جگہ ایک دن کی قضا کر لینا ۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ میزبان اگر محض حاضری سے خوش ہو جائے اور نہ کھانے سے اذیت محسوس نہ کرے تو افطار نہ کرے اور اگر نہ کھانے سے اذیت محسوس کرے تو افطار کر دینا چاہئے اور بعد میں اس کی
The book of fasting: Then upon abandoning it (the fast), qada becomes obligatory. Then according to one of two narrations in our school, breaking a voluntary fast without an excuse is not permissible due to the proof we mentioned, and with an excuse it is permissible, and hospitality is an excuse because the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Break the fast and make up one day in its place.' Explanation of the issue: If someone begins a voluntary prayer or voluntary fast and then invalidates it, making it up is obligatory upon him. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad said that qada is not obligatory at all. Imam Malik said that if the invalidation was due to an excuse, qada is not necessary, but if without an excuse, qada is obligatory. The basis of the disagreement between us and the Shafi'is is that breaking a fast without an excuse is not permissible according to us, but it is permissible according to the Shafi'is. So when breaking is not permissible for us, he becomes guilty of a transgression, and the one who commits a transgression must perform qada. Therefore, breaking a voluntary fast obligates qada in our view. According to the Shafi'is, since it is permissible, breaking is not a transgression, and hence qada is not necessary. Imam Shafi'i also uses evidence that when one begins a voluntary prayer or fast and performs a part of it, he is a volunteer and a doer of good for that part. The remaining part he has not volunteered, so it is not binding on him; otherwise it would contradict the verse 'There is no blame on the doers of good' (9:91). So the remaining part is not binding, and leaving it does not require qada, because qada is only obligatory for what was obligatory to perform, and what is not obligatory does not necessitate qada. An example: if someone places two dirhams in his pocket intending charity, then gives one dirham, the other is not obligatory on him because if he had given none, nothing would have been obligatory on him. Imam Shafi'i also uses the hadith of Umm Hani' narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi: 'The Prophet (SAW) said: The voluntary fasting person is the commander of his own self; if he wishes he may fast, and if he wishes he may break the fast.' This shows that breaking a voluntary fast without an excuse is permissible, so no transgression occurs and qada is not required. In Sahih Muslim: 'Aisha (RA) said: The Prophet (SAW) came to me one day and said: Do you have anything? We said: No. He said: Then I am fasting. Then another day he came and we said: O Messenger of Allah, we have been gifted some hays. He said: Bring it to me; I had started the morning fasting, then he ate.' This also shows that completing the fast is not obligatory, and since obligation of completion is the basis for qada, when completion is not obligatory, qada is also not necessary. Our evidence is that the voluntary fast that has been begun is an act of worship, and it is obligatory to protect acts from being nullified. Allah says: 'Do not nullify your acts.' Protecting acts from nullification is achieved by completing them. So after beginning, completing the act is obligatory, and if it is invalidated, making it up is also obligatory. Our school is supported by the hadith narrated by Nasa'i, Tirmidhi, and Muwatta of Imam Malik: 'Aisha said: I and Hafsah began the morning as voluntary fasting persons. Then food was gifted to us and we broke our fast on it. Then the Messenger of Allah came to us. Hafsah preceded me (in asking), and she was the daughter of her father, so she asked him about that. He said: Make up a day in its place.' This hadith clearly indicates that qada is obligatory upon breaking a voluntary fast. The words 'and she was the daughter of her father' are Aisha's, referring to Hafsah's boldness, meaning she is the daughter of Umar, who was very bold. So her daughter is also bold. The response to the hadith of Umm Hani' presented by Imam Shafi'i is that 'iftar' in the hadith means not fasting in the first place, not breaking an ongoing fast. It means the one who intends a voluntary fast is master of himself: he may fast or not fast (i.e., not begin). And the response to the hadith of Aisha presented by Imam Shafi'i is that it only mentions that the Prophet broke his fast when hays was gifted due to the excuse of hospitality, and breaking a fast due to an excuse is permissible. This narration does not prove obligatory or non-obligatory qada. But the hadith of Aisha that we mentioned in support explicitly indicates the obligation of qada, so that narration is interpreted in light of this one which includes the addition of obligation. Finally, it is said that breaking a voluntary fast due to an excuse is unanimously permissible, but regarding breaking without an excuse there are two narrations: one of permissibility, the other of non-permissibility. The proof for non-permissibility is the verse 'Do not nullify your acts.' The author of Hidayah says: Hospitality is also an excuse. That is, if someone invites him and he is observing a voluntary fast, he may break his fast due to the invitation. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad that hospitality is not an excuse, because it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: 'When one of you is invited, he should respond. If he is not fasting, he should eat; if he is fasting, he should pray for goodness for the inviter.' This shows that hospitality is not an excuse, so breaking the fast is not permitted. The evidence for the first opinion is the hadith: 'The Prophet (SAW) was at the hospitality of a man from the Ansar. A man refrained from eating and said, I am fasting. The Prophet (SAW) said: Your brother invited you to honor him, so break your fast and make up a day in its place.' Some mashayikh said: If the host is pleased merely by your presence and does not feel hurt by you not eating, then do not break the fast; but if he feels hurt, then you should break the fast and later make it up.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of making up (qada) a voluntary (nafl) fast that one has broken after starting it. The Hanafi school holds that once a voluntary act of worship is begun, it becomes necessary to complete it. If one invalidates it, one must make it up. The Shafi'i school, alongside Ahmad ibn Hanbal, holds that qada is not required at all because the act was voluntary and one can abandon it at will. Imam Malik takes a middle position: if broken due to an excuse, no qada; if without excuse, qada is required.

The main point of contention is whether breaking a voluntary fast without a valid excuse is permissible (mubah) or not. For the Hanafis, it is not permissible; therefore, breaking it constitutes a transgression (jinayah) which obligates compensation (qada). For the Shafi'is, it is permissible, so no transgression occurs and no qada is needed.

The Shafi'is argue from the principle that a volunteer is only bound by what he has voluntarily performed; the remaining portion is not binding, as per the verse 'there is no blame on the doers of good' (Surah al-Tawbah: 91). They analogize it to someone who intends to give two dirhams in charity but only gives one—the other is not obligatory.

They also cite the hadith of Umm Hani': 'The voluntary fasting person is the commander of his own self; if he wishes he may fast, and if he wishes he may break the fast.' This is reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. Additionally, the hadith of Aisha in Sahih Muslim relates that the Prophet began the morning intending to fast, but when food was brought, he ate, indicating that completion is not obligatory.

The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Umm Hani' refers to the initial intention—whether to start fasting or not—not to breaking an already commenced fast. The hadith of Aisha about the Prophet eating is interpreted as being due to the excuse of hospitality (diyafah), which is a valid excuse making it permissible, but it does not negate the obligation of qada when there is no excuse. The Hanafis rely on the Quranic verse 'Do not nullify your acts' (Surah Muhammad: 33), which implies that once begun, an act of worship must be protected from nullification by completion, and if invalidated, by making it up.

Their key proof is the hadith narrated by al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi, and in Malik's Muwatta: Aisha and Hafsah were observing a voluntary fast when food was gifted to them; they broke their fast. The Prophet (SAW) instructed them: 'Make up a day in its place.' This explicit command indicates obligation.

The discussion then extends to the ruling on hospitality as an excuse. The author of Hidayah states that hospitality is an excuse, so if someone is invited while fasting a nafl fast, he may break it. However, there is a narration (riwayah) from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad that hospitality is not an excuse, based on the hadith saying a fasting person should simply pray for the inviter. The first opinion is supported by another hadith where the Prophet told someone invited to break his fast and make it up. Some later mashayikh reconcile these by considering the host's feelings: if the host would be hurt, breaking is recommended; otherwise, not.

The passage concludes by noting that breaking a nafl fast without an excuse has two narrations in the Hanafi school: one regarding permissibility, one regarding impermissibility. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is not explicitly settled here, but the overall context suggests that impermissibility is the stronger position.

Key Terms
نفلی روزہ (nafli roza): A voluntary (supererogatory) fast, not obligatory but recommended.
قضا (qada): Making up a missed or broken act of worship by performing it at a later time.
ضیافت (diyafah): Hospitality; the act of hosting or being invited as a guest.
جنایت (jinayah): Transgression or offense; here, breaking a fast without valid reason is considered a legal offense requiring compensation.
مباح (mubah): Permissible; an action that is neither commanded nor forbidden, and incurs neither reward nor punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling if someone breaks a voluntary (nafl) fast after starting it?
A) No qada is required because it was voluntary.
B) Qada is required only if broken without an excuse; with an excuse, no qada.
C) Qada is required regardless of excuse.
D) The fast is simply invalid, and no action is needed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires qada for a broken nafl fast, based on the principle that once begun, a voluntary act becomes binding, and this is supported by the explicit prophetic command.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Breaking a Voluntary Fast and the Obligation of Qada
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that breaking a voluntary fast requires qada, with proofs and responses to opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a broken voluntary fast, explain the primary proof from the hadith of 'Aisha, and apply the exception for hospitality.

Core Idea
A voluntary fast becomes binding once started; breaking it requires qada.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common point of confusion: whether a voluntary (nafl) fast can be ended without consequence. The Hanafi school rules that once a nafl fast is begun, it becomes akin to an obligation to complete; if broken, qada (make-up) is wajib. The author provides textual evidence and responds to opposing views, including a discussion of valid excuses such as hospitality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is breaking a voluntary fast. The ruling is that qada (making it up) is wajib. Note that this applies whether the fast is broken with or without a valid excuse, though the permissibility differs.
The obligation of qada is established regardless of the excuse.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the hadith of 'Aisha and Hafsah who broke their voluntary fast and were ordered by the Prophet to 'replace it with another day'. The imperative 'اقضيا' (make up) indicates obligation according to Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Understand the logical principle
The verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33) provides the basis: once an act of worship is started, it must be completed. Invalidation necessitates compensation.
This principle is applied to all nafl ibadat in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that qada is not required, citing hadith of Umm Hani (where 'iftar' is interpreted as not starting a fast) and another hadith of 'Aisha about sweets. The Hanafi response distinguishes these and relies on the explicit command in the primary hadith.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi requires qada; Shafi'i does not.
5
Apply the exception for hospitality
The passage discusses a valid excuse: hospitality (diyafah). The preferred view allows breaking before noon if the host would be offended, but qada is still wajib. A variant view (Hasan ibn Ziyad) does not allow it. The mufta bihi is the permissive view.
Breaking after noon is only allowed to avoid disobedience to parents.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
خداوندی ہے وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا اعْمَالَكُم اور اعمال کو باطل ہونے سے بچانا اس طرح ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کو پورا کیا جائے ۔ بہر حال شروع کرنے کے بعد عمل کو پورا کرنا واجب ہے اور جب عمل کو پورا کرنا واجب ہے تو فساد کی صورت میں اس کی قضا کرنا بھی واجب ہوگا۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو نسائی اترندی اور موطا امام مالک میں بیان کیا ہے عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ أصْبَحْتُ أَنَا وَحَفْصَةٌ صَائِمَتَيْنِ مُتَطَوِعَتَيْنِ فَاهَدَى إِلَيْنَا طَعَامِ فَافْطَرْنَا عَلَيه فَدَخَلَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَدَرَ تُنِي حَفْصَةً وَكَانَتْ إِبْنَةُ أَيْهَا فَسَا لَتْهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ اقْضِيَا يَوْمًا مَّكَانَهُ حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ میں اور حفصہ نفلی روزے سے تھیں کہ ہمارے سامنے طعام آیا پس ہم نے روزہ افطار کر ڈالا تو ہمارے پاس رسول اللہ تشریف لائے تو حفصہ نے مجھ سے سبقت تو کر کے آپ سے اس واقعہ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کی جگہ ایک دن قضاء کر لو۔ یہ حدیث صاف دلالت کرتی ہے کر نفلی روزہ فاسد کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قضا واجب ہے اس حدیث میں وَ كَانَتْ إبنة أبيها کا لفظ حضرت عائشہ کا ہے اس لفظ میں حفصہ کی دلیری اور بہادری کا ذکر ہے حضرت عائشہ نے حضرت حفصہ کے سبقت کرنے کی وجہ سے فرمایا کہ آخر وہ اپنے باپ کی بیٹی ہے۔" مراد یہ ہے کہ حضرت حفصہ ، حضرت عمر کی بیٹی ہے اور حضرت عمر انتہائی جری اور بہادر انسان ہیں۔ لہذا ان کی بیٹی بھی ویسی ہی جرمی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ام ہانی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں افطار کے معنی روز و تو رنے کے نہیں ہیں بلکہ روزہ نہ رکھنے کے ہیں یعنی جو شخص نفلی روزہ کا ارادہ کرے وہ اپنی ذات کا خود حاکم ہے چاہے روزہ رکھے اور چاہئے نہ رکھے ۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث عائشہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں صرف اتناذکر ہے کہ حلوائے جیس کا ہدیہ آنے پر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے روزہ توڑا ہے اور عذر ضیافت کی وجہ سے روزہ توڑنا جائز ہے اس سے زیادہ وجوب قضاء یا عدم وجوب قضاء اس روایت سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا لیکن وہ حدیث عائشہ جس کو ہم نے اپنی تائید میں ذکر کیا ہے وہ وجوب قضاء پر صراحت دلالت کرتی ہے لہذا اس کو اسی حدیث پر محمول کیا جائے گا جس میں وجوب قضا کی زیادتی موجود ہے آخر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ عذر کی وجہ سے نفلی روز و تو ڑ نا بالاتفاق مباح ہے لیکن با اعذر توڑنے میں
دوروایتیں ہیں۔ ایک اباحت کی ، دوم عدم اباحت کی ، عدم اباحت پر دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ضیافت بھی عذر ہے یعنی اگر کوئی کسی کی دعوت کرے اور وہ نفلی روزے سے ہو تو وہ اس نفلی روزہ کو اگر ضیافت اور دعوت کی وجہ سے تو ڑنا چاہئے تو تو ڑ سکتا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت ہے کہ ضیافت عذر نہیں ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے إِذَا دُعِيَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَجِبْ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْطِرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَائِمًا فَلْيَصِلُ یعنی اگر تم میں سے کسی کی دعوت کی جائے تو قبول کر لے پھر وہ اگر روزہ دارنہ ہو تو کھالے اور اگر روزہ دار ہو تو داعی کو دعائے خیر دیدے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ضیافت عذر نہیں ہے اس لئے روزہ توڑنے کی اجازت نہیں دی گئی ہے۔ اور قول اول کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اُنه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوة والسّلامُ كَانَ فِى ضِيَافَةِ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ فَامْتَنَعَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الأكلِ وَقَالَ إِنِّى صَائِمٌ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلوةُ وَالسّلام إِنَّما دَعَاكَ اَخُوكَ لِتَكْر مُهُ فَافْطِرُ وَاقْضِ يَوْماً مَّكَانَهُ۔ یعنی نبی اعظم ایک انصاری کی دعوت میں شریک تھے ایک صاحب کھانے سے رک گئے اور کہا کہ میرا روزہ ہے جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تیرے بھائی نے تجھ کو دعوت دی ہے تجھ کو اس کا اکرام کرنا چاہے تم افطار کر لو اور اس کی جگہ ایک دن کی قضا کر لینا ۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ میزبان اگر محض حاضری سے خوش ہو جائے اور نہ کھانے سے اذیت محسوس نہ کرے تو افطار نہ کرے اور اگر نہ کھانے سے اذیت محسوس کرے تو افطار کر دینا چاہئے اور بعد میں اس کی
قضا کرلے۔ لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ افطار کی اجازت زوال سے پہلے ہے زوال کے بعد افطار نہ کرنا چاہتے ہاں اگر افطار نہ کرنے کی صورت میں والدین یا ان میں سے ایک کی نافرمانی ہوتی ہو تو پھر زوال کے بعد بھی افطار کر دینا چاہئے۔
The Book of Fasting. Allah says 'Do not invalidate your deeds', and protecting deeds from invalidation is by completing them. After starting an action, completing it is wajib, and if it becomes invalid, making it up (qada) becomes wajib. Our school is supported by the hadith narrated by Nasa'i and in Muwatta of Imam Malik from 'Aisha: 'I and Hafsah started voluntary fasts, then food was gifted to us, so we broke our fast. The Prophet entered and Hafsah asked him. He said: Replace it with another day.' This hadith clearly indicates that qada is wajib for breaking a voluntary fast. The word 'and she was the daughter of her father' refers to Hafsah's boldness. The answer to the Shafi'i hadith of Umm Hani is that 'iftar' there means not fasting, not breaking. The answer to the hadith of 'Aisha about the sweet is that it only shows breaking due to hospitality, not qada, but our hadith explicitly proves qada. Finally, breaking a voluntary fast for an excuse is permissible by consensus, but without excuse there are two transmissions: one allowing, one not. The proof for not allowing is the verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds'. The author of Hidayah says hospitality is an excuse, and breaking is allowed. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad that it is not an excuse, based on the hadith: 'When invited, respond; if not fasting, eat; if fasting, supplicate.' The first view is supported by the hadith that the Prophet was at a meal and told a fasting man to break and replace it. Some mashayikh said: if the host is pleased with presence, do not break; if offended, break and make it up. Note: breaking is only allowed before noon; after noon it is not allowed unless it involves disobedience to parents.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from the Hanafi school. It discusses the obligation of qada (make-up) when a voluntary (nafl) fast is broken. The passage begins by citing the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33) as a rational proof that once an act of worship is started, it must be completed; if invalidated, qada is wajib. Then it presents a hadith from 'Aisha where she and Hafsah broke their voluntary fast and the Prophet ordered them to make it up. This is the primary proof for the Hanafi position that qada is wajib for broken nafl fasts. The passage then answers two objections from Imam al-Shafi'i: (1) the hadith of Umm Hani – it is argued that 'iftar' there means not starting a fast, not breaking it; (2) another hadith of 'Aisha about sweets – it only shows permissibility of breaking for hospitality, not qada. The Hanafi response is that the explicit wording of the first hadith (with the command 'replace it') outweighs the general reports. The passage then discusses whether hospitality (diyafat) is a valid excuse to break a nafl fast. It notes that there are two transmissions from Abu Hanifa: the preferred view (from Zahir al-Riwayah) allows it if the host would be offended; the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad does not allow it. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that breaking for hospitality is permissible before noon, provided the host is not merely pleased with attendance, and qada is required. Additionally, if not breaking would cause disobedience to parents, it is allowed even after noon.

Key Terms
نفلی روزہ (nafl roza): A voluntary (supererogatory) fast performed outside Ramadan and obligatory fasts.
قضاء (qadaa): Making up a missed or broken obligatory or voluntary act of worship.
ضیافت (diyafah): Hospitality, especially being invited to a meal; considered a valid excuse to break a nafl fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on qada when a voluntary (nafl) fast is broken without a valid excuse?
A) Qada is not required, as the fast was optional.
B) Qada is wajib (obligatory).
C) Qada is sunnah (recommended).
D) The fast is simply invalid, and no compensation is needed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, breaking a voluntary fast makes qada obligatory, even if broken for a valid excuse like hospitality before noon.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qada for Newly Eligible Fasters
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imsaak and qada for newly eligible fasters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) on qada for a child who reaches puberty or a disbeliever who accepts Islam during a Ramadan day, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
No qada for the day; only imsaak is wajib out of respect for the time.

When a child becomes adult or a disbeliever converts during a Ramadan day, do they have to make up that day's fast? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the relied-upon Hanafi position and an alternative view from Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the school handles eligibility and the indivisibility of fasting obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the newly eligible person
Note that both the child who reaches puberty and the convert to Islam must abstain (imsaak) for the rest of the day, but they are not required to make up (qada) that day if they break it. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the change occurs before or after noon.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The reason is that fasting is not divisible into parts; the obligation is for the entire day. Since eligibility (ahliyyah) was absent at the beginning of the day, the obligation never attached. The cause (sabab) of fasting is the first part of the day, and eligibility must exist then.
Contrast with prayer: if a person becomes eligible during prayer time, they must perform the prayer because the cause is the entire time.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's objection
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the change occurs before zawal (noon), qada becomes wajib because the person reached the time of intention (niyyah). The time of intention is still available before noon, so the obligation can attach.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the opposing school is within the same madhhab.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The Zahir al-Riwayah response is that fasting cannot be split in obligation; the first part of the day lacked eligibility, so the entire day remains non-obligatory. The time of intention is not sufficient to create obligation for a day that already began without eligibility.
The face of the Zahir (al-Marghinani) adopts this view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical application
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Zahir al-Riwayah: no qada, only imsaak. A child may also intend a voluntary (nafl) fast for that day, but a convert may not, because a disbeliever is not eligible for nafl acts.
This ruling applies to similar situations: a menstruating woman who becomes pure, a traveler who becomes resident, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رمضان کے دن میں بچہ بالغ ہو گیا، کافر مسلمان ہو گیا تو بقیہ دن کھانے پینے سے رکے رہیں
وَإِذَا بَلَعَ الصَّبِيُّ أو أسلَمَ الْكَافِرُ فِي رَمَضَانَ أَمْسَكَا بَقِيَّةٌ يَوْمِهِمَا فَضَاء لِحَقِّ الوَقْتِ بِالتَّشَهِ وَلَوْ أقْطَرًا فيه لا فَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِمَا لِأَنَّ الصَّومَ غَيْرُ وَاجِبٍ فِيهِ وَ صَامَا مَا بَعْدَهُ لِتَحَقِّقِ السَّبَبِ وَالْأَهْلِيَّةِ وَلَمْ يَقْضِيَا يَوْمَهُمَا وَلَا مَا مَضَى لِعَدَمِ الْخِطَابِ وَهذَا بِخِلَافِ الصَّلوة لأنَّ السَّبَبَ فِيهَا الْجُزْءُ الْمُتَّصِلُ بِالْأَدَاءِ فَوَجَدَتِ الْأَهْلِيَّةُ عِندَهُ وَ فِى الصَّوْمِ الْجُزْءُ الْأَوَّلُ وَالْاَهْلِيَّةُ مُنْعَدِمَةٌ عِنْدَهُ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسَفَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا زَالَ الكُفْرُ وَالصّبى قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ لأَنه أَدْرَكَ وَقتَ النّيَةِ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ الصَّومَ لَا يَتَجَزَى وُجُوبًا وَأَهْلِيَّةُ الوُجُوبِ مُنْعَدِمَةٌ فِى ) أَنَّ لِلصَّبِيِّ أنْ يَنْوِى لِلتَّطَوع فِى هَذِهِ الصُّوَرَةِ دُونَ الْكَافِرِ عَلَى مَا قَالُوا لِأَنَّ الْكَافِرَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أهْلَ التَّطَوُّع أيضًا وَالصَّبِيُّ أَهَل لَهُ
ترجمہ اور جب رمضان کے دن میں بچہ بالغ ہو گیا یا کافر مسلمان ہو گیا تو دن کے باقی حصہ میں رکے رہیں تا کہ روزہ داروں کے ساتھ مشابہت اختیار کرتے ہوئے وقت کا حق ادا ہو جائے۔ اور اگر ان دونوں نے باقی دن میں بھی افطار کر لیا تو ان پر قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ روزہ اس دن میں واجب نہیں ہے اور اس دن کے مابعد ایام رمضان کا روزہ رکھیں کیونکہ سبب اور اہلیت متحقق ہو گئے ہیں ، اور دونوں اپنے اس دن کی اور گذشتہ ایام کی قضا نہ کریں اس لئے کہ خطاب نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور یہ نماز کے برخلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز کے اندر سبب وہ جز ہے جو ادا کے ساتھ متصل ہے پس اس وقت میں لیاقت موجود ہے اور روزہ کے اندر سبب جزء اول ہوتا ہے اور اس وقت میں اہلیت معدوم ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ جب کفر یا عدم بلوغ زوال سے پہلے زائل ہو گیا تو اس پر قضا ، واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے نیت کا وقت پالیا ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ روزہ وجو باٹکڑے نہیں ہوتا اور اول نہار میں املیت وجوب معدوم ہے مگر کیہ بچہ کے لئے اس صورت میں نقل کی نیت کرنا جائز ہے نہ کہ کافر کے لئے جیسا کہ مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اس لئے کہ کا فرانضل کا بھی اہل نہیں ہے اور بچہ نفل کا اہل ہے۔
تشریح اس مسئلہ کا مدار ایک ضابطہ پر ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے دنوں میں اگر کوئی شخص دن کے آخری حصہ میں اسی صفت اور حالت پر ہو گیا کہ اگر یہ شخص دن کے اول حصہ میں اس حال پر ہوتا تو اس پر روزہ رکھنا فرض ہوتا۔ پس اس شخص پر دن کے باقی حصہ میں امساک یعنی روزہ داروں کی طرح رہنا واجب ہے مثلا حائضہ یا نفاس والی عورت طلوع فجر کے بعد دن کے کسی حصہ میں اپنے حیض و نفاس سے پاک ہوگی یا کوئی شخص مجنون تھا اسکو افاقہ ہوگیا یا بیا تھا شفایاب ہو گیا یا مسافر تھا مقیم ہو گیا اور جو شخص ایسی صفت پر نہ ہوا اس پر امساک یعنی روزہ داروں کی طرح رہنا واجب نہیں ہے جیسے کہ کوئی عورت پورے دن حیض یا نفاس کی حالت میں رہے تو اس پر امساک واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے لئے کھانا پینا جائز ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ باقی دن کا امساک واجب ہے یا مستحب ہے، تو اس بارے میں محمد بن شجاع کہتے ہیں کہ یہ امساک مستحب ہے کیونکہ جب دن کا ایک حصہ حالت افطار میں گزر گیا تو باقی دان میں مفطرات سے رکنا کس
If a child becomes adult or a disbeliever accepts Islam during Ramadan, they must abstain for the rest of the day out of respect for the time. If they break it, there is no qada on them because fasting is not obligatory for that day. They will fast the following days (of Ramadan) because the cause and eligibility are now present. They do not make up that day or past days because there was no command. This is contrary to prayer because the cause in prayer is the part connected to performance, so eligibility exists at that time. In fasting, the cause is the first part, and eligibility is absent at that time. From Abu Yusuf: if disbelief or childhood ends before zawal (noon), qada is obligatory because he reached the time of intention. The face of the Zahir al-Riwayah: fasting is not divisible in obligation, and eligibility for obligation is absent at the beginning. However, a child can intend nafl (voluntary) in this case, but a disbeliever cannot, because a disbeliever is not eligible for nafl acts either, while a child is. Explanation: The rule is that if a person, in the later part of the day, becomes in a state such that had they been in that state at the beginning, fasting would be obligatory, then they must abstain for the rest of the day. For example, a menstruating woman who becomes pure, an insane person who recovers, a sick person who recovers, a traveler who becomes resident. If not, they are not required to abstain. Muhammad ibn Shuja' said this abstaining is mustahab (recommended), not wajib.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the Hidayah commentary. It discusses the situation when a child reaches puberty or a disbeliever accepts Islam during the day in Ramadan. The ruling is that such a person must abstain (imsaak) from eating, drinking, etc. for the remainder of the day as a form of honoring the sacred time (haqq al-waqt). However, they are not required to make up (qada) that day if they break it, because the obligation to fast that entire day was not present when they were ineligible. They still must fast the remaining days of Ramadan because eligibility now exists. The reason given is that the cause (sabab) for fasting is the first part of the day, and eligibility was absent at that time; this is contrasted with prayer, where the cause is the entire time connected to performance, so a convert or newly-eligible person must pray the remainder of the time and also make up missed parts? Actually, the text says for prayer, the cause is the part connected to performance, so eligibility is found at that time, i.e., if one becomes Muslim during prayer time, he must pray that prayer as soon as he can? The passage then presents the view of Imam Abu Yusuf: if the change (conversion or puberty) occurs before zawal (noon), then qada is wajib because they have reached the time of intention (niyyah) for that day's fast. But the Zahir al-Riwayah position (of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) holds that fasting is not divisible into parts; the obligation is for the entire day, and since the first part was without eligibility, the whole day's fast is not wajib, and thus no qada. The passage also notes a secondary ruling: a child in this situation may intend a voluntary (nafl) fast, but a disbeliever may not, because a child (mumayyiz) is eligible for nafl acts, while a disbeliever is not. The tashreeh then explains the general principle (zabita) that if a person, in the later part of the day, attains a state that would have made fasting obligatory on them from the beginning, they must abstain. Examples include a woman ending her menses, an insane person recovering, a traveler settling, etc. If they do not attain such a state, no abstaining required. Finally, there is a mention that some scholars (Muhammad ibn Shuja') consider this imsaak to be mustahab (recommended), not wajib.

Key Terms
امساک (imsak): Abstaining from food, drink, and other nullifiers of fast for the remainder of the day, even though the fast is not obligatory.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The authentic and relied-upon transmission of the Hanafi school from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نفل کی نیت (niyyat al-nafl): Intention to perform a voluntary (supererogatory) fast; a child who becomes adult during the day may intend nafl for that day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A boy reaches puberty at 11 AM during Ramadan. According to the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling?
A) He must fast the rest of the day and make up that day later.
B) He must fast the rest of the day but does not need to make it up.
C) He is not required to abstain at all, as the day started when he was not obliged.
D) He must make up that day regardless of abstaining.

Key Takeaway
When a person becomes eligible to fast during a Ramadan day, they must abstain for the remainder but do not need to make up that day, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on One Who Becomes Obligated During a Ramadan Day
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for mid-day obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on imsak and qada for one who becomes obligated mid-day, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the majority.

Core Idea
Fasting is indivisible in obligation; if the cause finds no capacity at dawn, no fast is wajib even if capacity arises later.

This passage from the sharh of al-Hidayah addresses a critical scenario: a child who reaches puberty or a disbeliever who embraces Islam during a Ramadan day. The ruling has significant practical implications and involves a subtle principle about the cause (sabab) of fasting and the indivisibility of its obligation. We will unpack the majority view and the alternate opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with two cases: a child becoming baligh and a disbeliever converting to Islam at any point during a Ramadan day. The initial ruling is that they must refrain (imsak) for the remainder of the day.
Imsak here means abstaining from eating, drinking, and intercourse.
2
Understand the sabab (cause) of fasting obligation
The Hanafi school holds that the cause for the obligation of a particular day's fast is the first part of the day (al-juz' al-awwal), from dawn. At that moment, the person lacked capacity (ahliyyah) due to childhood or disbelief.
This contrasts with prayer, where the cause is the part of time connected to performance.
3
Apply the principle of indivisibility (la yatajazzā wujūban)
Fasting cannot be obligatory in part of the day and not in another. Since the first part lacked capacity, the entire day's fast is not wajib. Hence, no qada is required if imsak is broken.
This is the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's contrary view
Abu Yusuf holds that if the impediment (kufr or childhood) ends before zawal (midday), qada becomes obligatory because the person has reached the time for intention (waqt al-niyyah).
His reasoning is that a valid intention for fasting can be made before zawal, so the rest of the day becomes wajib.
5
Contrast the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the majority, no qada is required regardless of the time of removal. According to Abu Yusuf, qada is obligatory if removal occurs before zawal.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the majority view from zahir al-riwayah.

اول حصہ میں عدم بلوغ اور کفر کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں اہلیت صوم معدوم ہے پس
Translation: And when a boy reaches puberty or a disbeliever embraces Islam during Ramadan, they must refrain for the remainder of their day as an observance of the right of the time through emulation. And if they break fast therein, no qada is upon them because fasting is not obligatory therein. And they fast what is after it due to the realization of the cause and capacity. And they do not make up that day nor what has passed because of absence of address. And this is contrary to prayer because the cause in it is the part connected to performance, so capacity is found at that time, while in fasting the cause is the first part and capacity is absent at that time. And from Abu Yusuf: when disbelief or childhood ceases before zawal, then qada is upon him because he reached the time of intention. The face of the apparent narration is that fasting is not divisible in obligation and the capacity for obligation is absent at the beginning of the day. However, the boy may intend supererogatory fasting in this case, unlike the disbeliever, as they said, because the disbeliever is not of the people of supererogatory worship either, while the boy is eligible for it.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Hidayah discusses the ruling for a child who reaches puberty or a disbeliever who embraces Islam during a Ramadan day. The core principle (ضابطہ) stated is that if a person attains the condition that would make fasting obligatory at the beginning of the day, they must refrain (امساک) from eating, drinking, and intercourse for the remainder of the day out of respect for the sacred time and to emulate the fasting community. However, if they do break the fast, no qada (make-up) is required for that day because the obligation of fasting had not been established upon them at the start of the day. The cause (سبب) for the obligation of fasting in Ramadan is the first part of the day (الجزء الأول), and at that moment, the capacity (اہلیت) for obligation was absent due to childhood or disbelief. This distinguishes fasting from prayer, where the cause is the part of time connected to the performance (الجزء المتصل بالأداء), so if one becomes obligated at the last moment of the prayer time, qada is required. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the condition (kufr or childhood) ends before zawal (midday), then qada is obligatory because the person reached the time of intention (وقت النية), since the intention for fasting can be made before zawal. The apparent narration (ظاہر الروایہ) maintained by Imam Muhammad and the majority of the Hanafi school is that fasting is indivisible in obligation (لا يتجزى وجوبًا); it cannot be partially obligatory. Since the capacity for obligation was absent at the first part of the day, the entire day's fasting is not wajib, hence no qada. The commentary also notes a related point: a child who has reached the age of discernment (صبی) may intend supererogatory fasting for the day after becoming baligh before zawal, whereas a disbeliever cannot, as disbelief prevents even supererogatory worship.

Key Terms
امساک (imsāk): Refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse; here it means abstaining from these for the remainder of the day out of respect for Ramadan, not as an obligatory fast.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation of fasting; in this context, the first part of the day (al-juz' al-awwal) from dawn is the cause for wajub al-sawm.
اهلیت (ahliyyah): Legal capacity: here, the capacity to be obligated (ahliyyat al-wujub) for fasting. A child and disbeliever lack this capacity at the time of the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah), what is the ruling for a disbeliever who embraces Islam during a Ramadan day after dawn but before zawal (midday)?
A) He must fast the remainder of the day and make up that day later if he breaks it.
B) He must refrain from eating, drinking, and intercourse for the remainder of the day but does not have to make it up if he breaks it.
C) He is not required to do anything; he may eat and drink openly.
D) He must fast the entire day from the moment of his conversion and make it up if broken.

Key Takeaway
The cause for the obligation of fasting is the first part of the day; if capacity is absent at that time, the fast is not wajib, and only imsak is required without qada.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Qada for One Who Becomes Obligated During a Ramadan Day
Explains rule for child baligh/convert during Ramadan day and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a child reaching puberty or a convert during a Ramadan day, distinguish the Zahir al-Riwaya position from that of Imam Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle that fasting is not divisible in obligation.

Core Idea
Fasting cannot be split: if the dawn lacked eligibility, the whole day's fast is not wajib, so no qada after conversion or puberty during the day.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a child who reaches puberty or a non-Muslim who accepts Islam during a Ramadan day must make up that day's fast if they break imsaak. The passage from Al-Hidayah, via the commentary Ashraf al-Bidayah, presents the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwaya view and contrasts it with the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi principle that the obligation of fasting is not divisible (ghayr mutajazzi) across the day.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position on Imsaak and Qada
First, identify the ruling that imsaak (refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse) for the remainder of the day is wajib, but the fast of that day itself is not wajib, so no qada is required if imsaak is broken.
This is the Zahir al-Riwaya position.
2
Identify the Opposing View of Imam Abu Yusuf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the incapacity (childhood or disbelief) is removed before zawal (noon), the person can intend the fast, and if broken, qada becomes wajib. Note that he sees disbelief as a legal impediment, not an essential one.
This differs from the relied-upon view.
3
Follow the Proof for Each View
For Zahir al-Riwaya: the obligation of fasting cannot be divided (mutajazzi); since eligibility was absent at dawn, the fast never became wajib. For Abu Yusuf: the analogy with a person who intended to break fast but re-intended before zawal shows that intention can be made after dawn; similarly, conversion before zawal allows intention.
The hadith 'فَلْيَصُمْ بَقِيَّةَ يَوْمِہ' supports the obligation of imsaak, not the full fast.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to Abu Yusuf
The Zahir al-Riwaya responds that the analogy fails because in that case, the person was eligible from dawn; here, eligibility was absent at dawn. The principle of non-divisibility prevents the fast from becoming wajib in the second half of the day.
This argument hinges on the nature of the fast's obligation.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the Zahir al-Riwaya view. It is the relied-upon position for fatwa because it is rooted in the foundational sources (Zahir al-Riwaya) and the principle of non-divisibility is strong.
The mufta bihi: no qada required for that day's fast.

The book of Fasting. Page 246. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 3. It will become wajib. And Shaykh Imam Zahid al-Sighar said that imsaak (refraining) is wajib because Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut in the book of Siyam: 'فَلْيَصُمْ بَقِيَّةَ يَوْمِہ' (so let him fast the remainder of his day) and 'فليصم' is a command and the imperative form indicates obligation. And regarding a menstruating woman, he said: 'إِذَا طَهُرَتْ فِی بَعْضِ النَّهَارِ فَلْتَدَعِ الأكُلَ وَالشِّرْبَ' (when she becomes pure during part of the day, then let her refrain from eating and drinking) and 'لتدع' is an imperative form which indicates obligation. Under this rule is the issue: In a Ramadan day, if a minor child reaches puberty or a non-Muslim becomes Muslim, then both these individuals should refrain from eating, drinking, and intercourse for the remainder of the day, so that by adopting similarity with those fasting, the sanctity of Ramadan time is fulfilled. Because it is an evil thing that the whole world is fasting and these are eating and drinking. Therefore, they should refrain from nullifiers. But despite this, if the minor after attaining puberty or the disbeliever after becoming Muslim eats or drinks something in that Ramadan day, then the qada (make-up) of that day is not wajib upon them, because the fast of that day was never wajib upon them. Rather, the imsaak (refraining) for the remainder of the day is wajib, and qada is wajib for the fast, not for imsaak. So qada of that day is not wajib. Yes, for the remaining days of Ramadan after that day, the fast is fard upon them because they now have capacity and eligibility for fasting, being sane, adult, Muslim, and free from legal impediments, and the cause of fast (Ramadan) is present. So when eligibility and cause are both present, what objection is there to the fast being fard? However, the passing days and the day of reaching puberty or embracing Islam have no qada because at that time these individuals were not addressed by Shari'ah. And when they were not addressed and obligated, then ada was not wajib upon them, and when ada was not wajib, how can qada become wajib? In contrast is prayer: if at the very end of the prayer time a child reaches puberty or a non-Muslim becomes Muslim, then qada of that prayer becomes wajib upon them. Because the cause for prayer to become wajib is that part of the time which is connected to the performance. But if the time became narrow and they did not perform the prayer, then that narrow time itself is the cause. So when in that narrow time the non-Muslim becomes Muslim or the child reaches puberty, the eligibility for prayer is found. Now when eligibility for prayer exists and the cause for wajib prayer is also found, then this prayer becomes obligatory upon them. But since the time for performance has not remained, qada becomes wajib. As for fasting, the cause for its wajib is the first part of the day, which is the part immediately connected to the break of dawn. In that strength, i.e., in the first part of the day, eligibility is absent due to disbelief or non-puberty. And when eligibility is absent, the fast of that day is not obligatory. And when the fast is not obligatory, its qada is not wajib. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if disbelief or childhood is removed before zawal (noon), i.e., the disbeliever becomes Muslim before zawal or the child reaches puberty, then qada of that day's fast becomes wajib upon them because he has reached the time of intention (niyyah) for fasting, because if one makes intention for fasting before zawal, the fast becomes valid. An example is: if someone intended to break fast in the morning but did not eat or drink, then before zawal he made intention for fasting, his fast would be valid even though breaking the fast (afṭār) is contrary to fasting. Similarly, disbelief is contrary to fasting legally (ḥukman), not essentially (ḥaqīqatan). Therefore, if he becomes Muslim before zawal and makes intention for fasting, his fast is valid provided he did not eat or drink from morning. The reason of Zahir al-Riwaya is that fasting is not divisible (mutajazzi) in obligation, i.e., it cannot be that the fast is non-obligatory in the first half of the day and obligatory in the second half. And it is established that in the first part of the day, due to lack of puberty or disbelief, eligibility for fasting is absent. Now since in the first part of the day, due to lack of eligibility for obligation, the fast was not wajib upon them. And in the remainder of the day it will not become wajib because fasting is not divisible in obligation. The result is that the fast of that day is not wajib upon them, and when the wajib of that day's fast is not established, qada is also not wajib. However, this much is necessary: if a child reaches puberty before zawal and intends nafl fast, then the nafl fast will be valid provided he did not eat or drink from morning. And if a non-Muslim becomes Muslim before zawal and intends nafl fast, then his nafl fast is not valid because a non-Muslim is not eligible for nafl fast. But a minor child is eligible for nafl fast.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqh ruling (with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute) regarding a child who reaches puberty or a non-Muslim who converts to Islam during a Ramadan day. The author first establishes that refraining (imsaak) from eating, drinking, and intercourse for the remainder of the day is wajib, based on the command in the hadith 'فَلْيَصُمْ' (so let him fast) and 'فَلْتَدَعِ' (so let her refrain). The purpose is to maintain the sanctity of Ramadan by not openly violating the fast while others are fasting. However, if such a person does break the fast after becoming obligated to refrain, he does not owe a make-up (qada) for that day, because the fast itself was never obligatory on him. The obligation to refrain is separate from the obligation to fast. The author then contrasts this with the case of prayer, where if a child becomes adult or a convert becomes Muslim at the very end of a prayer time, qada becomes obligatory because the cause of prayer is the last part of its time, which connects to the performance. For fasting, the cause is the first part of the day (dawn), and at that time the person lacked eligibility. Therefore, the fast is not obligated and thus no qada. An exception is reported from Imam Abu Yusuf: if the incapacity (childhood or disbelief) is removed before zawal (noon), and the person intends a fast, then the fast becomes valid and if broken, qada becomes wajib. This is because the intention can be made before zawal, and the prohibition of fasting (due to disbelief) is only legal, not essential. The Zahir al-Riwaya position (the relied-upon view) opposes this, stating that the day's obligation cannot be split: the first part lacked eligibility, so the whole day's fast cannot become wajib. Consequently, qada is not required. However, if a child reaches puberty before zawal and intends a nafl fast, it is valid because a child is eligible for nafl. But a non-Muslim's nafl fast is not valid even if he converts before zawal, because he was not eligible for any worship before Islam.

Key Terms
امساک (imsaak): Refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse for the remainder of the day out of respect for Ramadan, even though the fast is not obligatory.
قضاء (qada): The make-up of an obligatory act after its prescribed time has passed. Here, qada of a fast is required only if the fast itself was obligatory.
متجری (mutajazzi): Not divisible; the obligation of fast cannot be split into parts across the day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwaya, if a non-Muslim converts to Islam at 2 PM (after zawal) during Ramadan, what is the ruling regarding qada of that day's fast?
A) He must make up that day's fast.
B) He must only refrain for the rest of the day, but no qada.
C) He must both fast the rest of the day and make it up later.
D) He need not do anything.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of fasting for a given day cannot be partially applied: if eligibility for obligation is absent at dawn, the entire day's fast is never wajib, so no qada is required even if the person later becomes eligible and breaks the imsaak.
