Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Traveler's Fast Valid After Return Before Zawal
Ruling on a traveler who returns before zawal and intends to fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a fast for a traveler who returns home before zawal and makes a new intention, and explain the reasoning based on eligibility, concession removal, and the a fortiori argument.

Core Idea
A traveler's valid intention before zawal makes his fast valid and, in Ramadan, obligatory; doubt from the concession prevents kaffara.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a traveler who had intended at night not to fast, but returns to his hometown before noon (zawal) and makes a fresh intention to fast. The Hanafi school holds that this fast is valid, regardless of whether it is a voluntary fast or an obligatory Ramadan fast. The reasoning involves a key legal maxim about travel not negating eligibility, and an a fortiori qiyas argument. We will also explore why no kaffara is due if he breaks the fast in this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling
Read the passage carefully. The scenario: a traveler intends at night to break his fast (i.e., not fast), then returns to his hometown before zawal, makes a new intention to fast, and has not eaten or drunk. The ruling: the fast is valid and, if in Ramadan, becomes wajib.
This covers both voluntary and obligatory fasts.
2
Understand the Legal Maxim
The passage states: 'travel does not oppose the eligibility for obligation nor the validity of commencement.' This means a traveler retains the capacity to fast and can validly start a fast. The concession (rukhsa) does not remove the essential qualification.
This is the basis for the validity of the intention.
3
Apply Removal of Concession in Ramadan
In Ramadan, once the traveler becomes resident before zawal, the concession for breaking the fast is removed at the time of intention. Therefore, fasting becomes obligatory. The passage compares to the case of a resident who travels later: the initial residence outweighs the travel.
This is a qiyas awwali (a fortiori) argument.
4
Analyze the Qiyas Awwali Argument
The author uses an a fortiori reasoning: if a person who starts the day as resident and then travels is not allowed to break his fast (because residence at dawn prevails), then even more so a traveler who becomes resident before zawal should not be allowed to break, because the concession is entirely absent at the time of breaking.
This strengthens the ruling.
5
Note the Shubha Effect on Kaffara
If the traveler breaks the fast in either scenario, no kaffara is due because there exists a doubt (shubha) arising from the existence of a concession to break. Kaffara is only applied when the prohibition is certain.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that penalties are suspended in cases of doubt.

مسافر نے افطار کی نیت کی پھر زوال سے پہلے شہر آ گیا پھر روزہ کی نیت کر لی یہ روزہ ہو جائے گا۔ وَإِذَا نَوَى الْمُسَافِرُ الْإِفْطَارَ ثُمَّ قَدِمَ الْمِصْرَ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ فَنَوَى الصَّوْمَ أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّ السَّفَرَ لَا يُنَا فِي أُهْلِيَّةَ الْوُجُوبِ وَلَا صِحَّةَ الشَّرُوعِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي رَمَضَانِ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَصُومَ لِزَوَالِ الْمُرَخَّصِ فِي وَقْتِ النِّيَةِ الْاتَرَى أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ مُقِيِّمًا فِى أَوَّلِ الْيَوْمِ ثُمَّ سَافَرَ لَا يُبَاحُ لَهُ الْفِطْرُ تَرْجِيْحًا لِجَانِبِ الْإِقَامَةِ فَهُذَا أَوْلَى إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا أَفْطَرَ فِى الْمَسْأَلَتَيْنِ لا تلومه الكَفَّارَة لقيام شُبهة الميح تَلُومُهُ
ترجمہ اور جب مسافر نے افطار کی نیت کی پھر وہ زوال سے پہلے شہر میں آگیا پھر روزے کی نیت کی ، تو اس کو یہ روزہ کافی ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ سفر نہ تو اہلیت وجوب کے منافی ہے اور نہ صحت شروع کے۔ اور اگر یہ واقعہ رمضان میں ہوا تو اس پر روزہ رکھنا واجب ہے کیونکہ نیت کے وقت میں مرخص زائل ہو گیا ہے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر کوئی دن کے اول میں مقیم ہو پھر اس نے سفر کیا تو اس کے لئے جانب اقامت کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے افطار کرنا مباح نہیں ہے تو یہ صورت اولی ہے مگر یہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے دونوں صورتوں میں افطار کر دیا تو اس پر کفاره ۱۱ زم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ میچ کا شبہ موجود ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غیر رمضان میں مسافر نے رات میں یہ نیت کی کہ کل روزہ نہیں رکھوں گا۔ پھر اس نے زوال سے پہلے اپنے وطن میں پہنچ کر نفلی روزہ کی نیت کر لی حال یہ کہ ابھی تک اس نے کچھ کھایا پیا بھی نہیں ہے تو اس کا یہ نفلی روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا کیونکہ سفر نہ تو ثبوت کی اہلیت کی منافی ہے اور نہ صحت شروع کے منافی ہے یعنی مسافر کے لئے روزہ رکھنے کی اہلیت بھی ثابت ہے اور اس سے روز ہ شروع کرنا بھی صحیح ہوتا ہے حتی کہ اگر مسافرنفلی روزہ کو فاسد کر دے تو قضا واجب ہوتی ہے اور اگر مسافر کا رات میں افطار کی نیت کرنا اور زوال سے پہلے اپنے وطن پہنچ جانا رمضان میں پیش آیا تو اس پر اس دن کا روزہ رکھنا لازم ہے کیونکہ نیت کے وقت میں یعنی زوال سے پہلے مرخص یعنی سفر جو افطار کی رخصت دیتا تھا وہ زائل ہو گیا پس جب نیت کے وقت میں مرخص زائل ہو گیا تو روزہ رکھنا لازم ہو گیا۔ چنانچہ آپ ملا خط فرما ئیں کہ اگر کوئی شخص دن کے اول حصہ میں مقیم ہو پھر اس نے سفر شروع کیا تو سفر کی وجہ سے افطار مباح نہیں ہے کیونکہ دن کے اول حصہ میں مقیم ہونے کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ افطار مباح نہ ہو اور دن کے آخر حصہ میں مسافر ہونے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ افطار مباح ہو پس مقیم ہونے کی جانب کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے افطار کو غیر مباح قرار دیا گیا۔ پس جب اس صورت میں افطار غیر مباح ہے تو پہلی صورت میں ( یعنی جب مسافر زوال سے پہلے مقیم ہو گیا ) بدرجہ اولی افطار غیر مباح ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ مسئلہ ثانیہ میں باوجود یکہ افطار کے وقت مرخص یعنی سفر موجود ہے پھر بھی افطار مباح نہیں تو جس صورت میں افطار کے وقت مرخص یعنی سفر بھی موجود نہیں تو بدرجہ اولی افطار کرنا غیر مباح ہوگا۔
A traveler intended to break the fast, then came to the city before zawal (noon) and then intended the fast; this fast will be valid. And when the traveler intends al-iftaar (breaking fast) then arrives at the town before zawal and then intends the fast, it suffices him. Because travel does not oppose the eligibility for obligation nor the validity of commencement (of the fast). And if this is in Ramadan, then upon him is to fast because the concession (rukhsa) is removed at the time of intention. Do you not see that if one was resident at the beginning of the day and then traveled, breaking fast is not permissible for him, giving preference to the side of residence; so this (case) is even more apt. However, if he breaks the fast in both cases, no kaffara (expiation) is due upon him because there exists a doubt (shubha) due to the concession.

Translation: And when a traveler intended to break the fast, then he came to the city before zawal, then intended to fast, then this fast will be sufficient for him. Because travel neither contradicts eligibility for obligation nor validity of commencement. And if this happened in Ramadan, then upon him is to fast because the concession (murakhkhas) was removed at the time of intention. Do you not see that if someone was resident at the beginning of the day, then he traveled, it is not permissible for him to break the fast, giving preference to the side of residence; so this case is even more apt. But if he broke the fast in both cases, no kaffara is due upon him because the doubt of permissibility exists.

Explanation: The case is that if in non-Ramadan, a traveler intended at night that he will not fast tomorrow, then before zawal he reached his hometown and intended a nafl fast, while he had not eaten or drunk anything, then this nafl fast of his will be valid because travel neither opposes the eligibility for obligation nor the validity of commencement. That is, the eligibility for fasting is established for a traveler and commencing the fast is also valid from him, even to the extent that if a traveler invalidates a nafl fast, qada becomes wajib upon him. And if the traveler's intending to break fast at night and arriving at his hometown before zawal occurred in Ramadan, then upon him it is necessary to fast that day because at the time of intention, i.e., before zawal, the concession (i.e., travel) which gave permission to break fast was removed. So when the concession was removed at the time of intention, fasting became necessary. Accordingly, please note: if a person was resident at the first part of the day, then he started traveling, due to travel it is not permissible to break the fast because the requirement of being resident in the first part of the day is that breaking fast is not permissible, and the requirement of being a traveler in the later part of the day is that breaking fast is permissible. So, giving preference to the side of residence, breaking fast was declared not permissible. So when breaking fast is not permissible in that case, then in the first case (i.e., when a traveler becomes resident before zawal), it is even more apt that breaking fast is not permissible. Because in the second case, despite the existence of the concession (travel) at the time of breaking, still breaking fast is not permissible; then in the case where the concession (travel) is not even present at the time of breaking, it is even more apt that breaking fast is not permissible.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a traveler who had initially intended not to fast (either for a voluntary fast outside Ramadan or for a Ramadan fast) but returns to his town before zawal (noon). The core ruling: if such a traveler makes a new intention to fast before zawal and has not eaten or drunk anything since dawn, his fast is valid. This holds for both voluntary (nafl) and obligatory (Ramadan) fasts. The reasoning: travel (safar) does not negate the eligibility for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub) nor the validity of starting a fast (sihhat al-shuru'). Travel merely permits breaking the fast, but does not prevent a valid intention. However, if it is Ramadan and he becomes resident before zawal, the concession (rukhsa) no longer exists at the time of intention, so fasting becomes obligatory. The passage uses an a fortiori argument (qiyas awwali): if a person who was resident at the beginning of the day then travels later is not allowed to break his fast (because the stronger aspect—residence at dawn—prevails), then even more so, a traveler who becomes resident before zawal should not break his fast, because the concession is completely absent. Yet, if he does break the fast in any of these cases, no expiation (kaffara) is due because there is a doubt (shubha) arising from the fact that travel provides a concession to break the fast. This doubt prevents the application of kaffara, which is a severe penalty only applied when the impermissibility is absolutely clear.

Key Terms
مرخص (murakhkhas): The concession (rukhsa) granted to a traveler to break the fast due to hardship.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of severe penalties like kaffara. Here, the existence of a license (rukhsa) creates a doubt about the prohibition of breaking the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a traveler intended at night to break his fast (i.e., not fast), but then returns to his hometown before zawal and makes a new intention to fast for Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is not valid because he already intended to break.
B) The fast is valid and becomes wajib; if he breaks it, no kaffara is due.
C) The fast is valid but only as a nafl fast.
D) He must fast the rest of the day but qada is required.

Key Takeaway
A traveler who returns home before zawal and makes a fresh intention to fast has a valid fast, and in Ramadan it is wajib; the doubt from the license precludes kaffara if broken.
